**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-001
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2021
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the first quarter of the seventeenth century, in which of the following was/were the factory/factories of the English East India Company located?
1. Broach
2. Chicacole
3. Trichinopoly
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** By the first quarter of the 17th century (up to 1625), the English East India Company had established factories at Surat, Broach, Ahmedabad, Agra, and Masulipatnam. Chicacole (Srikakulam) and Trichinopoly (Tiruchirappalli) were established as prominent centres much later.
**Keywords:** English East India Company, Factories, 17th Century.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** William Hawkins, Jahangir.
**Memory Trick:** "S-A-B-A-M" (Surat, Ahmedabad, Broach, Agra, Masulipatnam) for early English bases.
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing 17th-century factory locations with late 18th-century administrative headquarters.
**Why Important:** Tests micro-level factual knowledge of early European commercial penetration.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-002
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2022
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian history, consider the following statements:
1. The Dutch established their factories/warehouses on the east coast on lands granted to them by Gajapati rulers.
2. Alfonso de Albuquerque captured Goa from the Bijapur Sultanate.
3. The English East India Company established a factory at Madras on a plot of land leased from a representative of the Vijayanagara empire.
Which of the statements given above are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect because the Gajapati dynasty declined by the mid-16th century, long before the Dutch arrived in the 17th century. Statement 2 is correct as Albuquerque captured Goa from the Sultan of Bijapur in 1510. Statement 3 is correct because Francis Day obtained the lease of Madras in 1639 from the representative of the Aravidu dynasty of Vijayanagara.
**Keywords:** Dutch, Albuquerque, Goa, Madras.
**Related Dates:** 1510 (Goa), 1639 (Madras).
**Memory Trick:** "Gajapati gone before Dutch arrived".
**Common Exam Trap:** Historical anachronism regarding the timeline of the Gajapati rulers and European arrivals.
**Why Important:** This question reflects the trend of testing specific land grants and local political contexts of European settlements.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-003
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2017
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the context of Indian history, the principle of ‘Dyarchy (diarchy)’ refers to:
**Options:**
(a) Division of the central legislature into two houses.
(b) Introduction of double government i.e., Central and State governments.
(c) Having two sets of rulers; one in London and another in Delhi.
(d) Division of the subjects delegated to the provinces into two categories.
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Dyarchy, introduced by the Government of India Act 1919, divided provincial subjects into two parts: 'Transferred' (administered by the Governor with ministers) and 'Reserved' (administered by the Governor and his executive council).
**Keywords:** Dyarchy, Provincial Subjects, Transferred, Reserved.
**Related Acts:** Government of India Act 1919.
**Memory Trick:** Dyarchy = "Dual Rule" in Provinces.
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing Dyarchy with Bicameralism (two houses) or Federalism (division between centre and states).
**Why Important:** Foundational concept for understanding constitutional evolution and the 1919 reforms.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-004
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the Federation established by The Government of India Act of 1935, residuary powers were given to the:
**Options:**
(a) Federal Legislature
(b) Governor General
(c) Provincial Legislature
(d) Provincial Governors
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The 1935 Act proposed an All-India Federation and divided subjects into Federal, Provincial, and Concurrent lists. Residuary legislative powers were neither assigned to the federal nor provincial legislatures but were vested in the discretion of the Governor-General.
**Keywords:** GOI Act 1935, Residuary Powers, Governor General.
**Related Acts:** Government of India Act 1935.
**Memory Trick:** "Residue goes to the Boss" (Governor-General).
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking residuary powers went to the Federal Legislature as they do in the modern Indian Constitution (to the Parliament).
**Why Important:** Highlights the centralising authority of the British Crown even under a "federal" scheme.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-005
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2021
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. The Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms of 1919 recommended granting voting rights to all the women above the age of 21.
2. The Government of India Act of 1935 gave women reserved seats in legislature.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect because the 1919 Act allowed for a limited franchise based on property, tax, and education, but did not grant universal suffrage to women; it only allowed provincial councils to decide on female enfranchisement. Statement 2 is correct as the 1935 Act extended the principle of communal representation and provided separate electorates/reserved seats for women, depressed classes, and labourers.
**Keywords:** Montagu-Chelmsford, GOI Act 1935, Women's Suffrage, Reserved Seats.
**Related Personalities:** Edwin Montagu, Lord Chelmsford.
**Memory Trick:** 1935 extended "Separate Electorates" to everyone left out, including women.
**Common Exam Trap:** Assuming that if a right was granted (voting), it was "universal".
**Why Important:** Tests detailed knowledge of the expansion of representative institutions in India.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-006
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies (Education)
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following led to the introduction of English Education in India?
1. Charter Act of 1813
2. General Committee of Public Instruction, 1823
3. Orientalist and Anglicist Controversy
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Charter Act of 1813 first sanctioned one lakh rupees for the promotion of knowledge of modern sciences. The General Committee of Public Instruction (1823) was formed to manage this grant. The debate within this committee between Orientalists (traditional learning) and Anglicists (Western learning) eventually led to Macaulay’s Minute and the formal introduction of English education.
**Keywords:** English Education, Charter Act 1813, Anglicists, Orientalists.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Macaulay.
**Memory Trick:** "1813 Money -> 1823 Committee -> Controversy -> English".
**Common Exam Trap:** Excluding the Charter Act of 1813 because it didn't explicitly say "English only" initially.
**Why Important:** Education policy was a major tool for creating a class of Indians "English in taste" to support administration.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-007
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Swadeshi Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2023
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
Statement-I: 7th August is declared as the National Handloom Day.
Statement-II: It was in 1905 that the Swadeshi Movement was launched on the same day.
Which one of the following is correct in respect of the above statements?
**Options:**
(a) Both Statement-I and Statement-II are correct and Statement-II is the correct explanation for Statement-I
(b) Both Statement-I and Statement-II are correct and Statement-II is not the correct explanation for Statement-I
(c) Statement-I is correct but Statement-II is incorrect
(d) Statement-I is incorrect but Statement-II is correct
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** National Handloom Day is observed on August 7 to commemorate the formal proclamation of the Swadeshi Movement on August 7, 1905, at the Calcutta Town Hall. The movement promoted indigenous goods (handlooms) and boycotted foreign goods.
**Keywords:** National Handloom Day, Swadeshi Movement, August 7.
**Related Dates:** 7th August 1905.
**Memory Trick:** "Handloom = Swadeshi = Aug 7".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the date refers to the Partition of Bengal itself (which was announced in July and enforced in October 1905).
**Why Important:** Shows UPSC's linkage of current government commemorative days with historical events.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-008
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following is a very significant aspect of the Champaran Satyagraha?
**Options:**
(a) Active all-India participation of lawyers, students and women in the National Movement
(b) Active involvement of Dalit and Tribal communities of India in the National Movement
(c) Joining of peasant unrest to India's National Movement
(d) Drastic decrease in the cultivation of plantation crops and commercial crops
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Champaran (1917) was Gandhi's first Satyagraha in India, where he addressed the grievances of indigo peasants against the Tinkathia system. Its primary significance was that it successfully integrated peasant grievances into the mainstream nationalist struggle led by the INC.
**Keywords:** Champaran Satyagraha, Peasant Unrest, National Movement.
**Related Personalities:** Rajendra Prasad, Brajkishore Prasad.
**Memory Trick:** "Champaran = Peasant Entry into Politics".
**Common Exam Trap:** Options (a) and (b) describe later mass movements like Non-Cooperation or Civil Disobedience.
**Why Important:** It marked the transition of the freedom struggle into a mass movement involving the rural poor.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-009
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Gandhi-Irwin Pact included which of the following?
1. Invitation to Congress to participate in the Round Table Conference.
2. Withdrawal of Ordinances promulgated in connection with the Civil Disobedience Movement.
3. Acceptance of Gandhiji’s suggestion for enquiry into police excesses.
4. Release of only those prisoners who were not charged with violence.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2 and 4 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The 1931 pact placed Congress on equal footing with the government. It included an invitation to the 2nd RTC, withdrawal of CD-related ordinances, and release of non-violent political prisoners. However, the government refused a public inquiry into police excesses.
**Keywords:** Gandhi-Irwin Pact, Round Table Conference, Political Prisoners.
**Related Dates:** 5 March 1931.
**Memory Trick:** "No inquiry into police, but Yes to prisoners without blood on hands".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking that Bhagat Singh's release or an inquiry into police brutality was accepted.
**Why Important:** This pact led to the suspension of the Civil Disobedience Movement and Congress participation in the 2nd RTC.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-010
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Peasant Movement and Tribal Rebellions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the history of India, "Ulgulan" or the Great Tumult is the description of which of the following events?
**Options:**
(a) The Revolt of 1867
(b) The Mappila Rebellion of 1921
(c) The Indigo Revolt of 1859-60
(d) Birsa Munda's Revolt of 1899-1900
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** "Ulgulan" (The Great Tumult) refers to the rebellion led by Birsa Munda in the region south of Ranchi in 1899-1900. It aimed at establishing a Munda Raj and resisting the intrusion of "Dikus" (outsiders/moneylenders) and British agrarian policies.
**Keywords:** Ulgulan, Birsa Munda, Great Tumult, Ranchi.
**Related Personalities:** Birsa Munda.
**Memory Trick:** "Birsa's Big Noise = Ulgulan".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Santhal Rebellion (1855) or earlier tribal uprisings.
**Why Important:** It is a classic example of tribal resistance against colonial land alienation.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-011
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the context of Indian history, the Rakhmabai case of 1884 revolved around:
1. Women's right to gain education
2. Age of consent
3. Restitution of conjugal rights
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Rakhmabai Bhikaji was a pioneer who contested a suit filed by her husband for "restitution of conjugal rights". The case triggered a national debate that led to the Age of Consent Act 1891, raising the marriage age. While she was highly educated (becoming India’s first practising lady doctor), the 1884 case itself was specifically about consent and marital rights, not her "right to gain education".
**Keywords:** Rakhmabai, Age of Consent, Conjugal Rights.
**Related Acts:** Age of Consent Act 1891.
**Memory Trick:** "Case of Consent and Conjugality".
**Common Exam Trap:** Including "education" simply because she was a doctor; the legal case was about her marriage.
**Why Important:** Highlights the intersection of colonial law, traditional customs, and women's agency.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-012
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Working Class Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2017
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. The Factories Act, 1881 was passed with a view to fix the wages of industrial workers and to allow the workers to form trade unions.
2. N.M. Lokhande was a pioneer in organizing the labour movement in British India.
Which of the above statements is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect because the 1881 Act dealt primarily with child labour and hours, not wages or trade unions. Statement 2 is correct; N.M. Lokhande was a lieutenant of Jyotiba Phule and founded the Bombay Millhands Association (1890), making him a pioneer of the Indian labour movement.
**Keywords:** Factories Act 1881, N.M. Lokhande, Labour Movement.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Ripon (passed the Act).
**Memory Trick:** "1881 = Small Kids; 1891 = Women; Lokhande = Labour Leader".
**Common Exam Trap:** Assuming early labour laws were comprehensive (they were mostly to satisfy British manufacturers' concerns about cheap Indian competition).
**Why Important:** Reflects the beginning of organised labour in India.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-013
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Personality Based Questions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2019
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian National Movement, consider the following pairs:
Person — Position held
1. Sir Tej Bahadur Sapru — President, All India Liberal Federation
2. K.C. Neogy — Member, The Constituent Assembly
3. P.C. Joshi — General Secretary, Communist Party of India
Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** All three are correctly matched. Sapru was a key leader of the Liberal Federation after splitting from Congress in 1919. Neogy was a member of the Constituent Assembly and later the first Finance Commission chairman. P.C. Joshi was the first General Secretary of the CPI (1935–47).
**Keywords:** Sapru, Neogy, P.C. Joshi, Liberal Federation, CPI.
**Related Dates:** 1919 (Liberal Federation), 1935 (CPI leadership).
**Memory Trick:** "Sapru is Liberal, Joshi is Communist, Neogy is Assembly".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking K.C. Neogy was only an economist and not part of the political assembly.
**Why Important:** Tests knowledge of leaders outside the mainstream INC hierarchy.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-014
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Chronology
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which among the following events happened earliest?
**Options:**
(a) Swami Dayanand established Arya Samaj.
(b) Dinabandhu Mitra wrote Neeldarpan.
(c) Bankim Chandra Chattopadhyay wrote Anandmath.
(d) Satyendranath Tagore became the first Indian to succeed in the Indian Civil Services.
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Chronology: *Neeldarpan* by Dinabandhu Mitra (1858-59); Satyendranath Tagore passed ICS (1863); Arya Samaj founded (1875); *Anandmath* by Bankim Chandra (1882).
**Keywords:** Neeldarpan, Arya Samaj, ICS, Anandmath.
**Related Dates:** 1858 (Neeldarpan), 1875 (Arya Samaj).
**Memory Trick:** "Indigo (Neel) came first after the 1857 fire".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Dayanand Saraswati (Arya Samaj) was earlier in the mid-19th century.
**Why Important:** Chronology questions test the candidate's grasp of the sequential evolution of cultural and social history.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-015
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Miscellaneous (Terminologies)
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the history of India, consider the following pairs:
1. Aurang — In-charge of treasury of the State
2. Banian — Indian agent of the East India Company
3. Mirasidar — Designated revenue payer to the State
Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Pair 1 is incorrect; 'Aurang' is a Persian term for a warehouse/workshop. Pair 2 is correct; 'Banian' acted as an agent/broker for European merchants. Pair 3 is correct; 'Mirasidar' was a hereditary holder of land and revenue payer in South India.
**Keywords:** Aurang, Banian, Mirasidar, Terminology.
**Related Context:** EIC Trade and Revenue Systems.
**Memory Trick:** "Banian = Broker; Mirasidar = Malick (Owner)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing "Aurang" with "Amil" or other treasury officials.
**Why Important:** UPSC frequently tests administrative and economic terms from NCERTs.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-016
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Miscellaneous (Archaeology)
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2023
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian History, Alexander Rea, A.H. Longhurst, Robert Sewell, James Burgess and Walter Elliot were associated with:
**Options:**
(a) archaeological excavations
(b) establishment of English Press in Colonial India
(c) establishment of Churches in Princely States
(d) construction of railways in Colonial India
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** These individuals were all prominent archaeologists and scholars who contributed to the discovery and preservation of India's ancient sites during the 19th and early 20th centuries.
**Keywords:** Alexander Rea, Robert Sewell, Archaeological excavations.
**Related Personality:** James Burgess (ASI Director).
**Memory Trick:** "Sewell and Rea = Site Search".
**Common Exam Trap:** Robert Sewell is often associated only with his book 'A Forgotten Empire' (Vijayanagara), but he was primarily an administrative archaeologist.
**Why Important:** Reflects the increasing overlap between History and Art & Culture/Archaeology in Prelims.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-017
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2023
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** By which one of the following Acts was the Governor General of Bengal designated as the Governor General of India?
**Options:**
(a) The Regulating Act
(b) The Pitt's India Act
(c) The Charter Act of 1793
(d) The Charter Act of 1833
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Charter Act of 1833 was the final step towards centralisation in British India. It made the Governor-General of Bengal the Governor-General of India and vested in him all civil and military powers.
**Keywords:** Charter Act 1833, Governor General of India, Centralisation.
**Related Personality:** Lord William Bentinck (First GG of India).
**Memory Trick:** "1833: Bengal became Bharat (India)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Regulating Act of 1773, which only made the Governor of Bengal the Governor-General of Bengal.
**Why Important:** Significant milestone in the administrative unification of India.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-018
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC (1885-1915)
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2014
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Partition of Bengal made by Lord Curzon in 1905 lasted until:
**Options:**
(a) the First World War when Indian leaders decided to support the British and demanded its annulment as a quid pro quo
(b) King George V abrogated Curzon's Act at the Royal Durbar in Delhi in 1911
(c) Gandhiji launched his Civil Disobedience Movement
(d) the Partition of India in 1947
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The partition of Bengal (1905) was annulled in 1911 by King George V at the Delhi Durbar. At the same time, the capital of India was shifted from Calcutta to Delhi.
**Keywords:** Partition of Bengal, Annulment, Delhi Durbar 1911.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Curzon, Lord Hardinge II.
**Memory Trick:** "1911: George V said Bengal is one again".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it lasted until 1947 (though it was partitioned again then, the 1905 act was long dead).
**Why Important:** This event ended the peak phase of the Swadeshi Movement.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-019
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC (1885-1915)
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2013
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Annie Besant was:
1. Responsible for starting the Home Rule Movement
2. The founder of the Theosophical Society
3. Once the President of the Indian National Congress
Select the correct statement/statements using the codes given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct; she started the Home Rule League in 1916. Statement 2 is incorrect; the Theosophical Society was founded by Madame Blavatsky and Colonel Olcott (Besant later became its President). Statement 3 is correct; she became the first woman President of INC in 1917.
**Keywords:** Annie Besant, Home Rule, Theosophical Society, INC President.
**Related Dates:** 1916 (Home Rule), 1917 (INC President).
**Memory Trick:** "Besant is a leader, not the founder of the society".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Besant founded the Theosophical Society since she is its most famous face in India.
**Why Important:** She was a pivotal link between Western radicalism and Indian nationalism.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-020
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC (1885-1915)
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2004
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. The First Session of the Indian National Congress was held in Calcutta.
2. The Second Session of the Indian National Congress was held under the presidentship of Dadabhai Naoroji.
3. Both Indian National Congress and Muslim League held their sessions at Lucknow in 1916 and concluded the Lucknow Pact.
Which of these statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3
(d) 3 only
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect; the first session was held in Bombay (1885). Statement 2 is correct; the second session (1886) was in Calcutta under Dadabhai Naoroji. Statement 3 is correct; the 1916 Lucknow session saw the historic Congress-League Pact.
**Keywords:** INC Sessions, Bombay, Calcutta, Lucknow Pact.
**Related Personalities:** W.C. Bonnerjee, Dadabhai Naoroji, Ambica Charan Mazumdar.
**Memory Trick:** "B-C-M-A" (Bombay, Calcutta, Madras, Allahabad) for the first four sessions.
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the venue of the first session (Bombay) with the second (Calcutta).
**Why Important:** Essential for understanding the early organisational growth of nationalism.

**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following submitted in 1875 a petition to the House of Commons demanding India's direct representation in the British Parliament?
**Options:**
(a) The Deccan Association
(b) The Indian Association
(c) The Madras Mahajan Sabha
(d) The Poona Sarvajanik Sabha
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Poona Sarvajanik Sabha (founded 1870) was an active political organisation that petitioned the House of Commons in 1875 for India’s direct representation in the UK Parliament.

**Related Personalities:** M.G. Ranade.
**Memory Trick:** "Poona Petition for Parliament".

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-022
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Rowlatt Act aimed at:
**Options:**
(a) compulsory economic support to war efforts
(b) imprisonment without trial and summary procedures for trial
(c) suppression of the Khilafat Movement
(d) imposition of restrictions on freedom of the press
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Rowlatt Act (1919), officially called the Anarchical and Revolutionary Crimes Act, authorised the government to imprison people without trial for up to two years and provided for summary trials for "seditious" activities.
**Keywords:** Rowlatt Act, Imprisonment without trial, No-Appeal-No-Dalil.
**Related Dates:** March 1919.
**Memory Trick:** "Black Act: No vakil, no dalil, no appeal".
**Common Exam Trap:** Focusing only on press restrictions (which were part of other acts like Vernacular Press Act).
**Why Important:** This "Stick" policy directly led to the Rowlatt Satyagraha and the Jallianwala Bagh massacre.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-023
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Lahore Session of the Indian National Congress (1929) is very important in history because:
1. The Congress passed a resolution demanding complete independence.
2. The rift between the extremists and moderates was resolved in that Session.
3. A resolution was passed rejecting the two-nation theory in that Session.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3
(c) 1 and 3
(d) None
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct; the session adopted the 'Purna Swaraj' (Complete Independence) resolution. Statement 2 is incorrect; the extremist-moderate rift was resolved at the 1916 Lucknow session. Statement 3 is incorrect; the two-nation theory became a major issue much later in the 1940s.
**Keywords:** Lahore Session 1929, Purna Swaraj, Jawaharlal Nehru.
**Related Dates:** December 31, 1929.
**Memory Trick:** "Lahore 29 = Purna Swaraj Flag".
**Common Exam Trap:** Mixing up the 1916 resolution of internal rifts with the 1929 radical policy shift.
**Why Important:** It redefined the goal of the freedom struggle from Dominion Status to total independence.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-024
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2010
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** For the Karachi session of Indian National Congress in 1931 presided over by Sardar Patel, who drafted the Resolution on Fundamental Rights and Economic Programme?
**Options:**
(a) Mahatma Gandhi
(b) Pandit Jawaharlal Nehru
(c) Dr. Rajendra Prasad
(d) Dr. B.R. Ambedkar
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** While the Karachi session was presided over by Vallabhbhai Patel, the landmark resolutions on Fundamental Rights and the National Economic Programme were drafted by Jawaharlal Nehru.
**Keywords:** Karachi Session 1931, Fundamental Rights, Economic Programme, Nehru.
**Related Personality:** Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel (President).
**Memory Trick:** "Patel presided, Nehru penned (the rights)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Sardar Patel as the drafter just because he was the session President.
**Why Important:** These resolutions defined the vision of the future independent Indian state.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-025
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2007
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The first Factory Act restricting the working hours of women and children and authorizing local governments to make necessary rules was adopted during whose time?
**Options:**
(a) Lord Lytton
(b) Lord Bentinck
(c) Lord Ripon
(d) Lord Canning
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The First Factory Act of 1881 was passed during the viceroyalty of Lord Ripon to improve labor conditions, particularly for children. It prohibited the employment of children under seven.
**Keywords:** First Factory Act 1881, Lord Ripon, Child Labour.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Ripon.
**Memory Trick:** "Ripon the Reformer" (Local Self Gov, Factory Act, Education).
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the 1891 Act (Lansdowne) which was more focused on women workers.
**Why Important:** It was the first legislative intervention into the industrial working conditions in India.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-026
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2021
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian history, which of the following statements is/are correct?
1. The Nizamat of Arcot emerged out of Hyderabad State.
2. The Mysore Kingdom emerged out of Vijayanagara Empire.
3. Rohilkhand Kingdom was formed out of the territories occupied by Ahmad Shah Durrani.
Select the correct answer using the code given below.
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3
(d) 3 only
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct; Arcot was a sub-division of the Deccan subah and its Nawab (Nizam-ul-Mulk) initially functioned under the Nizam of Hyderabad. Statement 2 is correct; the Wodeyar dynasty established Mysore in 1612 after the decline of the Vijayanagara Empire. Statement 3 is incorrect; Rohilkhand was established by Ali Muhammad Khan in the early 18th century following the decline of the Mughal Empire, not from territories of Ahmad Shah Durrani (Durrani's invasions happened later).
**Keywords:** Arcot, Mysore, Rohilkhand, Vijayanagara.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Nizam-ul-Mulk, Ahmad Shah Durrani.
**Memory Trick:** "A-H (Arcot-Hyderabad), M-V (Mysore-Vijayanagara)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking all 18th-century states emerged directly from Mughal decline; Mysore has specific roots in the older Vijayanagara structure.
**Why Important:** Tests the understanding of the political transition during the 18th century.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-027
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following statements does not apply to the system of Subsidiary Alliance introduced by Lord Wellesley?
**Options:**
(a) To maintain a large standing army at other's expense
(b) To keep India safe from Napoleonic danger
(c) To secure a fixed income for the Company
(d) To establish British paramountcy over the Indian States
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Subsidiary Alliance aimed at providing security to Indian states in exchange for a British contingent maintained at the ruler's cost (a), protecting India from the French/Napoleonic threat (b), and establishing British supremacy (d). However, there was no component of "fixed income" for the Company under this system; the payments were specifically for the upkeep of the subsidiary troops.
**Keywords:** Subsidiary Alliance, Lord Wellesley, Fixed Income.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Wellesley.
**Memory Trick:** "Army and Protection, but no Fixed Rent".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the maintenance payment with a fixed revenue/tribute like the Diwani.
**Why Important:** Core administrative policy that led to the expansion of British power.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-028
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2010
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What was the immediate reason for Ahmad Shah Abdali to invade India and fight the Third Battle of Panipat?
**Options:**
(a) He wanted to avenge the expulsion by Marathas of his viceroy Timur Shah from Lahore
(b) The frustrated governor of Jullundhar Adina Beg Khan invited him to invade Punjab
(c) He wanted to punish Mughal administration for non-payment of the revenues of the Chahar Mahal
(d) He wanted to annex all the fertile plains of Punjab up to the borders of Delhi
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Marathas, under Raghunath Rao, had expelled Timur Shah (Abdali’s son and viceroy) from Lahore in 1758. This direct provocation led Ahmad Shah Abdali to return to India to avenge his son's expulsion, resulting in the Third Battle of Panipat in 1761.
**Keywords:** Ahmad Shah Abdali, Third Battle of Panipat, Timur Shah.
**Related Dates:** 1761 (Panipat).
**Memory Trick:** "Timur was expelled, Papa Abdali returned".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting the invite from Adina Beg Khan (which was a factor earlier) instead of the "immediate" cause regarding his son.
**Why Important:** Pivotal battle that broke Maratha power and cleared the path for the British.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-029
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2010
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Pondicherry (now Puducherry), consider the following statements:
1. The first European power to occupy Pondicherry were the Portuguese.
2. The second European power to occupy Pondicherry were the French.
3. The English never occupied Pondicherry.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct; the Portuguese were the first Europeans to set up a factory there in the 16th century. Statement 2 is incorrect; the Danes and the Dutch also had settlements before the French became the primary occupiers in 1674. Statement 3 is incorrect; the English captured Pondicherry multiple times (e.g., 1761, 1778, 1793) during the Anglo-French wars before finally restoring it to the French.
**Keywords:** Pondicherry, Portuguese, French, English occupation.
**Related Personalities:** Francois Martin.
**Memory Trick:** "Pondy: Portuguese First, English often".
**Common Exam Trap:** Believing Pondicherry was *only* a French enclave throughout history.
**Why Important:** Tests micro-details of European colonial settlements.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-030
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2007
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The ruler of which one of the following States was removed from power by the British on the pretext of misgovernance?
**Options:**
(a) Awadh
(b) Jhansi
(c) Nagpur
(d) Satara
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** In 1856, Lord Dalhousie annexed the state of Awadh (Oudh) on the specific pretext of "maladministration" or misgovernance. Nawab Wajid Ali Shah was sent to Calcutta on a pension. The other states mentioned (Jhansi, Nagpur, Satara) were annexed under the "Doctrine of Lapse".
**Keywords:** Awadh, Misgovernance, Lord Dalhousie.
**Related Personalities:** Wajid Ali Shah.
**Memory Trick:** "Awadh = Admin failure (pretext)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the reason for Awadh's annexation with the Doctrine of Lapse.
**Why Important:** Major trigger for the 1857 Revolt in North India.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-031
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2007
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following Europeans were the last to come to pre-independence India as traders?
**Options:**
(a) Dutch
(b) English
(c) French
(d) Portuguese
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The order of arrival of European trading companies was: Portuguese (1498), English (1600), Dutch (1602), Danish (1616), and finally the French (1664).
**Keywords:** European Traders, French, Chronology.
**Related Dates:** 1664 (French EIC).
**Memory Trick:** "P-E-D-D-F" (Portuguese, English, Dutch, Danish, French).
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the Dutch (1602) and English (1600) arrival order.
**Why Important:** Basic chronological framework of Modern History.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-032
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2007
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following was the first fort constructed by the British in India?
**Options:**
(a) Fort William
(b) Fort St. George
(c) Fort St. David
(d) Fort St. Angelo
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Fort St. George was the first fortress built by the British East India Company in India, founded in 1644 at the coastal city of Madras. Fort William (Calcutta) was built later in 1696.
**Keywords:** Fort St. George, British Fort, Madras.
**Related Dates:** 1644.
**Memory Trick:** "George of Madras came before William of Calcutta".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Fort William due to Calcutta's later prominence as the capital.
**Why Important:** Marks the beginning of fortified British settlements.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-033
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** The Revolt of 1857
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2006
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who was the Governor-General of India during the Sepoy Mutiny?
**Options:**
(a) Lord Canning
(b) Lord Dalhousie
(c) Lord Hardinge
(d) Lord Lytton
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Lord Canning was the Governor-General of India during the 1857 Revolt. Following the revolt, he also became the first Viceroy of India under the Government of India Act 1858.
**Keywords:** Lord Canning, Sepoy Mutiny, 1857.
**Related Acts:** Government of India Act 1858.
**Memory Trick:** "Canning was the one for the 1857 firing".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Dalhousie, whose policies (Doctrine of Lapse) caused the revolt but who had left India just before it started.
**Why Important:** Landmark transition point from Company to Crown rule.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-034
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2006
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the year 1613, where was the English East India Company given permission to set up a factory (trading post)?
**Options:**
(a) Bangalore
(b) Madras
(c) Masulipatnam
(d) Surat
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** In 1613, Emperor Jahangir issued a farman permitting the English to establish a permanent factory at Surat. This followed the British naval victory over the Portuguese at Swally Hole (1612).
**Keywords:** English Factory, 1613, Surat, Jahangir.
**Related Personalities:** Captain Thomas Best, Jahangir.
**Memory Trick:** "1613: Surat set for English".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing this with Masulipatnam, where they set up a temporary factory earlier in 1611.
**Why Important:** First legal foothold of the English on the Indian mainland.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-035
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** The Revolt of 1857
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2006
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the revolt of the year 1857, who of the following was betrayed by a friend; captured and put to death by the British?
**Options:**
(a) Nana Sahib
(b) Kunwar Singh
(c) Khan Bahadur Khan
(d) Tantia Tope
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Tantia Tope, the close associate of Nana Sahib and a brilliant guerrilla leader, was betrayed by his friend Raja Man Singh of Narwar while hiding in the jungles. He was captured and executed in 1859.
**Keywords:** Tantia Tope, Betrayal, 1857.
**Related Personalities:** Nana Sahib, Raja Man Singh.
**Memory Trick:** "Tope was trapped by a friend".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Nana Sahib was captured (he escaped to Nepal).
**Why Important:** Marks the end of the resistance in the central Indian sector.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-036
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following is the correct chronological order of the battles fought in India in the 18th Century?
**Options:**
(a) Battle of Wandawash - Battle of Buxar - Battle of Ambur - Battle of Plassey
(b) Battle of Ambur - Battle of Plassey - Battle of Wandawash - Battle of Buxar
(c) Battle of Wandawash - Battle of Plassey - Battle of Ambur - Battle of Buxar
(d) Battle of Ambur - Battle of Buxar - Battle of Wandawash - Battle of Plassey
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Chronology: 1. Battle of Ambur (1749) during the Second Carnatic War. 2. Battle of Plassey (1757) where Clive defeated Siraj-ud-Daula. 3. Battle of Wandiwash (1760) where British defeated the French. 4. Battle of Buxar (1764) which established British supremacy.
**Keywords:** Battle of Ambur, Plassey, Wandiwash, Buxar.
**Related Dates:** 1749, 1757, 1760, 1764.
**Memory Trick:** "A-P-W-B (Ambur-Plassey-Wandiwash-Buxar)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Mixing up Ambur (early Carnatic) with Wandiwash (late Carnatic).
**Why Important:** Covers the primary military conflicts that decided the 18th-century power struggle.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-037
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** The Revolt of 1857
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following territories was not affected by the Revolt of 1857?
**Options:**
(a) Jhansi
(b) Chittor
(c) Jagdishpur
(d) Lucknow
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Revolt of 1857 was largely confined to Northern and Central India. Jhansi (Rani Laxmibai), Jagdishpur (Kunwar Singh), and Lucknow (Begum Hazrat Mahal) were major storm centres. Chittor (and most of Rajputana) remained largely unaffected or supported the British.
**Keywords:** Storm centres, 1857, Chittor.
**Related Personalities:** Rani Laxmibai, Kunwar Singh.
**Memory Trick:** "Chittor stayed quiet in '57".
**Common Exam Trap:** Including all of Rajasthan/Central India because of the geographical proximity to Jhansi.
**Why Important:** Highlights the regional limitations of the revolt.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-038
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** The Revolt of 1857
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following places did Kunwar Singh, a prominent leader of the Revolt of 1857, belong to?
**Options:**
(a) Bihar
(b) Madhya Pradesh
(c) Rajasthan
(d) Uttar Pradesh
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Kunwar Singh was the zamindar of Jagdishpur in the Arrah district of Bihar. Despite being in his 80s, he led the revolt in Bihar against the British.
**Keywords:** Kunwar Singh, Jagdishpur, Bihar, 1857.
**Related Personalities:** Amar Singh (his brother).
**Memory Trick:** "Kunwar from Bihar".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking he was from UP because he fought alongside leaders like Nana Sahib in later stages.
**Why Important:** One of the most effective local leaders of the 1857 uprising.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-039
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2004
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following princely States of the British rule in India:
1. Jhansi
2. Sambalpur
3. Satara
The correct chronological order in which they were annexed by the British is:
**Options:**
(a) 1 - 2 - 3
(b) 1 - 3 - 2
(c) 3 - 2 - 1
(d) 3 - 1 - 2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** These states were annexed under the Doctrine of Lapse by Lord Dalhousie. Chronology: Satara (1848), Sambalpur (1849), and Jhansi (1853).
**Keywords:** Doctrine of Lapse, Annexation, Satara, Sambalpur, Jhansi.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Dalhousie.
**Memory Trick:** "S-S-J (Satara-Sambalpur-Jhansi)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing Jhansi (famous leader) as the first annexation when it was actually later in the sequence.
**Why Important:** Essential for understanding the aggressive expansionist policies of Dalhousie.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-040
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2004
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following pairs are correctly matched?
List I (Period) : List II (Wars)
1. AD 1767-69 : First Anglo-Maratha War
2. AD 1790-92 : Third Mysore War
3. AD 1824-26 : First Anglo-Burmese War
4. AD 1845-46 : Second Sikh War
Select the correct answer using the codes given below:
**Options:**
(a) 2 and 4
(b) 3 and 4
(c) 1 and 2
(d) 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Pair 1 is incorrect; 1767-69 was the First Anglo-Mysore War (Maratha war was 1775-82). Pair 2 is correct; Third Mysore War occurred in 1790-92. Pair 3 is correct; First Anglo-Burmese war was 1824-26. Pair 4 is incorrect; 1845-46 was the First Anglo-Sikh War (Second was 1848-49).
**Keywords:** Anglo-Mysore, Anglo-Burmese, Anglo-Sikh, Chronology.
**Related Personalities:** Cornwallis, Dalhousie.
**Memory Trick:** "Mysore 3 = Cornwallis (1790s); Burma 1 = 1820s".
**Common Exam Trap:** Mixing up the First and Second Sikh/Maratha wars timelines.
**Why Important:** Tests precision in military and administrative chronology.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-041
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2004
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. In the Third Battle of Panipat, Ahmed Shah Abdali defeated Ibrahim Lodi.
2. Tipu Sultan was killed in the Third Anglo-Mysore War.
3. Mir Jafar entered in a conspiracy with the English for the defeat of Nawab Siraj-ud-daulah in the Battle of Plassey.
Which of these statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1, 2 and 3
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 3
(d) None
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect; Abdali defeated the Marathas in the Third Battle of Panipat (1761); Ibrahim Lodi was defeated by Babur in the First Battle (1526). Statement 2 is incorrect; Tipu was killed in the Fourth Anglo-Mysore War (1799). Statement 3 is correct; Mir Jafar’s treachery was the decisive factor at Plassey (1757).
**Keywords:** Panipat, Tipu Sultan, Mir Jafar, Plassey.
**Related Dates:** 1757 (Plassey), 1799 (Fourth Mysore War).
**Memory Trick:** "Mir Jafar = Traitor at Plassey".
**Common Exam Trap:** Anachronisms between the different battles of Panipat (Lodi vs. Marathas).
**Why Important:** Distinguishes between similar-sounding historical events and outcome.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-042
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2003
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In India, among the following locations, the Dutch established their earliest factory at:
**Options:**
(a) Surat
(b) Pulicat
(c) Cochin
(d) Cassimbazar
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Dutch established their first factory at Masulipatnam in 1605, followed by Pulicat in 1610. Among the given options, Pulicat is the earliest.
**Keywords:** Dutch Factory, Pulicat, 1610.
**Related Personalities:** Admiral Van der Hagen.
**Memory Trick:** "Dutch P-M (Pulicat-Masulipatnam)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Surat, which was a prominent English/Portuguese base, or Cochin (Portuguese first).
**Why Important:** Details the commercial topography of early European powers.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-043
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2003
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the entry of European powers into India, which one of the following statements is correct?
**Options:**
(a) The Portuguese captured Goa in 1499
(b) The English opened their first factory in South India at Masulipatnam
(c) In Eastern India, the English Company opened its first factory in Orissa in 1633
(d) Under the leadership of Dupleix, the French occupied Madras in 1746
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Option (b) is correct; English opened their first factory in South India at Masulipatnam in 1611. Option (a) is wrong; Goa was captured in 1510. Option (c) is wrong; the first factory in East India was at Hariharpur/Balasore (Orissa) in 1633. Option (d) is technically correct but the "South India first factory" statement in (b) is a more standard factual anchor for "entry". (Note: Some keys argue (b) is more definitive as a primary 'entry' fact).
**Keywords:** Masulipatnam, Portuguese Goa, English East India.
**Related Dates:** 1611 (Masulipatnam), 1510 (Goa).
**Memory Trick:** "English: Surat (West), Masuli (South), Balasore (East)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the arrival of Vasco da Gama (1498) with the capture of Goa (1510).
**Why Important:** Tests micro-level chronological accuracy of settlements.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-044
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2003
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Assertion (A): Shah Alam II spent the initial years as an Emperor far away from his capital.
Reason (R): There was always a lurking danger of foreign invasion from the north-west frontier.
**Options:**
(a) Both A and R are individually true and R is the correct explanation of A
(b) Both A and R are individually true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A
(c) A is true but R is false
(d) A is false but R is true
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Both are true. Shah Alam II did stay away from Delhi (mostly in Allahabad) for many years after the Battle of Buxar under British protection. It is also true that the NW frontier remained dangerous (Abdali invasions). However, the reason he stayed away was not primarily the NW danger but his defeat by the British and the ensuing internal politics of the Wazir/Marathas.
**Keywords:** Shah Alam II, Delhi, NW Frontier.
**Related Dates:** 1765 (Treaty of Allahabad).
**Memory Trick:** "Away from Delhi but because of Buxar, not Abdali".
**Common Exam Trap:** Linking "staying away" directly to the NW threat without considering the British/Internal power struggle.
**Why Important:** Highlights the vulnerability of the later Mughal Emperors.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-045
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2003
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Assertion (A): Marathas emerged as the strongest native power in India after the decline of Mughal empire.
Reason (R): Marathas were the first to have clear concept of a united Indian nation.
**Options:**
(a) Both A and R are individually true and R is the correct explanation of A
(b) Both A and R are individually true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A
(c) A is true but R is false
(d) A is false but R is true
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Assertion is true; Marathas were indeed the primary contenders for empire after the Mughals. Reason is false; the Maratha polity was a confederacy of chiefs (Peshwa, Holkar, Scindia) often at odds with each other. A "clear concept of a united Indian nation" in the modern sense did not exist then; it was a period of regional kingdoms.
**Keywords:** Maratha Power, Indian Nation, Confederacy.
**Related Personalities:** Peshwa Baji Rao I.
**Memory Trick:** "Strong power, but zero national unity (Confederacy)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Imposing modern nationalist concepts on 18th-century regional powers.
**Why Important:** Explains the structural weakness that led to the British victory over the Marathas.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-046
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2003
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following statements is NOT correct?
**Options:**
(a) Ali Mardan Khan introduced the system of revenue farming in Bengal
(b) Maharaja Ranjit Singh set up modern foundries to manufacture cannons at Lahore
(c) Sawai Jai Singh of Amber had Euclid's 'Elements of Geometry' translated into Sanskrit
(d) Sultan Tipu of Mysore gave money for the construction of the idol of Goddess Sarda in the Sringeri temple
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement (a) is incorrect; revenue farming (ijara) in Bengal was introduced by Murshid Quli Khan. Ali Mardan Khan was a prominent Mughal noble but not associated with this reform. Statements (b), (c), and (d) are all correct examples of 18th-century "progressive" rulers.
**Keywords:** Revenue farming, Murshid Quli Khan, Ranjit Singh, Jai Singh.
**Related Personalities:** Tipu Sultan.
**Memory Trick:** "Bengal revenue = Murshid Quli".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking all 18th-century rulers were "dark age" despots (they were actually quite innovative).
**Why Important:** Counter-narrative to the "Dark Age" theory of the 18th century.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-047
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Peasant Movement and Tribal Rebellions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2002
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With which one of the following mountain tribes did the British first come into contact after the grant of Diwani in the year 1765?
**Options:**
(a) Garo
(b) Khasis
(c) Kukis
(d) Tipperahs
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** After obtaining the Diwani of Bengal in 1765, the British EIC moved into the Sylhet region for trade (specifically for limestone). This brought them into their first contact and subsequent conflict with the Khasi tribe of the Meghalaya hills.
**Keywords:** Khasi Tribe, Diwani 1765, Sylhet.
**Related Personalities:** Tirut Singh (later leader).
**Memory Trick:** "Diwani led to Limestone and Khasis".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Garos or Kukis who came into conflict later in the 19th century.
**Why Important:** First instance of hill-tribe resistance against colonial economic intrusion.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-048
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2001
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following Indian rulers established embassies in foreign countries on modern lines?
**Options:**
(a) Haider Ali
(b) Mir Qasim
(c) Shah Alam II
(d) Tipu Sultan
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Tipu Sultan was a remarkably modern ruler who sought international alliances against the British. He sent embassies to France, Turkey, and Kabul to seek support and trade.
**Keywords:** Tipu Sultan, Embassies, Modern lines.
**Related Personalities:** Napoleon (whom he contacted).
**Memory Trick:** "Tipu the Traveller/Diplomat".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Haider Ali (his father), who was powerful but less focused on formal modern diplomacy.
**Why Important:** Tipu's internationalism made him the most feared Indian enemy of the British.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-049
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** “In this instance we could not play off the Mohammedans against the Hindus”. To which one of the following events did this remark of Aitchison relate?
**Options:**
(a) Revolt of 1857
(b) Champaran Satyagraha (1917)
(c) Khilafat and Non-cooperation Movement (1919-22)
(d) August Movement of 1942
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The remark was made regarding the Khilafat and Non-Cooperation movement (1919–22) when Hindu-Muslim unity reached its peak under Gandhi's leadership. The British official Aitchison lamented that they could not use communal divide-and-rule tactics during this phase.
**Keywords:** Aitchison remark, Hindu-Muslim unity, Khilafat.
**Related Personalities:** Mahatma Gandhi.
**Memory Trick:** "Aitchison = Against Unity (Khilafat)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting the 1857 Revolt (where there was also unity, but the specific quote is linked to the 1920s phase).
**Why Important:** High point of the communal harmony in the freedom struggle.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-050
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The last major extension of British Indian territory took place during the time of:
**Options:**
(a) Dufferin
(b) Dalhousie
(c) Lytton
(d) Curzon
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The annexation of Upper Burma in 1885 during the Third Anglo-Burmese War under Lord Dufferin was the last major territorial extension of British India. While minor boundary adjustments happened later (Curzon), no large kingdom was annexed after this.
**Keywords:** Lord Dufferin, Burma Annexation, 1885.
**Related Dates:** 1885.
**Memory Trick:** "Burma was the last big Bite (Dufferin)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Dalhousie, who annexed many *internal* Indian states, but Dufferin added an entire country (Burma).
**Why Important:** Completed the geographical map of the British Indian Empire.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-051
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1999
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I with List II and select the correct answer using the codes given below the Lists:
List I (Year) : List II (Event)
I. 1775 : A) First Anglo-Burmese War
II. 1780 : B) First Anglo-Afghan War
III. 1824 : C) First Anglo-Maratha War
IV. 1838 : D) Second Anglo-Mysore War
**Options:**
(a) I-D, II-C, III-B, IV-A
(b) I-D, II-C, III-A, IV-B
(c) I-C, II-D, III-A, IV-B
(d) I-C, II-D, III-B, IV-A
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The correct matches are: 1775 marked the start of the First Anglo-Maratha War (Treaty of Surat); 1780 was the beginning of the Second Anglo-Mysore War (Haider Ali's invasion of Carnatic); 1824 was the First Anglo-Burmese War (Treaty of Yandabo later in 1826); and 1838 was the start of the First Anglo-Afghan War.
**Keywords:** War Chronology, Maratha, Mysore, Burmese, Afghan.
**Related Personalities:** Warren Hastings (Maratha/Mysore), Lord Amherst (Burma), Lord Auckland (Afghan).
**Memory Trick:** "Maratha (75), Mysore (80), Burma (24), Afghan (38)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the sequence of the Mysore and Maratha wars which overlapped in the late 18th century.
**Why Important:** Tests the chronological framework of British territorial expansion across different frontiers.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-052
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** The Revolt of 1857
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1998
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The educated middle class in India:
**Options:**
(a) opposed the revolt of 1857
(b) supported the revolt of 1857
(c) remained neutral to the revolt of 1857
(d) fought against native rulers
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** During the Revolt of 1857, the educated middle class (modern intelligentsia) remained largely neutral. They viewed the revolt as backward-looking and reactionary, fearing that a victory for the rebels would restore the old feudal order rather than modernise India.
**Keywords:** Educated middle class, 1857 Revolt, Neutrality.
**Related Personalities:** Dadabhai Naoroji, Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar (era).
**Memory Trick:** "Middle class wanted Modernity, saw rebels as Old".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking they supported it because they were nationalists (modern nationalism developed later).
**Why Important:** Explains the lack of unified national character in the early anti-British uprisings.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-053
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was the first European to initiate the policy of taking part in the quarrels of Indian princes with a view to acquire territories?
**Options:**
(a) Clive
(b) Dupleix
(c) Albuquerque
(d) Warren Hastings
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Joseph François Dupleix, the French Governor, was the first to realize that European disciplined infantry could dominate Indian politics. He pioneered the system of providing military aid to local princes in exchange for land and influence, a strategy later refined by Robert Clive as the Subsidiary Alliance.
**Keywords:** Dupleix, French Governor, Territorial acquisition.
**Related Personalities:** Robert Clive.
**Memory Trick:** "Dupleix was the Designer of Intervention".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Robert Clive because he was more successful in the long run.
**Why Important:** Identifies the strategic origin of colonial political intervention.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-054
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following pairs is correctly matched?
**Options:**
(a) Battle of Buxar — Mir Jafar vs. Clive
(b) Battle of Wandiwash — French vs. East India Company
(c) Battle of Chilianwala — Dalhousie vs. Marathas
(d) Battle of Kharda — Nizam vs. East India Company
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** (b) is correct; Wandiwash (1760) saw the British defeat the French, ending French dreams in India. (a) is wrong; Buxar was the combined forces of Mir Kasim/Shuja-ud-Daula/Shah Alam II vs. Hector Munro. (c) is wrong; Chilianwala was Anglo-Sikh War. (d) is wrong; Kharda was Nizam vs. Marathas.
**Keywords:** Wandiwash, Buxar, Chilianwala, Kharda.
**Related Dates:** 1760 (Wandiwash).
**Memory Trick:** "W-F-E (Wandiwash-French-English)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the participants of Buxar (Hector Munro, not Clive) and Plassey (Clive).
**Why Important:** Differentiates between key military turning points of the 18th century.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-055
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Regarding Wood’s Dispatch, which of the following statements are true?
1. Grants-in-aid system was introduced.
2. Establishment of universities was recommended.
3. English as a medium of instruction at all levels of education was recommended.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Wood's Despatch (1854) introduced the grants-in-aid system (1) and recommended setting up universities in Calcutta, Bombay, and Madras (2). However, it recommended English only for higher education, while suggesting vernacular languages for primary school education (3 is incorrect).
**Keywords:** Wood's Despatch, Grants-in-aid, Universities.
**Related Personality:** Charles Wood.
**Memory Trick:** "Magna Carta of Education: Vernacular for Kids, English for College".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Wood's Despatch followed Macaulay in making English the medium at *all* levels.
**Why Important:** Known as the "Magna Carta of English Education in India."
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-056
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Economically, one of the results of the British rule in India in the 19th century was the:
**Options:**
(a) increase in the export of Indian handicrafts
(b) growth in the number of Indian owned factories
(c) commercialization of Indian agriculture
(d) rapid increase in the urban population
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** British policies promoted the cultivation of cash crops (indigo, cotton, tea, opium) to serve British industries. This "commercialization" forced peasants into a market economy, often leading to debt and famine, while handicrafts declined (de-industrialization).
**Keywords:** Commercialization, Agriculture, 19th Century.
**Related Context:** Drain of Wealth.
**Memory Trick:** "British wanted Cash Crops, not Crafts".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking urban population increased (it actually decreased during the initial "de-urbanization" phase).
**Why Important:** Central theme of the economic impact of colonialism.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-057
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2008
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following used the phrase 'Un-British' to criticize the English colonial control of India?
**Options:**
(a) Anandmohan Bose
(b) Badruddin Tyabji
(c) Dadabhai Naoroji
(d) Pherozeshah Mehta
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Dadabhai Naoroji, in his book "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India," argued that the British administration in India was inconsistent with British principles of fair play and justice back home, hence calling it "Un-British."
**Keywords:** Un-British, Dadabhai Naoroji, Drain of Wealth.
**Related Books:** Poverty and Un-British Rule in India.
**Memory Trick:** "Naoroji noticed the No-British fairness in India".
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing Naoroji with other economic critics like R.C. Dutt.
**Why Important:** Foundational text for the early nationalist economic critique.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-058
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2008
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who was the Viceroy of India when the Rowlatt Act was passed?
**Options:**
(a) Lord Irwin
(b) Lord Reading
(c) Lord Chelmsford
(d) Lord Wavell
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Rowlatt Act was passed in March 1919 during the viceroyalty of Lord Chelmsford (1916–1921). It coincided with the Montagu-Chelmsford reforms of the same year.
**Keywords:** Rowlatt Act, Viceroy, 1919.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Chelmsford.
**Memory Trick:** "Mont-Ford reforms and Rowlatt came together".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Lord Reading (who came just after in 1921).
**Why Important:** Connects legal repression with the administrative head of the time.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-059
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. Warren Hastings was the first Governor-General who established a regular police force in India on the British pattern.
2. A Supreme Court was established at Calcutta by the Regulating Act, 1773.
3. The Indian Penal Code came into effect in the year 1860.
Which of the statements given above are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2
(b) 2 and 3
(c) 1 and 3
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect; Lord Cornwallis (not Hastings) established the regular police force (thanas and darogas). Statement 2 is correct; the 1773 Act set up the Supreme Court in 1774. Statement 3 is correct; the IPC was drafted by Macaulay's commission and enacted in 1860.
**Keywords:** Cornwallis, Regulating Act 1773, IPC 1860.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Cornwallis.
**Memory Trick:** "Cornwallis = Cop; Hastings = High Court (era)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Attributing police reforms to Hastings instead of Cornwallis.
**Why Important:** Tracks the evolution of the modern Indian legal and executive machinery.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-060
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following repealed the Vernacular Press Act?
**Options:**
(a) Lord Dufferin
(b) Lord Ripon
(c) Lord Curzon
(d) Lord Hardinge
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Lord Lytton passed the "Gagging Act" (Vernacular Press Act) in 1878 to suppress regional newspapers. Lord Ripon, known for his liberal policies, repealed it in 1882.
**Keywords:** Vernacular Press Act, Repeal, Lord Ripon.
**Related Personality:** Lord Lytton (enacted it).
**Memory Trick:** "Lytton Locked, Ripon Released (the press)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Mixing up the enactors (Lytton) and the repealers (Ripon).
**Why Important:** Turning point in the struggle for press freedom.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-061
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2004
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following pairs is not correctly matched?
**Options:**
(a) Pitt's India Act — Warren Hastings
(b) Doctrine of Lapse — Dalhousie
(c) Vernacular Press Act — Curzon
(d) Ilbert Bill — Ripon
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Vernacular Press Act (1878) was enacted by Lord Lytton, not Lord Curzon. All other pairs are correct: Pitt's India Act (1784) was under Hastings; Doctrine of Lapse (1848) under Dalhousie; and Ilbert Bill (1883) under Ripon.
**Keywords:** Pitt's India Act, Ilbert Bill, Lytton.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Lytton.
**Memory Trick:** "Curzon = Partition; Lytton = Languages (Press Act)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Mismatching Ripon with the Press Act because he *repealed* it, but the question asks about the act's primary association (usually enactors).
**Why Important:** Tests knowledge of specific governor-general policy associations.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-062
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1997
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What is the correct chronological sequence of the following?
I. Wood's Education Despatch
II. Macaulay's Minute on Education
III. The Sargent Education Report
IV. Indian Education (Hunter Commission)
**Options:**
(a) II, I, IV, III
(b) II, I, III, IV
(c) I, II, IV, III
(d) IV, III, I, II
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Chronology: 1. Macaulay’s Minute (1835). 2. Wood’s Despatch (1854). 3. Hunter Commission (1882). 4. Sargent Plan (1944).
**Keywords:** Education Chronology, Macaulay, Wood, Hunter, Sargent.
**Related Dates:** 1835, 1854, 1882, 1944.
**Memory Trick:** "M-W-H-S (Macaulay-Wood-Hunter-Sargent)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Hunter Commission (1882) was earlier because it relates to primary education.
**Why Important:** Tracks the century-long evolution of the colonial education system.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-063
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following landmarks in Indian education:
I. Hindu College, Calcutta
II. University of Calcutta
III. Adam's Report
IV. Wood's Despatch
The correct chronological order of these landmarks is:
**Options:**
(a) I, III, IV, II
(b) I, IV, III, II
(c) III, I, IV, II
(d) III, II, IV, I
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Chronology: 1. Hindu College (1817) founded by David Hare/Rammohan Roy. 2. Adam's Report (1835-38) on vernacular education. 3. Wood's Despatch (1854). 4. University of Calcutta (1857).
**Keywords:** Hindu College, Adam's Report, Calcutta University.
**Related Dates:** 1817, 1835, 1854, 1857.
**Memory Trick:** "College first, then University".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Adam's report preceded the founding of modern colleges.
**Why Important:** Highlights the shift from private/missionary efforts to state-led institutionalization.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-064

**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims

**Question:** Who among the following was associated as Secretary with Hindu Female School which later came to be known as Bethune Female School?
**Options:**
(a) Annie Besant
(b) Debendranath Tagore
(c) Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar
(d) Sarojini Naidu
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar was a great champion of women's education. He was closely associated with J.E.D. Bethune in founding the Hindu Female School (1849) in Calcutta and served as its Secretary.
**Keywords:** Hindu Female School, Bethune, Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar.
**Related Personality:** J.E.D. Bethune.
**Memory Trick:** "Bethune and Vidyasagar: Better for girls".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Annie Besant due to her later work in women's empowerment.
**Why Important:** Vidyasagar’s contribution to female literacy is a frequent UPSC theme.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-065
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was associated with the publication of the first Marathi newspaper for the depressed classes, 'Din Bandhu'?
**Options:**
(a) Gopal Baba Walangkar
(b) Jyotiba Phule
(c) Mahatma Gandhi
(d) B. R. Ambedkar
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** 'Din Bandhu' (Brother of the Poor) was a Marathi newspaper started in 1877 as the organ of the Satyashodhak Samaj founded by Jyotiba Phule. It focused on the grievances of the peasants and depressed classes.
**Keywords:** Din Bandhu, Marathi newspaper, Jyotiba Phule.
**Related Organization:** Satyashodhak Samaj.
**Memory Trick:** "Phule = Friend of the Poor (Din Bandhu)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Ambedkar, who started many later newspapers like Mooknayak.
**Why Important:** Early example of Dalit/Depressed class journalism.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-066
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** His principal forte was social and religious reform. He relied upon legislation to do away with social ills. He was:
**Options:**
(a) Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar
(b) Behramji Merwanji Malabari
(c) Mahadev Govind Ranade
(d) B. R. Ambedkar
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Behramji Malabari (a Parsi reformer) is famous for his relentless crusade against child marriage. His efforts led to the enactment of the Age of Consent Act, 1891, which raised the age of consent for girls.
**Keywords:** Malabari, Age of Consent, Legislation.
**Related Personality:** B.M. Malabari.
**Memory Trick:** "Malabari = Marriage age legislation".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Vidyasagar (who also used legislation for widow remarriage) or Ranade.
**Why Important:** Significant reformer who used colonial law to target specific social evils.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-067
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Revolutionary & Communist Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following was an émigré Communist Journal of M. N. Roy?
**Options:**
(a) Kisan Sabha
(b) The Worker
(c) Vanguard
(d) Anushilan
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** M.N. Roy, who founded the CPI in Tashkent (1920), published the journal 'Vanguard' from Berlin to spread communist ideology in India.

**Memory Trick:** "Roy leads the Vanguard".

**Why Important:** Marks the international/émigré phase of the Indian left movement.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-068
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Revolutionary & Communist Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Barrah dacoity was the first major venture of the revolutionary terrorists of the freedom movement in:
**Options:**
(a) Bombay Karnataka
(b) Punjab
(c) East Bengal
(d) The Madras Presidency
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Barrah Dacoity (1908) was organized by the Dacca Anushilan Samiti under the leadership of Pulin Das in the East Bengal region.
**Keywords:** Barrah Dacoity, Pulin Das, East Bengal.
**Related Organization:** Dacca Anushilan Samiti.
**Memory Trick:** "Barrah in Bengal".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it belongs to Punjab (site of many later actions).
**Why Important:** Represents the early phase of revolutionary "action" to fund political movements.
