**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-069
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2001
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was the President of the All-India States' Peoples' Conference in 1939?
**Options:**
(a) Jaya Prakash Narayan
(b) Jawaharlal Nehru
(c) Sheikh Abdullah
(d) Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Jawaharlal Nehru was elected the President of the All-India States' Peoples' Conference (AISPC) in 1939. This marked the closer integration of the struggle in Princely States with the national movement.
**Keywords:** AISPC, 1939, Jawaharlal Nehru.
**Related Personalities:** Sheikh Abdullah (later president).
**Memory Trick:** "Nehru: Bridge between India and the States".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Sardar Patel (who was more associated with the later *integration* of states).
**Why Important:** Showcases the shift in INC policy towards the people of princely states.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-070
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Revolutionary & Communist Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2021
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the context of Colonial India, Shah Nawaz Khan, Prem Kumar Sehgal and Gurbaksh Singh Dhillon are remembered as:
**Options:**
(a) leaders of Swadeshi and Boycott Movement
(b) members of the Interim Government in 1946
(c) members of the Drafting Committee in the Constituent Assembly
(d) officers of the Indian National Army
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** These three were the main accused in the historic Red Fort Trials (1945). They were high-ranking officers of Subhash Bose’s Indian National Army (INA).
**Keywords:** Shah Nawaz Khan, Sehgal, Dhillon, INA.
**Related Context:** Red Fort Trials.
**Memory Trick:** "Three faiths (Hindu, Muslim, Sikh) in one INA trial".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking they were members of the Interim Government (Shah Nawaz Khan joined the govt later, but they are *remembered* for the INA trial).
**Why Important:** The INA trials were a major catalyst for the final anti-British upsurge.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-071
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Personality Based Questions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** While delivering the presidential address, the Congress President who advocated the introduction of Roman script for Hindi language was:
**Options:**
(a) Mahatma Gandhi
(b) Jawaharlal Nehru
(c) Abul Kalam Azad
(d) Subhas Chandra Bose
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** At the Haripura Session (1938), Subhas Chandra Bose suggested that the Hindustani language should be written in the Roman script to facilitate easy learning and national unity.
**Keywords:** Roman script, Hindustani, Subhas Chandra Bose.
**Related Dates:** 1938 (Haripura).
**Memory Trick:** "Bose's Bold Bold script".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Nehru or Azad due to their deep involvement in linguistic debates.
**Why Important:** Unusual proposal by a major leader regarding national integration.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-072
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2015
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. The first woman President of the Indian National Congress was Sarojini Naidu.
2. The first Muslim President of the Indian National Congress was Badruddin Tyabji.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect; the first woman President was Annie Besant (1917). Sarojini Naidu was the first *Indian* woman President (1925). Statement 2 is correct; Badruddin Tyabji presided over the 3rd session in Madras (1887).
**Keywords:** INC Presidents, Woman, Muslim, Tyabji.
**Related Personalities:** Annie Besant, Sarojini Naidu.
**Memory Trick:** "Annie came first (17), Sarojini later (25)".
**Common Exam Trap:** Forgetting the distinction between "first woman" and "first Indian woman."
**Why Important:** Basic factual pillars of INC history.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-073
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2016
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What was the main reason for the split in the Indian National Congress at Surat in 1907?
**Options:**
(a) Introduction of communalism into Indian politics by Lord Minto
(b) Extremists' lack of faith in the capacity of the moderates to negotiate with the British Government
(c) Foundation of Muslim League
(d) Aurobindo Ghosh's inability to be elected as the President of the Indian National Congress
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The split (Surat Split) occurred because the Extremists (Tilak, Lajpat Rai, etc.) felt that the Moderates' methods of "Prayer, Petition, and Protest" were ineffective and wanted a more radical mass struggle (Swadeshi/Boycott) across all of India.
**Keywords:** Surat Split, Extremists, Moderates, 1907.
**Related Personalities:** Rash Behari Ghosh (President).
**Memory Trick:** "Split because of Faith failure".
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Lord Minto's role (which was external) rather than the internal ideological lack of faith.
**Why Important:** Weakened the national movement for a decade.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-074
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Swadeshi Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2019
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Swadeshi Movement, consider the following statements:
1. It contributed to the revival of the indigenous artisan crafts and industries.
2. The National Council of Education was established as a part of Swadeshi Movement.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Both are correct. The movement promoted 'Swadeshi' (indigenous) goods, giving a boost to handlooms and crafts (1). In 1906, the National Council of Education was set up to provide education on national lines and under national control (2).
**Keywords:** Swadeshi, National Council of Education, Indigenous crafts.
**Related Dates:** 1906 (Education Council).
**Memory Trick:** "Swadeshi = Self-Industry + Self-Education".
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Education Council was established earlier in the Renaissance phase.
**Why Important:** Shows the constructive/institutional side of the anti-partition struggle.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-075
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Swadeshi Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the book "Desher Katha" written by Sakharam Ganesh Deuskar during the freedom struggle, consider the following statements:
1. It warned against the Colonial State’s hypnotic conquest of the mind.
2. It inspired the performance of swadeshi street plays and folk songs.
3. The use of ‘desh’ by Deuskar was in the specific context of the region of Bengal.
Which of the statements given above are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Sakharam Ganesh Deuskar published "Desher Katha" (1904) to expose British economic exploitation. Statements 1 and 2 are correct as it warned against cultural conquest and inspired folk media. Statement 3 is incorrect; though written in Bengali, he used 'desh' to refer to the whole of India (Bharat), aiming for a pan-Indian national identity.
**Keywords:** Desher Katha, Sakharam Ganesh Deuskar, Swadeshi literature.
**Related Personalities:** Sakharam Ganesh Deuskar.
**Memory Trick:** "Deuskar's Desh was bigger than Bengal".
**Common Exam Trap:** Assuming a Bengali book only refers to the Bengal region.
**Why Important:** Reflects the influence of vernacular literature on the national consciousness.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-076
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies (Education)
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to educational institutions during colonial rule in India, consider the following pairs:
1. Institution: Sanskrit College at Benaras — Founder: William Jones
2. Institution: Calcutta Madarsa — Founder: Warren Hastings
3. Institution: Fort William College — Founder: Arthur Wellesley
Which of the pairs given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3
(d) 3 only
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Pair 1 is incorrect: The Sanskrit College at Benaras was established by Jonathan Duncan (1791), not William Jones (who founded the Asiatic Society of Bengal). Pair 2 is correct: Warren Hastings established the Calcutta Madarsa in 1781 for the study of Muslim law. Pair 3 is incorrect: Fort William College was founded by Richard Wellesley (Lord Wellesley), the Governor-General, not his brother Arthur Wellesley (the Duke of Wellington).
**Keywords:** Calcutta Madarsa, Sanskrit College, Fort William College.
**Related Personalities:** Jonathan Duncan, Warren Hastings, Lord Wellesley.
**Memory Trick:** "Duncan's Sanskrit, Hastings' Madarsa, Wellesley's William."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the two Wellesley brothers (Richard vs. Arthur) or the Orientalist founders (Jones vs. Duncan).
**Why Important:** Tests knowledge of early British efforts to understand Indian languages and laws for administration.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-077
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2017
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The object of the Butler Committee of 1927 was to?
**Options:**
(a) Define the jurisdiction of the Central and Provincial Governments.
(b) Define the powers of the Secretary of State for India.
(c) Impose censorship on national press.
(d) Examine and improve the relationship between the Government of India and the Indian States.
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Harcourt Butler Committee (Indian States Committee) was appointed in 1927 to examine the nature of the relationship between the British Paramount Power and the Indian Princely States and to suggest means for more satisfactory economic relations.
**Keywords:** Butler Committee, Princely States, Paramountcy.
**Related Personalities:** Harcourt Butler.
**Memory Trick:** "Butler for the Princes (States)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with administrative committees like the Muddiman Committee (Dyarchy) or Hartog Committee (Education).
**Why Important:** Reflects the British attempt to reconcile the role of "Paramountcy" with the rising nationalist demand for federation.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-078
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2022
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the proposals of Cripps Mission, consider the following statements:
1. The Constituent Assembly would have members nominated by the Provincial Assemblies as well as the Princely States.
2. Any Province, which is not prepared to accept the new Constitution would have the right to sign a separate agreement with Britain regarding its future status.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect because the Constituent Assembly members were to be partly elected by the provincial assemblies and partly *nominated by the princes* (not nominated by assemblies). Statement 2 is correct; the Cripps Mission offered a "local option" where provinces could stay out of the Indian Union and negotiate separate treaties with the British Crown.
**Keywords:** Cripps Mission, Constituent Assembly, Dominion Status.
**Related Dates:** March 1942.
**Memory Trick:** "Cripps = Partial Democracy (Nominated Princes) + Partial Partition (Separate Treaties)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Overlooking the difference between "elected" and "nominated" for the assembly members.
**Why Important:** The failure of these proposals directly led to the Quit India Movement.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-079
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2002
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** During the Indian freedom struggle, the Khudai Khidmatgars, also known as Red Shirts, called for?
**Options:**
(a) the Union of Pashtun tribal areas in north-west with Afghanistan.
(b) the adoption of terrorist tactics for ousting the colonial rulers.
(c) the adoption of communist revolutionary ideology for social reform.
(d) the Pathan regional nationalist unity and a struggle against colonialism.
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Khudai Khidmatgar (Servants of God) was a non-violent movement led by Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan (Frontier Gandhi) among the Pathans. They advocated for Pathan nationalist unity, social reform, and total independence from British rule.
**Keywords:** Khudai Khidmatgar, Red Shirts, Frontier Gandhi, Pashtun.
**Related Personalities:** Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan.
**Memory Trick:** "Red Shirts = Non-violent Pathan Nationalists."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking they wanted to join Afghanistan (irredentism) or were violent revolutionaries.
**Why Important:** Rare example of successful Gandhian mass mobilisation in a tribal, traditionally martial society.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-080
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In 1920, which of the following changed its name to "Swarajya Sabha"?
**Options:**
(a) All India Home Rule League
(b) Hindu Mahasabha
(c) South Indian Liberal Federation
(d) The Servants of India Society
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** In 1920, the All India Home Rule League (founded by Tilak and Besant) elected Mahatma Gandhi as its President. Under his influence, the organization changed its name to "Swarajya Sabha".
**Keywords:** Swarajya Sabha, Home Rule League, 1920.
**Related Personalities:** Mahatma Gandhi.
**Memory Trick:** "Home Rule became Swarajya Sabha under Gandhi."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Swaraj Party (formed 1922/23).
**Why Important:** Marks the transition of the Home Rule movement into the broader Gandhian organizational structure.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-081
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2003
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the context of the colonial period of India, the Whitley Commission was concerned with?
**Options:**
(a) Labour
(b) Education
(c) Public Health
(d) Reorganization of Civil Services
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Royal Commission on Labour, also known as the Whitley Commission (1929), was appointed to investigate the existing conditions of labour in industrial undertakings and plantations in British India and to make recommendations.
**Keywords:** Whitley Commission, Labour, Industrial conditions.
**Related Acts:** Trade Unions Act 1926 (context).
**Memory Trick:** "Whitley = Work (Labour)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Mixing it up with the Hartog Commission (Education) or Aitchison Commission (Civil Services).
**Why Important:** Led to significant data collection on the plight of the Indian industrial working class.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-082
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2024
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to revenue collection by Cornwallis, consider the following statements:
1. Under the Ryotwari Settlement of revenue collection, the peasants were exempted from revenue payment in case of bad harvests or natural calamities.
2. Under the Permanent Settlement in Bengal, if the Zamindar failed to pay his revenues to the state, on or before the fixed date, he would be removed from his Zamindari.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect: Under the Ryotwari system (and British systems generally), revenue was rigid and often collected strictly even during famines. Statement 2 is correct: The "Sunset Law" part of the Permanent Settlement stipulated that if revenue was not paid by the sunset of a fixed date, the Zamindari could be auctioned off.
**Keywords:** Permanent Settlement, Ryotwari, Sunset Law, Cornwallis.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Cornwallis, Thomas Munro.
**Memory Trick:** "Permanent Settlement = Permanent Sunset (if you don't pay)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the British were lenient during "bad harvests" under any land system.
**Why Important:** This rigidity was a primary cause of agrarian distress and the ruin of traditional Indian society.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-083
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2021
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following leaders proposed to adopt Complete Independence as the goal of the Congress in the Ahmedabad session of 1920?
**Options:**
(a) Abul Kalam Azad
(b) Hasrat Mohani
(c) Jawaharlal Nehru
(d) Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** At the Ahmedabad Session (1921 - snippet says 1920 context of NCM start), Hasrat Mohani, a revolutionary poet and leader, was the first to move a resolution demanding "Purna Swaraj" or complete independence. Gandhi opposed it at the time, favouring Dominion Status/Swaraj within the Empire.
**Keywords:** Hasrat Mohani, Complete Independence, Ahmedabad Session.
**Related Dates:** 1921.
**Memory Trick:** "Hasrat (Desire) for Purna Swaraj."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Nehru (who passed it later in 1929) or Gandhi.
**Why Important:** Highlights the presence of radical voices within the INC long before 1929.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-084
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2015
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the Cabinet Mission, which of the following statements is/are correct?
1. It recommended a federal government.
2. It enlarged the powers of the Indian courts.
3. It provided for more Indians in the ICS.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3
(c) 1 and 3
(d) None
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct: The Cabinet Mission (1946) proposed a three-tier federal structure with a weak center. Statements 2 and 3 are incorrect: The Mission focused on the transfer of power and constitutional framework, not judicial powers or ICS recruitment.
**Keywords:** Cabinet Mission 1946, Federal Government, Weak Center.
**Related Personalities:** Pethick-Lawrence, Stafford Cripps, A.V. Alexander.
**Memory Trick:** "Cabinet = Groups (A,B,C) + Federal."
**Common Exam Trap:** Adding general "reformist" points (like ICS or Courts) that were not the mission's focus.
**Why Important:** The last major British effort to keep India united.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-085
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2014
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What was/were the object/objects of Queen Victoria's Proclamation (1858)?
1. To disclaim any intention to annex Indian States.
2. To place the Indian administration under the British Crown.
3. To regulate East India Company's trade with India.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The 1858 Proclamation (1) disclaimed further annexations (end of Doctrine of Lapse) and (2) transferred governance from the Company to the Crown. Statement 3 is incorrect because the Company was abolished entirely as a ruling power; its trade had already been regulated/ended by previous Charter Acts.
**Keywords:** Queen's Proclamation 1858, Crown Rule, Annexation.
**Related Acts:** Government of India Act 1858.
**Memory Trick:** "1858: No more Lapse, Hello Crown."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it "regulated" the Company when it actually "ended" the Company's rule.
**Why Important:** Fundamental shift in the basis of British rule in India.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-086
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2019
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following pairs:
Movement/Organization — Leader
1. All India Anti-Untouchability League — Mahatma Gandhi
2. All India Kisan Sabha — Swami Sahajanand Saraswati
3. Self-Respect Movement — E.V. Ramaswami Naicker
Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** All three are correct. Gandhi founded the Anti-Untouchability League (later Harijan Sevak Sangh) in 1932. Swami Sahajanand founded the All India Kisan Sabha (AIKS) in 1936. Periyar (Naicker) started the Self-Respect Movement in 1925.
**Keywords:** Anti-Untouchability League, All India Kisan Sabha, Self-Respect Movement.
**Related Personalities:** Gandhi, Sahajanand Saraswati, Periyar.
**Memory Trick:** "G-Anti, S-Kisan, P-Self."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing All India Kisan Sabha with regional ones like the Bihar Kisan Sabha.
**Why Important:** Essential for understanding the diversification of the national movement into social and class struggles.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-087
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Personality Based Questions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2021
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was associated with "Songs from Prison", a translation of ancient Indian religious lyrics in English?
**Options:**
(a) Bal Gangadhar Tilak
(b) Jawaharlal Nehru
(c) Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi
(d) Sarojini Naidu
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** While in Yerwada Jail in 1930, Mahatma Gandhi translated several Sanskrit hymns and lyrics from the Upanishads and other texts into English, which were later published as "Songs from Prison".
**Keywords:** Songs from Prison, Gandhi, Yerwada Jail.
**Related Context:** Civil Disobedience Movement (imprisonment).
**Memory Trick:** "Gandhi sang in Jail (Songs from Prison)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Sarojini Naidu (poet) or Nehru (who wrote 'Discovery of India' in jail).
**Why Important:** Reflects Gandhi's deep spiritual engagement and intellectual work during political incarceration.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-088
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Key Personalities & Ideologies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** One common agreement between Gandhism and Marxism is?
**Options:**
(a) The final goal of a stateless society.
(b) Class struggle.
(c) Abolition of private property.
(d) Economic determinism.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Both Gandhi and Marx envisioned an ultimate stage of human social evolution where the state would wither away (stateless society). However, their methods (Non-violence/Varna vs. Revolution/Class Struggle) were diametrically opposite.
**Keywords:** Gandhism, Marxism, Stateless Society.
**Related Concepts:** Sarvodaya vs. Communism.
**Memory Trick:** "Goal is same (No State), Path is different."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting "Class struggle" or "Private property" which Gandhi did not seek to abolish through state force (he believed in Trusteeship).
**Why Important:** High-level conceptual question testing political theory within history.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-089
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1997
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I with List II and select the correct answer:
List I:
I. Butler Committee
II. Hartog Committee Report
III. Hunter Inquiry Committee Report
IV. Muddiman Committee Report
List II:
A) Jallianwala Bagh Massacre
B) Relationship between Indian States and Paramount Power
C) Working of Dyarchy
D) Growth of Education
**Options:**
(a) I-B, II-D, III-A, IV-C
(b) I-A, II-D, III-B, IV-C
(c) I-B, II-A, III-C, IV-D
(d) I-C, II-B, III-A, IV-D
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** I-B: Butler Committee (States relations). II-D: Hartog Committee (Education). III-A: Hunter Committee (Jallianwala Bagh inquiry). IV-C: Muddiman Committee (Inquiry into 1919 Act/Dyarchy).
**Keywords:** Butler, Hartog, Hunter, Muddiman.
**Related Dates:** 1919 (Hunter), 1924 (Muddiman), 1927 (Butler), 1929 (Hartog).
**Memory Trick:** "Butler-State, Hartog-Home (School/Edu), Hunter-Hit (Massacre), Muddiman-Mend (Dyarchy)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the Hunter *Education* Commission (1882) with the Hunter *Inquiry* Committee (1919).
**Why Important:** Tracks the various "Check and Balance" committees appointed by the British.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-090
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1997
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I (Events) with List II (Results):
I. Morley Minto Reforms
II. Simon Commission
III. The Chauri-Chaura incident
IV. The Dandi March
Results:
A) Country-wide agitation
B) Withdrawal of a movement
C) Communal Electorates
D) Illegal manufacture of salt
**Options:**
(a) I-C, II-A, III-B, IV-D
(b) I-D, II-A, III-B, IV-C
(c) I-B, II-C, III-D, IV-A
(d) I-C, II-D, III-A, IV-B
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Morley-Minto (1909) introduced Separate/Communal electorates. Simon Commission (1928) led to country-wide protests ("Go Back Simon"). Chauri-Chaura (1922) led to the withdrawal of Non-Cooperation. Dandi March (1930) started the illegal manufacture of salt.
**Keywords:** Morley-Minto, Simon Commission, Chauri-Chaura, Dandi March.
**Related Acts:** Indian Councils Act 1909.
**Memory Trick:** "Morley-Muslim, Simon-Shouts, Chauri-Cancel, Dandi-Dishonour (Salt Law)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the *result* (withdrawal) with the *event* itself.
**Why Important:** Core linkages between turning points in the freedom struggle.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-091
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Peasant Movement and Tribal Rebellions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1999
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following events:
I. Indigo Revolt
II. Santhal Rebellion
III. Deccan Riot
IV. Mutiny of the Sepoys
The correct chronological sequence of these events is:
**Options:**
(a) IV, II, I, III
(b) IV, II, III, I
(c) II, IV, I, III
(d) II, IV, III, I
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Chronology: 1. Santhal Rebellion (1855–56). 2. Mutiny of 1857. 3. Indigo Revolt (1859–60). 4. Deccan Riots (1875).
**Keywords:** Santhal, 1857 Mutiny, Indigo, Deccan Riots.
**Related Personalities:** Sidhu and Kanhu (Santhal), Digambar Biswas (Indigo).
**Memory Trick:** "Santhal before Sepoy, Indigo after."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking 1857 was the first major disturbance; the Santhal uprising preceded it by two years.
**Why Important:** UPSC often tests pre-1857 vs. post-1857 disturbances.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-092
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Peasant Movement and Tribal Rebellions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1997
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I (Revolt) with List II (Region):
I. Moplah revolt
II. Pabna revolt
III. Eka Movement
IV. Birsa Munda revolt
List II (Region):
A) Kerala
B) Bihar
C) Bengal
D) Awadh
**Options:**
(a) I-A, II-C, III-D, IV-B
(b) I-B, II-C, III-D, IV-A
(c) I-A, II-B, III-C, IV-D
(d) I-C, II-D, III-A, IV-B
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Moplah (Malabar, Kerala). Pabna (East Bengal). Eka Movement (Awadh/Hardoi, UP). Birsa Munda (Ranchi, Bihar/Jharkhand).
**Keywords:** Moplah, Pabna, Eka, Birsa Munda.
**Related Personalities:** Madari Pasi (Eka).
**Memory Trick:** "Mop-Kerala, Pabna-Bengal, Eka-Awadh, Birsa-Bihar."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Eka was in Bengal due to its proximity to peasant movements there.
**Why Important:** Geography-history linkage is a strong UPSC theme.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-093
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Peasant Movement and Tribal Rebellions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Sarabandi (no tax) campaign of 1922 was led by?
**Options:**
(a) Bhagat Singh
(b) Chittaranjan Das
(c) Lala Lajpat Rai
(d) Vallabhbhai Patel
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Vallabhbhai Patel led the "no-tax" or Sarabandi campaign in the Bardoli taluka (Gujarat) in the context of the Non-Cooperation Movement era (though the most famous one was 1928, the 1922 campaign was also under his leadership).
**Keywords:** Sarabandi, No-tax campaign, Vallabhbhai Patel.
**Related Personalities:** Sardar Patel.
**Memory Trick:** "Patel for Peasants (Taxes)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Gandhi (who authorized it but Patel executed it).
**Why Important:** Established Patel as the "Sardar" of the Indian peasantry.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-094
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2015
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Rowlatt Satyagraha, which of the following statements is/are correct?
1. The Rowlatt Act was based on the recommendations of the 'Sedition Committee'.
2. In Rowlatt Satyagraha, Gandhiji tried to utilize the Home Rule League.
3. Demonstrations against the arrival of Simon Commission coincided with Rowlatt Satyagraha.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct: The act was based on Justice Rowlatt's Sedition Committee. Statement 2 is correct: Gandhi utilized Home Rule League networks and Pan-Islamic groups for the Rowlatt Satyagraha. Statement 3 is incorrect: Rowlatt Satyagraha was in 1919; the Simon Commission arrived in 1928.
**Keywords:** Rowlatt Satyagraha, Sedition Committee, Home Rule League.
**Related Dates:** 1919.
**Memory Trick:** "Rowlatt (19) is not Simon (28)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Chronological anachronism (mixing up 1919 and 1928).
**Why Important:** First all-India political movement by Gandhi.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-095
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2014
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The 1929 Session of Indian National Congress is of significance in the history of the Freedom Movement because the?
**Options:**
(a) attainment of Self-Government was declared as the objective of the Congress.
(b) attainment of Poorna Swaraj was adopted as the goal of the Congress.
(c) Non-Cooperation Movement was launched.
(d) decision to participate in the Round Table Conference in London was taken.
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Lahore Session (1929), presided by Jawaharlal Nehru, passed the historic resolution of 'Purna Swaraj' (Complete Independence) and decided to launch the Civil Disobedience Movement.
**Keywords:** Lahore Session 1929, Purna Swaraj, Complete Independence.
**Related Personalities:** Jawaharlal Nehru.
**Memory Trick:** "Lahore 29 = Total Freedom Goal."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing Swaraj (1906 - within empire) with Purna Swaraj (1929 - complete independence).
**Why Important:** Shift from constitutionalism to a final demand for sovereign independence.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-096
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2019
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the British colonial rule in India, consider the following statements:
1. Mahatma Gandhi was instrumental in the abolition of the system of 'indentured labour'.
2. In Lord Chelmsford's 'War Conference', Mahatma Gandhi supported the resolution on recruiting Indians for World War.
3. Consequent upon the breaking of Salt Law by Indian people, the Indian National Congress was declared illegal by the colonial rulers.
Which of the statements given above are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct: Gandhi campaigned heavily against the Girmitiya (indentured) system in South Africa and India, leading to its abolition in 1917. Statement 2 is incorrect: Gandhi attended the 1918 conference but initially had reservations; though he later agreed to recruit, the statement phrasing often triggers debate on "supporting the resolution" (some sources say he did support it in hopes of Swaraj as a reward, but the source suggests he was instrumental in *abolishing* labor systems, while others mark the recruitment support as a complex point). Statement 3 is correct: INC was banned after the Civil Disobedience start. (Note: Correct key is often (b) or (d) depending on nuance of "supporting").
**Keywords:** Indentured labour, War Conference, Salt Law.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Chelmsford.
**Memory Trick:** "Gandhi: No to Slaves (Indentured), Yes to Soldiers (initially/conflicted), No to Salt Tax."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Gandhi was always anti-recruitment; he actually served as a stretcher-bearer and recruited during WWI hoping for British goodwill.
**Why Important:** Complex look at Gandhi's relationship with the Empire.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-097
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1998
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Simon Commission of 1927 was boycotted because?
**Options:**
(a) There was no Indian member in the Commission.
(b) It supported the Muslim League.
(c) Congress felt that the people of India are entitled to Swaraj.
(d) There were differences among the members.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The commission was "all-white," consisting only of British members. This was seen as a violation of the principle of self-determination, as Indians were not considered fit to decide their own constitutional future.
**Keywords:** Simon Commission, Boycott, All-White.
**Related Personalities:** John Simon.
**Memory Trick:** "Simon: See No Indians (No Indian members)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it was boycotted because of its *proposals* (the boycott happened before it even landed/reported).
**Why Important:** United various factions of Indian politics for a brief period.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-098
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following first mooted the idea of a constituent assembly to frame a constitution for India?
**Options:**
(a) Swaraj Party in 1934
(b) Congress Party in 1936
(c) Muslim League in 1942
(d) All Parties Conference in 1946
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Swaraj Party, led by M.N. Roy's ideological influence, first officially mooted the demand for a Constituent Assembly in 1934. The INC officially adopted the demand in 1935.
**Keywords:** Constituent Assembly, Swaraj Party, 1934.
**Related Personalities:** M.N. Roy (individual), Swarajists.
**Memory Trick:** "Swaraj (34) before Congress (36) for Assembly."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting the Cabinet Mission (which *formed* it) instead of who *mooted* the idea.
**Why Important:** Origin of the sovereign body that created the Indian Republic.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-099
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following observations is not true about the Quit India Movement of 1942?
**Options:**
(a) It was a non-violent movement.
(b) It was led by Mahatma Gandhi.
(c) It was a spontaneous movement.
(d) It did not attract the labour class in general.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** While Gandhi called for the movement, it quickly became violent in response to large-scale arrests of leadership. It is often described as the most violent mass uprising since 1857, making (a) the "not true" statement.
**Keywords:** Quit India, 1942, Violence, Do or Die.
**Related Context:** Arrest of Gandhi on Aug 9.
**Memory Trick:** "Quit India = Spontaneous Fire (not purely non-violent)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Gandhi wasn't the leader (he was, though he was in jail) or that workers didn't participate (they did in massive strikes).
**Why Important:** The final mass push for independence.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-100
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following pairs is not correctly matched?
**Options:**
(a) Jamnalal Bajaj — Satyagraha Ashram at Wardha
(b) Dadabhai Naoroji — Bombay Association
(c) Lala Lajpat Rai — National School at Lahore
(d) Bal Gangadhar Tilak — Satya Shodhak Sabha
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Pair (d) is incorrect: The Satya Shodhak Sabha was founded by Jyotiba Phule in 1873, not Tilak. Jamnalal Bajaj was a close associate of Gandhi at Wardha. Naoroji was a key founder of the Bombay Association (1852). Lajpat Rai founded the National School in Lahore during the Non-Cooperation phase.
**Keywords:** Satya Shodhak Sabha, Jyotiba Phule, Jamnalal Bajaj.
**Related Personalities:** Jyotiba Phule.
**Memory Trick:** "Phule found Truth (Satya)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Linking Tilak with all Marathi social movements.
**Why Important:** Distinguishes between upper-caste nationalist leadership and anti-caste social reformers.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-101
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Post-Independence India
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2024
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following pairs:
Party — Its Leader
1. Bharatiya Jana Sangh — Dr. Shyama Prasad Mukherjee
2. Socialist Party — C. Rajagopalachari
3. Congress for Democracy — Jagjivan Ram
4. Swatantra Party — Acharya Narendra Dev
How many of the above are correctly matched?
**Options:**
(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Pair 1 is correct: Bharatiya Jana Sangh was founded by Dr. Shyama Prasad Mukherjee in 1951. Pair 2 is incorrect: The Socialist Party was associated with leaders like Jayaprakash Narayan and Acharya Narendra Dev (C. Rajagopalachari founded the Swatantra Party). Pair 3 is correct: Jagjivan Ram founded the Congress for Democracy in 1977. Pair 4 is incorrect: The Swatantra Party was led by C. Rajagopalachari, while Acharya Narendra Dev was a Socialist leader.
**Keywords:** Jana Sangh, Socialist Party, Swatantra Party, Jagjivan Ram.
**Related Personalities:** C. Rajagopalachari, Narendra Dev.
**Memory Trick:** "Jana-SPM, CFD-Ram, Swatantra-Rajaji."
**Common Exam Trap:** Swapping Socialist and Swatantra leaders.
**Why Important:** Tests knowledge of political pluralism in early independent India.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-102
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following statements does **not** apply to the system of Subsidiary Alliance introduced by Lord Wellesley?
**Options:**
(a) To maintain a large standing army at other's expense
(b) To keep India safe from Napoleonic danger
(c) To secure a fixed income for the Company
(d) To establish British paramountcy over the Indian States
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Subsidiary Alliance aimed to protect the Company from French (Napoleonic) threats (b), maintain a standing army funded by Indian rulers (a), and establish British supremacy (d). It did not aim to secure a "fixed income" for the Company; rather, it was a strategic military-political tool.
**Keywords:** Subsidiary Alliance, Wellesley, Napoleon.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Wellesley.
**Memory Trick:** "Wellesley wanted Soldiers and Safety, not Salaries (fixed income)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Company wanted direct profit from the alliance (it wanted indirect control and troop maintenance).
**Why Important:** Key mechanism of British expansion without direct annexation.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-103
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Post-Independence India
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. In the first Lok Sabha, the single largest party in the opposition was the Swatantra Party.
2. In the Lok Sabha, a “Leader of the Opposition” was recognised for the first time in 1969.
3. In the Lok Sabha, if a party does not have a minimum of 75 members, its leader cannot be recognised as the Leader of the Opposition.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect: The CPI was the largest opposition party in the first Lok Sabha (Swatantra Party was formed later in 1959). Statement 2 is correct: Ram Subhag Singh became the first officially recognized LoP in 1969. Statement 3 is incorrect: The requirement is 10% of the total strength (approx 55 members), not 75.
**Keywords:** First Lok Sabha, Leader of Opposition, 1969.
**Related Personalities:** Ram Subhag Singh.
**Memory Trick:** "LoP needed 1/10th of the House."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the first opposition party with later prominent ones.
**Why Important:** Connects historical parliamentary evolution with contemporary polity rules.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-104
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Indigo cultivation in India declined by the beginning of the 20th century because of:
**Options:**
(a) peasant resistance to the oppressive conduct of planters
(b) its unprofitability in the world market because of new inventions
(c) national leaders' opposition to the cultivation of indigo
(d) Government control over the planters
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The invention of synthetic dyes in Germany made natural indigo uncompetitive and unprofitable in the global market, leading to its decline by the early 20th century.
**Keywords:** Indigo, Synthetic dyes, Germany.
**Related Context:** Champaran Satyagraha (1917).
**Memory Trick:** "Synthetic dyes killed Natural Blue."
**Common Exam Trap:** Attributing it primarily to peasant revolts (which occurred but the *decline* was economic).
**Why Important:** Explains the economic context of the Champaran struggle.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-105
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Wellesley established the Fort William College at Calcutta because:
**Options:**
(a) he was asked by the Board of Directors at London to do so
(b) he wanted to revive interest in oriental learning in India
(c) he wanted to provide some employment to his friends
(d) he wanted to train British civilians for administrative purpose in India
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Lord Wellesley founded Fort William College in 1800 to train young British civil servants in Indian languages and customs to improve administration.
**Keywords:** Fort William College, Training, Civil Servants.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Wellesley.
**Memory Trick:** "Fort William = Foundation for Bureaucrats."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it was for "oriental learning" (like the Asiatic Society) rather than purely administrative training.
**Why Important:** Early institutionalization of civil service training.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-106
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1999
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** There was no independent development of industries in India during British rule because of the:
**Options:**
(a) absence of heavy industries
(b) scarcity of foreign capital
(c) scarcity of natural resources
(d) preference of the rich to invest in land
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** British policy focused on extracting raw materials and selling finished goods. They discouraged the development of heavy/basic industries (like steel or machine tools) in India to keep the colony dependent on the UK.
**Keywords:** Industrial development, Heavy industries, Colonial economy.
**Related Concept:** De-industrialization.
**Memory Trick:** "No Machines = No Industry."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (d) (land investment), which was a *symptom* rather than the primary structural cause.
**Why Important:** Highlights the structural underdevelopment of the Indian economy.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-107
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Swadeshi Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1998
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Assertion (A): The Partition of Bengal in 1905 brought an end to the Moderates’ role in the Indian freedom movement.
Reason (R): The Surat session of the Indian National Congress separated the Moderates from the Extremists.
**Options:**
(a) Both A and R are true, and R is the correct explanation of A
(b) Both A and R are true, but R is NOT a correct explanation of A
(c) A is true, but R is false
(d) A is false, but R is true
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Assertion A is false because the Moderates continued to play a role in the movement (e.g., Morley-Minto reforms, 1916 reunion) even after 1905. Reason R is true; the 1907 Surat session did see the split between the two factions.
**Keywords:** Partition of Bengal, Moderates, Surat Split.
**Related Dates:** 1905 (Partition), 1907 (Split).
**Memory Trick:** "Split happened (R), but Moderates stayed in the game (A is false)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking "End of role" means they vanished immediately.
**Why Important:** Differentiates between a shift in dominance and a total exit.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-108
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1998
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What is the correct sequence of the following events?
I. Tilak’s Home Rule League
II. Kamagatamaru Incident
III. Mahatma Gandhi’s arrival in India
**Options:**
(a) I, II, III
(b) III, II, I
(c) II, III, I
(d) II, I, III
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** 1. Kamagatamaru Incident (May 1914). 2. Gandhi’s arrival from South Africa (January 1915). 3. Tilak founded his Home Rule League (April 1916).
**Keywords:** Chronology, Kamagatamaru, Gandhi arrival, Home Rule.
**Related Dates:** 1914, 1915, 1916.
**Memory Trick:** "Ship (14) -> Saint (15) -> Swaraj (16)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Gandhi arrived after the Home Rule Movement started.
**Why Important:** Essential timeline for the transition into the Gandhian era.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-109
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1998
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Indian Muslims, in general, were not attracted to the Extremist movement because of the:
**Options:**
(a) Influence of Sir Sayyid Ahmed Khan
(b) Anti-Muslim attitude of extremist leaders
(c) Indifference shown to Muslim aspirations
(d) Extremists’ policy of harping on Hindu past
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Extremist leaders like Tilak and Aurobindo often used Hindu symbols (Ganesh festival, Shivaji festival) and religious metaphors (Kali) to mobilize the masses. This alienated many Muslims who viewed the movement as purely Hindu in character.
**Keywords:** Extremists, Hindu Past, Shivaji Festival.
**Related Personalities:** B.G. Tilak.
**Memory Trick:** "Harping on Hindu past hindered unity."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (b) (anti-Muslim attitude), which is too strong; it was the *methodology* rather than a personal attitude.
**Why Important:** Explains the socio-religious limitations of early militant nationalism.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-110
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2017
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian freedom struggle, consider the following events:
1. Mutiny in Royal Indian Navy
2. Quit India Movement launched
3. Second Round Table Conference
What is the correct chronological sequence of the above events?
**Options:**
(a) 1-2-3
(b) 2-1-3
(c) 3-2-1
(d) 3-1-2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** 1. Second Round Table Conference (1931). 2. Quit India Movement (1942). 3. RIN Mutiny (February 1946).
**Keywords:** RTC, Quit India, RIN Mutiny.
**Related Dates:** 1931, 1942, 1946.
**Memory Trick:** "Talk (RTC) -> Fight (Quit India) -> Revolt (RIN)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Placing the RIN Mutiny before Quit India due to its "revolutionary" nature.
**Why Important:** Tracks the final steps towards the British exit.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-111
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2010
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following statements is/are correct regarding the 'Bombay Manifesto' signed in 1936?
1. It openly opposed the preaching of socialist ideals.
2. It was signed by prominent business leaders including Purushottamdas Thakurdas and Walchand Hirachand.
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Bombay Manifesto (1936) was a reaction by 21 prominent Indian businessmen (including Thakurdas and Hirachand) who were alarmed by Nehru's socialist rhetoric at the Lucknow session. It explicitly opposed socialist ideals as harmful to private property and enterprise.
**Keywords:** Bombay Manifesto, Socialism, 1936.
**Related Personalities:** Purushottamdas Thakurdas.
**Memory Trick:** "Businessmen against Bolsheviks (Socialism)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the capitalists always supported the Congress unconditionally.
**Why Important:** Highlights the class conflict within the national movement.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-112
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following pairs is correctly matched?
Movement/Satyagraha — Person actively associated
**Options:**
(a) Champaran — Rajendra Prasad
(b) Ahmedabad Mill Workers — Morarji Desai
(c) Kheda — Vallabhbhai Patel
(d) Vaikom — Periyar
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** (a) is the best match as Rajendra Prasad was a key associate of Gandhi in Champaran. (c) Vallabhbhai Patel was associated with Kheda, but the source lists Champaran/Prasad as a standard pillar match. (Note: Periyar joined Vaikom later, but Prasad-Champaran is the primary NCERT-level association).
**Keywords:** Movement association, Rajendra Prasad.
**Related Context:** Early Gandhian Satyagrahas.
**Memory Trick:** "Prasad in Champaran, Patel in Kheda."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Morarji Desai for Ahmedabad (he was active much later).
**Why Important:** Links leaders to the specific regional struggles where they emerged.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-113
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** At which Congress Session was the Working Committee authorized to launch a programme of Civil Disobedience?
**Options:**
(a) Bombay
(b) Lahore
(c) Lucknow
(d) Tripura
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The 1929 Lahore Session authorized the Congress Working Committee to launch the Civil Disobedience Movement (which began with the Dandi March in 1930).
**Keywords:** Lahore Session 1929, Civil Disobedience, Authorization.
**Related Personalities:** Jawaharlal Nehru.
**Memory Trick:** "Lahore 29 = Launch of CDM."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the 1920 Nagpur session (which authorized Non-Cooperation).
**Why Important:** Turning point from constitutional agitation to mass civil resistance.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-114
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1998
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What is the correct sequence of the following events?
I. August Offer
II. INA Trial
III. Quit India Movement
IV. Royal Indian Navy Mutiny
**Options:**

(b) III, I, II, IV
(c) I, III, IV, II
(d) II, IV, I, III
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** 1. August Offer (August 1940). 2. Quit India Movement (August 1942). 3. INA Trials (November 1945). 4. RIN Mutiny (February 1946).
**Keywords:** August Offer, INA Trial, Quit India, RIN Mutiny.
**Related Dates:** 1940, 1942, 1945, 1946.
**Memory Trick:** "Offer (40) -> Quit (42) -> Trial (45) -> Mutiny (46)."

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-115
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1997
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I with List II and select the correct answer:
List I: I. Surat Split, II. Communal Award, III. All-Party Convention, IV. Poorna Swaraj Resolution
List II: A) 1929, B) 1928, C) 1932, D) 1907
**Options:**
(a) I-D, II-C, III-A, IV-B
(b) I-D, II-C, III-B, IV-A
(c) I-B, II-A, III-C, IV-D
(d) I-A, II-D, III-B, IV-C
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** I-D: Surat Split (1907). II-C: Communal Award (1932). III-B: All-Party Convention (1928, relating to Nehru Report). IV-A: Poorna Swaraj Resolution (1929).
**Keywords:** Surat Split, Communal Award, Nehru Report, Poorna Swaraj.
**Related Personalities:** Ramsay MacDonald (Communal Award).
**Memory Trick:** "Split 07, Report 28, Swaraj 29, Award 32."
**Common Exam Trap:** Mixing up 1928 (Report/Convention) and 1929 (Swaraj).
**Why Important:** Covers the major political milestones of the struggle.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-116
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What is the correct sequence of the following events?
I. The Lucknow Pact
II. The Introduction of Dyarchy
III. The Rowlatt Act
IV. The Partition of Bengal
**Options:**
(a) I, II, III, IV
(b) IV, I, III, II
(c) I, III, II, IV
(d) IV, III, II, I
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** 1. Partition of Bengal (1905). 2. Lucknow Pact (1916). 3. Rowlatt Act (March 1919). 4. Introduction of Dyarchy (via GOI Act 1919, December).
**Keywords:** Bengal Partition, Lucknow Pact, Rowlatt Act, Dyarchy.
**Related Dates:** 1905, 1916, 1919.
**Memory Trick:** "Bengal (05) -> Unity (16) -> Act (19) -> Reform (19 later)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Rowlatt Act came after the Dyarchy reforms were implemented.
**Why Important:** Tracks the path from administrative partition to constitutional reform.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-117
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In 1930 Mahatma Gandhi started Civil Disobedience Movement from:
**Options:**
(a) Sevagram
(b) Dandi
(c) Sabarmati
(d) Wardha
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The movement *started* with the historic march from Sabarmati Ashram on March 12, 1930, and *reached* Dandi on April 6, 1930.
**Keywords:** Civil Disobedience, Sabarmati, Dandi.
**Related Dates:** March 12, 1930.
**Memory Trick:** "Start at Home (Sabarmati), Reach the Sea (Dandi)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Dandi as the *starting* point because it is called the "Dandi March".
**Why Important:** One of the most iconic events in the freedom struggle.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-118
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Revolutionary & Communist Movements

**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I with List II:
I. Chittagong Armoury Raid, II. Abhinav Bharat, III. Anushilan Samiti, IV. Kuka Movement
List II: A) Kalpana Dutt, B) Guru Ram Singh, C) V.D. Savarkar, D) Aurobindo Ghosh
**Options:**
(a) I-A, II-C, III-D, IV-B
(b) I-A, II-C, III-B, IV-D
(c) I-C, II-A, III-B, IV-D
(d) I-C, II-A, III-D, IV-B
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** I-A: Chittagong Raid (Kalpana Dutt was an associate of Surya Sen). II-C: Abhinav Bharat (V.D. Savarkar). III-D: Anushilan Samiti (Aurobindo Ghosh). IV-B: Kuka Movement (Guru Ram Singh).

**Related Personalities:** Surya Sen, Kalpana Dutt.

**Why Important:** Focuses on the role of women and regional revolts in the revolutionary phase.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-120

**Question:** 'Abhinav Bharat' a secret society of revolutionaries was organised by:
**Options:**
(a) Khudiram Bose
(b) V. D. Savarkar
(c) Prafulla Chaki
(d) Bhagat Singh
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** V.D. Savarkar and his brother Ganesh Savarkar organized the Mitra Mela in 1899, which was later renamed Abhinav Bharat in 1904.
**Keywords:** Abhinav Bharat, 1904, Savarkar.
**Related Personalities:** Ganesh Savarkar.
**Memory Trick:** "Savarkar for Secret Society."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Khudiram Bose (who belonged to Anushilan Samiti).
**Why Important:** Essential factual core of the revolutionary movement in Maharashtra.

I. Abhinav Bharat Society, II. Anushilan Samiti, III. Ghadar Party, IV. Swaraj Party
List II: A) Sri Aurobindo Ghosh, B) Lala Hardayal, C) C. R. Das, D) V.D. Savarkar

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-124
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Revolutionary & Communist Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The radical wing of the Congress Party, with Jawaharlal Nehru as one of its main leaders, founded the 'Independence for India League' in opposition to:
**Options:**
(a) the Gandhi Irwin Pact
(b) the Home Rule Movement
(c) the Nehru Report
(d) the Montford Reforms
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Independence for India League (1928) was formed by Jawaharlal Nehru and Subhas Chandra Bose. They were dissatisfied with the Nehru Report (drafted by Motilal Nehru), which demanded 'Dominion Status' instead of their goal of 'Complete Independence'.
**Keywords:** Independence for India League, 1928, Nehru Report.
**Related Personalities:** Subhas Chandra Bose.
**Memory Trick:** "League for Independence against Dominion Status (Report)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking they opposed Gandhi personally; it was a specific policy disagreement over Dominion Status.
**Why Important:** Prelude to the 1929 Purna Swaraj declaration.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-125
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2002
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I (Acts) with List II (Provisions):
A. Indian Council Act 1861, B. GOI Act 1919, C. GOI Act 1935, D. Indian Council Act 1892
List II: 1. Provincial Autonomy, 2. Portfolio System, 3. Dyarchy, 4. Indirect Election
**Options:**
(a) A-2 B-4 C-3 D-1
(b) A-1 B-3 C-4 D-2
(c) A-2 B-3 C-4 D-1
(d) A-1 B-4 C-3 D-2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** A-2: 1861 Act introduced the Portfolio system. B-3: 1919 Act introduced Dyarchy in provinces. C-1: 1935 Act introduced Provincial Autonomy. D-4: 1892 Act first introduced the principle of indirect election.
**Keywords:** Portfolio, Dyarchy, Autonomy, Indirect Election.
**Related Acts:** Indian Councils Acts.
**Memory Trick:** "61-Port, 92-Elect, 19-Dyar, 35-Auto."
**Common Exam Trap:** Swapping Dyarchy (19) and Autonomy (35).
**Why Important:** Core constitutional evolution milestones.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-126
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1997
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Poona Pact which was signed between the British Government and Mahatma Gandhi in 1932 provided for:
**Options:**
(a) the creation of dominion status for India
(b) separate electorates for the Muslims
(c) separate electorate for the Harijans
(d) joint electorate with reservation for Harijans
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Poona Pact (September 1932) was an agreement between B.R. Ambedkar and Mahatma Gandhi. It abandoned the idea of separate electorates for the depressed classes (Harijans) that had been granted by the Communal Award. Instead, it provided for reserved seats for them within the joint electorate of the general population.
**Keywords:** Poona Pact, Joint Electorate, Reservation.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** B.R. Ambedkar, Ramsay MacDonald.
**Memory Trick:** "Pact for Joint Presence (Joint Electorate)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Poona Pact was between the British and Gandhi; it was primarily between Gandhi and Ambedkar (though the British government accepted it).
**Why Important:** Prevented a permanent political split within the Hindu community.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-127
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2013
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian History, the Members of the Constituent Assembly from the Provinces were:
**Options:**
(a) directly elected by the people of those Provinces
(b) nominated by the Indian National Congress and the Muslim League
(c) elected by the Provincial Legislative Assemblies
(d) selected by the Government for their expertise in constitutional matters
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The members of the Constituent Assembly were not directly elected by the people on the basis of universal adult franchise. Instead, they were elected indirectly by the members of the Provincial Legislative Assemblies, who themselves had been elected on a limited franchise under the GOI Act 1935.
**Keywords:** Constituent Assembly, Indirect Election, Provinces.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Cabinet Mission Plan 1946.
**Memory Trick:** "Assembly by Assemblies (Provincial)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting "directly elected," which was the demand of the Congress but not the actual method used.
**Why Important:** Explains the representative nature (and limitations) of the body that drafted the Constitution.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-128
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2008
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following suggested the reconstitution of the Viceroy’s Executive Council in which all the portfolios including that of War Members were to be held by the Indian leaders?
**Options:**
(a) Simon Commission
(b) Simla Conference
(c) Cripps Proposal
(d) Cabinet Mission
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Simla Conference (1945), based on the Wavell Plan, proposed a reconstitution of the Viceroy’s Executive Council. It suggested that all members of the council, except the Governor-General and the Commander-in-Chief, would be Indians, including the portfolio for External Affairs.
**Keywords:** Simla Conference, Wavell Plan, Portfolios.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Lord Wavell.
**Memory Trick:** "Wavell's War-leaders (Indians in Council)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Cabinet Mission, which proposed a long-term constitutional structure rather than just council reconstitution.
**Why Important:** It was the first formal British offer of a fully "Indianized" executive council.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-129
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2002
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The last opportunity to avoid the partition of India was lost with the rejection of:
**Options:**
(a) Cripps Mission
(b) Rajagopalachari Formula
(c) Cabinet Mission
(d) Wavell Plan
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Cabinet Mission (1946) proposed a federal structure for a united India with three groups of provinces (A, B, and C). The failure of the Congress and the Muslim League to agree on the interpretation of the grouping scheme led to the ultimate collapse of the plan and the inevitability of Partition.
**Keywords:** Cabinet Mission, Partition, Grouping Scheme.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Pethick-Lawrence, Stafford Cripps, A.V. Alexander.
**Memory Trick:** "Cabinet was the Last Call for Unity."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting the Cripps Mission (1942), which was an earlier attempt but the Cabinet Mission was the final definitive chance.
**Why Important:** Turning point leading directly to the Direct Action Day and Partition.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-130
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Montagu-Chelmsford Report formed the basis of:
**Options:**
(a) The Indian Councils Act, 1909
(b) The Government of India Act, 1919
(c) The Government of India Act, 1935
(d) The Indian Independence Act, 1947
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The 1918 Montagu-Chelmsford Report on constitutional reforms led directly to the enactment of the Government of India Act 1919, which introduced "Dyarchy" in the provinces.
**Keywords:** Montagu-Chelmsford, GOI Act 1919, Basis.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Edwin Montagu, Lord Chelmsford.
**Memory Trick:** "Mont-Ford = 1919 (Ford car era)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Morley-Minto reforms (1909).
**Why Important:** Landmark in the devolution of power to Indians.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-131
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Miscellaneous (Culture/History Linkage)
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following pairs is/are correctly matched?
**Tradition — State**
1. Chapchar Kut festival — Mizoram
2. Khongjom Parva ballad — Manipur
3. Thang-ta dance — Sikkim
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Pair 1 is correct: Chapchar Kut is a spring festival of Mizoram. Pair 2 is correct: Khongjom Parva is a traditional musical narrative (ballad) from Manipur. Pair 3 is incorrect: Thang-ta is a traditional martial art/dance from Manipur, not Sikkim.
**Keywords:** Chapchar Kut, Khongjom Parva, Thang-ta.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Northeast Traditions.
**Memory Trick:** "Thang-ta is from Manipur (Manipuri martial art)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Sikkim is often used as a distractor for Northeast cultural questions.
**Why Important:** Modern History and Art & Culture often overlap in Prelims.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-132
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the interim government formed in 1946, the Vice-President of the Executive Council was:
**Options:**
(a) Jawaharlal Nehru
(b) Dr. S. Radhakrishnan
(c) C. Rajagopalachari
(d) Dr. Rajendra Prasad
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** In the Interim Government formed in September 1946, the Viceroy remained the President of the Executive Council, while Jawaharlal Nehru was appointed as the Vice-President, effectively functioning as the Prime Minister.
**Keywords:** Interim Government, 1946, Vice-President.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Lord Wavell.
**Memory Trick:** "VP was the PM-in-waiting (Nehru)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting the President of the Council (who was the Viceroy).
**Why Important:** Marked the formal transfer of executive administration to Indian hands.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-133
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1998
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Indian National Congress agreed in 1947 to the partition of the country mainly because:
**Options:**
(a) the principle of two-nation theory was then acceptable to them
(b) it was imposed by the British Government and the Congress was helpless
(c) they wanted to avoid large-scale communal riots
(d) India would have otherwise lost the opportunity to attain freedom
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** By 1947, the spread of communal violence (following Direct Action Day) convinced many Congress leaders, including Nehru and Patel, that partition was a lesser evil than a civil war or a weak, chaotic central government.
**Keywords:** Partition, Communal Riots, Agreement.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Mountbatten Plan.
**Memory Trick:** "Peace over Partition (Avoid Riots)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Congress accepted the "Two-Nation Theory"; they accepted the *fact* of partition but never the *ideology* of it.
**Why Important:** Explains the pragmatic (and painful) shift in nationalist strategy.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-134
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Personality Based Questions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2021
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Madanapalle of Andhra Pradesh, which one of the following statements is correct?
**Options:**
(a) Pingali Venkayya designed the tricolour Indian National Flag here.
(b) Pattabhi Sitaramayya led the Quit India Movement of Andhra region from here.
(c) Rabindranath Tagore translated the National Anthem from Bengali to English here.
(d) Madame Blavatsky and Colonel Olcott set up headquarters of Theosophical Society first here.
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** In 1919, Rabindranath Tagore visited Besant Theosophical College in Madanapalle. It was here that he translated his Bengali song "Jana Gana Mana" into English as "The Morning Song of India."
**Keywords:** Madanapalle, Rabindranath Tagore, National Anthem.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** National Anthem.
**Memory Trick:** "Madanapalle = Morning Song."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Pingali Venkayya, who is from Andhra but associated with the flag design at the Bezwada (Vijayawada) session.
**Why Important:** Obscure but significant historical linkage often tested by UPSC.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-135
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** At the time of partition of India, which one of the following provinces of the British India came forward with a plan for a united and independent existence?
**Options:**
(a) Punjab
(b) Assam
(c) Bengal
(d) Bihar
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** H.S. Suhrawardy (Premier of Bengal) and Sarat Chandra Bose (brother of Subhas Bose) proposed a plan for a "United Independent Bengal" to avoid partition, but it was rejected by both the Congress (fear of communal majority) and the Muslim League (Jinnah's demand for Pakistan).
**Keywords:** United Bengal, Independent existence, Suhrawardy.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Sarat Chandra Bose.
**Memory Trick:** "Sarat's Sovereign Bengal."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Punjab, which was also partitioned but lacked a formal "independent third state" plan as prominent as Bengal's.
**Why Important:** Highlights the local attempts to bypass the binary partition of India and Pakistan.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-136
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Key Personalities & Ideologies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1997
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** “A graduate at 18, professor at 20, Secretary of the National Congress at 29, President of the Indian National Congress at 39 ……… a patriot whom Mahatma Gandhi himself regarded as his master.” This describes:
**Options:**
(a) Pandit Madan Mohan Malaviya
(b) Mahadev Govind Ranade
(c) Gopal Krishna Gokhale
(d) Bal Gangadhar Tilak
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Gopal Krishna Gokhale (1866–1915) was a moderate leader, founder of the Servants of India Society, and the political mentor (Guru) of Mahatma Gandhi.
**Keywords:** Gopal Krishna Gokhale, Gandhi's Master, Servants of India.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** B.G. Tilak (political rival).
**Memory Trick:** "Gokhale = Gandhi's Guru."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Ranade, who was Gokhale's mentor, but the quote specifically mentions Gokhale being Gandhi's master.
**Why Important:** Pillar of the moderate phase of the INC.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-137
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Key Personalities & Ideologies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match the following authors and books:
I. Surendranath Bannerjee — A) Hind Swaraj
II. M. K. Gandhi — B) The Indian Struggle
III. Subhash Chandra Bose — C) Autobiographical Writings
IV. Lajpat Rai — D) A Nation in Making
**Options:**
(a) I–D, II–A, III–C, IV–B
(b) I–A, II–D, III–C, IV–B
(c) I–A, II–D, III–B, IV–C
(d) I–D, II–A, III–B, IV–C
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Correct matches: Surendranath Bannerjee wrote *A Nation in Making* (D). Gandhi wrote *Hind Swaraj* (A). Subhash Bose wrote *The Indian Struggle* (B). Lala Lajpat Rai wrote *Autobiographical Writings* (C).
**Keywords:** Authors, Books, Nationalist Literature.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Surendranath Bannerjee, Lajpat Rai.
**Memory Trick:** "Gandhi-Hind, Bose-Struggle, Bannerjee-Nation."
**Common Exam Trap:** Swapping Bose's *Struggle* with Bannerjee's *Nation*.
**Why Important:** Literary contributions were key to building national consciousness.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-138
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Key Personalities & Ideologies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements about Jawaharlal Nehru:
I. He was the President of the Congress Party in 1947.
II. He presided over the Constituent Assembly.
III. He formed the first Congress Ministry in United Province before India's independence.
Of these statements:
**Options:**
(a) I, II and III are correct
(b) I and III are correct
(c) I and II are correct
(d) None is correct
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement I is false; J.B. Kripalani was the INC President in 1947. Statement II is false; Dr. Rajendra Prasad was the President of the Constituent Assembly. Statement III is false; Govind Ballabh Pant headed the first Congress Ministry in UP (1937).
**Keywords:** Jawaharlal Nehru, INC President, Constituent Assembly.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** J.B. Kripalani, Rajendra Prasad.
**Memory Trick:** "Nehru was PM, not the Assembly or Party head in '47."
**Common Exam Trap:** Assuming that since Nehru was the leader of the country, he must have held these specific organizational roles simultaneously.
**Why Important:** Tests factual precision regarding the roles of top leaders during the transfer of power.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-139
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Peasant, Tribal & Labour Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2002
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Assertion (A): The effect of labour participation in the Indian nationalist upsurge of the early 1930s was weak.
Reason (R): The labour leaders considered the ideology of the Indian National Congress as bourgeois and reactionary.
**Options:**
(a) Both A and R are individually true and R is the correct explanation of A
(b) Both A and R are individually true but R is not a correct explanation of A
(c) A is true but R is false
(d) A is false but R is true
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** During the Civil Disobedience Movement (1930s), many communist-influenced labour leaders distanced themselves from the Congress, viewing it as a representative of the capitalist class. This ideological rift resulted in limited labour participation compared to the Non-Cooperation era.
**Keywords:** Labour Movement, 1930s, Bourgeois, NCM.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** CPI, INC.
**Memory Trick:** "Leftists left the Congress (in the 30s)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking labour was always the core of mass movements; they were often aligned but split during specific ideological shifts in the 1920s-30s.
**Why Important:** Explains the limitations of the mass base of the 1930s upsurge.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-140
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Non-Cooperation Movement led to:
I. Congress becoming a mass movement for the first time.
II. Growth of Hindu-Muslim unity.
III. Removal of fear of the British might from the minds of the people.
IV. British government’s willingness to grant political concessions to Indians.
Select the correct answer:
**Options:**
(a) I, II and III
(b) II and III
(c) I and III
(d) III and IV
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The NCM (1920-22) successfully transformed the Congress into a mass organization (I), achieved peak Hindu-Muslim unity via Khilafat integration (II), and boosted national confidence (III). However, the British did not immediately offer significant concessions *because* of NCM; rather, they used repression.
**Keywords:** NCM, Mass Movement, Unity.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Chauri Chaura withdrawal.
**Memory Trick:** "Masses, Muslims, and Minds (Fear gone)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Including IV; concessions usually came after long stalemates or wars (like GOI 1935 or August Offer), not as a direct surrender to NCM.
**Why Important:** First true "Mass Phase" of the freedom struggle.
**Sources:**.
