**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-141
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1999
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The First Anglo-Maratha War ended with the treaty of:
**Options:**
(a) Salbai
(b) Surat
(c) Purandar
(d) Bassein
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The First Anglo-Maratha War (1775–1782) ended with the Treaty of Salbai, which established 20 years of peace between the British and the Marathas and restored status quo.
**Keywords:** Treaty of Salbai, 1782, First Anglo-Maratha War.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Warren Hastings, Mahadji Shinde.
**Memory Trick:** "Salbai saved the Marathas (for a while)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Treaty of Bassein (1802), which ended the second war phase/Subisidiary Alliance.
**Why Important:** Crucial pause that allowed the British to focus on Mysore and the French.
**Sources:**.

**Why Important:** Foundations of modern infrastructure and industrial exploitation.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-143

**Question Category:** Peasant, Tribal & Labour Movements

**Question:** Who among the following were the leaders of the Indigo Revolt of 1859-60?
**Options:**
(a) Digambar Biswas and Bishnu Biswas
(b) Budhu Bhagat
(c) Sidhu and Kanhu
(d) Birsa Munda
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Indigo Revolt (Neel Bidroho) in Bengal was led by two former employees of planters, Digambar Biswas and Bishnu Biswas, in the Nadia district.
**Keywords:** Indigo Revolt, Biswas Brothers, 1859.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Dinabandhu Mitra (*Neeldarpan*).
**Memory Trick:** "Biswas for Blue (Indigo)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Sidhu and Kanhu (Santhal Rebellion) or Birsa Munda (Ulgulan).
**Why Important:** One of the most successful peasant movements in colonial history.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-144
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following is/are the principal feature(s) of the Government of India Act, 1919?
1. Introduction of dyarchy in the executive government of the provinces.
2. Introduction of separate communal electorates for Muslims.
3. Devolution of legislative authority by the centre to the provinces.
Select the correct answer:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Features of 1919 Act: Introduced provincial dyarchy (1) and devolved powers via the classification of central and provincial subjects (3). However, statement 2 is incorrect because separate electorates for Muslims were introduced by the 1909 Act; the 1919 Act *extended* them to Sikhs, Europeans, and Anglo-Indians.
**Keywords:** GOI Act 1919, Dyarchy, Devolution.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms.
**Memory Trick:** "1919 = Dyarchy + Devolution."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking communal electorates started in 1919 (they started in 1909).
**Why Important:** Structural framework of provincial administration.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-145
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Congress ministries resigned in the seven provinces in 1939, because:
**Options:**
(a) the Congress could not form ministries in the other four provinces
(b) emergence of a ‘left wing’ in the Congress made the working of the ministries impossible
(c) there was widespread communal disturbance in the provinces
(d) None of the statements (a), (b) and (c) given above is correct
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** None of the reasons (a), (b), or (c) are the primary cause. The real reason was the unilateral decision of the British Government to involve India in World War II without consulting the Indian people or the provincial ministries.
**Keywords:** Resignation 1939, WWII, Ministries.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Lord Linlithgow.
**Memory Trick:** "War without Words (Consultation) = Resignation."
**Common Exam Trap:** Attributing it to internal Congress rifts or riots.
**Why Important:** Ended the brief experiment of constitutional self-rule (1937-39).
**Sources:**.

**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Keywords:** Ambedkar, SCF, ILP.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** B.R. Ambedkar.
**Memory Trick:** "Ambedkar = Labour and SC Federation."
**Common Exam Trap:** Including the Peasants and Workers Party due to its similar-sounding class focus.
**Why Important:** Essential for understanding the political organization of the depressed classes.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-147

**Year:** 1999
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The song 'Amar Sonar Bangla' written during the Swadeshi Movement of India inspired the liberation struggle of Bangladesh and was adopted as the National Anthem of Bangladesh. Who wrote this song?

(a) Bankim Chandra Chattopadhyay
(b) Rabindranath Tagore
(c) Qazi Nazrul Islam
(d) Sarat Chandra Chattopadhyay

**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with *Vande Mataram* (Bankim Chandra).
**Why Important:** Reflects the cross-border cultural impact of the Swadeshi Movement.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-148

**Question Category:** Key Personalities & Ideologies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following matches is NOT correct?
**Options:**
(a) Dr. S. Radhakrishnan — President of India

(c) Maulana Abul Kalam Azad — Education Minister
(d) Dr. B.R. Ambedkar — Chief Justice of India
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** (d) is incorrect. Dr. B.R. Ambedkar was India's first Law Minister and Chairman of the Drafting Committee, not the Chief Justice. H.J. Kania was the first CJI of independent India.

**Related Acts / Personalities:** B.R. Ambedkar.
**Memory Trick:** "Ambedkar = Law (Minister), not Judge (CJI)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking he was the CJI because of his deep legal knowledge.
**Why Important:** Basic factual identification of the first Cabinet roles.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-150
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The first Indian Governor-General of independent India was:
**Options:**
(a) C. Rajagopalachari
(b) Dr. Rajendra Prasad
(c) Lord Mountbatten
(d) B.R. Ambedkar
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** While Lord Mountbatten was the first Governor-General of independent India, C. Rajagopalachari (Rajaji) was the first *Indian* to hold that office, succeeding Mountbatten in 1948.
**Keywords:** Governor-General, Rajagopalachari, Independent India.
**Related Acts / Personalities:** Lord Mountbatten.
**Memory Trick:** "Rajaji was the only Indian GG."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing "First Governor-General" (Mountbatten) with "First *Indian* Governor-General" (Rajaji).
**Why Important:** Significant symbolic end to colonial administrative titles.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-151
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2015
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was/were economic critic/critics of colonialism in India?
1. Dadabhai Naoroji
2. G. Subramania Iyer
3. R.C. Dutt
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** All three were prominent early nationalist leaders who analysed and criticised the economic impact of British rule. Dadabhai Naoroji pioneered the "Drain of Wealth" theory. G. Subramania Iyer (founder of *The Hindu*) and R.C. Dutt (author of *Economic History of India*) provided detailed statistical and historical accounts of how British policies impoverished the Indian peasantry and destroyed local industries.
**Keywords:** Economic Critics, Drain of Wealth, R.C. Dutt.
**Related Personalities:** M.G. Ranade, G.V. Joshi, Prithwishchandra Ray.
**Memory Trick:** "N-I-D (Naoroji, Iyer, Dutt) - Not Investing (in) Development."
**Common Exam Trap:** Limiting the "economic critic" label to only Dadabhai Naoroji.
**Why Important:** This critique was the intellectual foundation for the demand for Swaraj.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-152
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The tendency for increased litigation in India after the introduction of the land settlement system by Lord Cornwallis is usually ascribed to which of the following provisions?
**Options:**
(a) Making Zamindar's position stronger vis-a-vis the ryot
(b) Making East India Company an overlord of Zamindars
(c) Making judicial system more efficient
(d) None of the (a), (b) and (c) above
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The surge in litigation after the Permanent Settlement (1793) was primarily due to the abolition of the Court Fee and the separation of executive and judicial functions (Cornwallis Code), which made courts accessible. However, the most technical reason (often cited in NCERT/Spectrum) was the removal of the *Collector's* judicial powers and the rigid "Sunset Law," which led to frequent land transfers and disputes. None of the options (a), (b), or (c) accurately describe the *primary* cause of the litigation explosion.
**Keywords:** Litigation, Cornwallis, Land Settlement, Court Fee.
**Related Acts:** Cornwallis Code 1793.
**Memory Trick:** "Litigation rose because the system got Law-heavy but Land-rigid."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (c) assuming efficiency always leads to more cases (it was accessibility/procedural changes).
**Why Important:** Tests micro-consequences of administrative "reforms" on social behavior.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-153
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the period of colonial rule in India, "Home Charges" formed an important part of drain of wealth from India. Which of the following funds constituted Home Charges?
1. Funds used to support the India Office in London.
2. Funds used to pay salaries and pensions of British personnel engaged in India.
3. Funds used for waging wars outside India by the British.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Home Charges were payments made in England by the East India Company/Crown from Indian revenues. They included the maintenance of the India Office (1), salaries and pensions of British civil and military officers (2), and interest on public debt. While wars were funded by Indian money, "Home Charges" specifically referred to the administrative overhead in London. Statement 3 (waging wars) is often considered part of the *general* drain of wealth but is debated as a technical constituent of "Home Charges" in some standard texts (UPSC 2011 official key accepted 1 and 2).
**Keywords:** Home Charges, Drain of Wealth, India Office.
**Related Personalities:** Dadabhai Naoroji.
**Memory Trick:** "Home Charges = Paying for the Boss's Home (London Office/Pensions)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Including every form of expenditure as "Home Charges" (it was specifically administrative costs in London).
**Why Important:** Core concept of the economic critique of the Raj.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-154
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the period of Indian freedom struggle, which of the following was/were recommended by the 'Nehru Report' (1928)?
1. Complete Independence for India.
2. Joint electorates for reservation of seats for minorities.
3. Provision of Fundamental Rights for the people of India in the Constitution.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Nehru Report (1928) demanded **Dominion Status**, not Complete Independence (making statement 1 incorrect). It recommended joint electorates with reservation for Muslims only where they were in a minority (2) and a bill of rights (3).
**Keywords:** Nehru Report, Dominion Status, Joint Electorate.
**Related Personalities:** Motilal Nehru (Chairman), Jawaharlal Nehru (Secretary).
**Memory Trick:** "Nehru Report = No to Separate Electorates, Yes to Rights."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Nehru Report demanded Purna Swaraj (it was the 1929 Lahore session that did).
**Why Important:** First major attempt by Indians to draft a comprehensive constitution.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-155
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Ilbert Bill controversy was a landmark in the history of the Indian National Movement because it related to the:
**Options:**
(a) imposition of certain restrictions on the Indians carrying arms.
(b) imposition of restrictions on Indian language newspapers and magazines.
(c) removal of racial disqualifications with the regard to the judicial education.
(d) None of the above.
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Ilbert Bill (1883) introduced by Lord Ripon sought to allow Indian judges to try Europeans in criminal cases, thereby removing racial discrimination in the judiciary. The fierce opposition by the British community in India (the "White Mutiny") revealed their deep-seated racism and spurred Indian nationalists to organize.
**Keywords:** Ilbert Bill, Lord Ripon, Racial discrimination.
**Related Context:** Pre-Congress associations.
**Memory Trick:** "Ilbert = Impartial Judiciary (attempted)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Vernacular Press Act (which Ripon repealed, but it wasn't the Ilbert Bill).
**Why Important:** Catalyst for the formation of the INC in 1885.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-156
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Personality Based Questions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2010
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following was a journal brought out by Abul Kalam Azad?
**Options:**
(a) Al-Hilal
(b) Comrade
(c) The Indian Sociologist
(d) Zamindar
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Maulana Abul Kalam Azad started the Urdu weekly *Al-Hilal* in 1912 to spread revolutionary ideas and promote Hindu-Muslim unity. *Comrade* was by Mohammad Ali, *Indian Sociologist* by Shyamji Krishna Varma, and *Zamindar* by Zafar Ali Khan.
**Keywords:** Al-Hilal, Abul Kalam Azad, Urdu Journalism.
**Related Personalities:** Maulana Azad.
**Memory Trick:** "Azad's Al-Hilal (A-A)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Swapping the journals of Khilafat-era leaders like Azad and the Ali brothers.
**Why Important:** Azad's role as a bridge between religious learning and secular nationalism.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-157
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Mahatma Gandhi said that some of his deepest convictions were reflected in a book titled, 'Unto this Last', and the book transformed his life. What was the message from the book that transformed Mahatma Gandhi?
**Options:**
(a) Uplifting the oppressed and poor is the moral duty of an educated man.
(b) The good of the individual is contained in the good of all.
(c) The life of celibacy and spiritual pursuit are essential for a noble life.
(d) All the statements (a), (b) and (c) are correct in this context.
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** John Ruskin's *Unto this Last* taught Gandhi the concept of 'Sarvodaya' (the welfare of all). He summarized its lessons as: (1) The good of the individual is contained in the good of all; (2) A lawyer's work has the same value as the barber's; (3) A life of labour is a life worth living.
**Keywords:** Unto this Last, John Ruskin, Sarvodaya.
**Related Books:** *Hind Swaraj*, *The Kingdom of God is Within You*.
**Memory Trick:** "Sarvodaya = Same value for all + Good of all."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting "Uplifting poor" (a) as the *deepest* conviction, though statement (b) captures the philosophical essence Gandhi adopted.
**Why Important:** These ideas led to the establishment of the Phoenix Settlement and Tolstoy Farm.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-158
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2009
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following wrote the book 'Bahuvivah'?
**Options:**
(a) Raja Ram Mohan Roy
(b) Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar
(c) Pandita Ramabai
(d) Rabindranath Tagore
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar, a fierce opponent of child marriage and polygamy, wrote the book *Bahuvivah* (Polygamy) to highlight the social evils associated with the practice among Kulin Brahmins in Bengal.
**Keywords:** Bahuvivah, Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar, Kulinism.
**Related Context:** Widow Remarriage Act 1856.
**Memory Trick:** "Vidyasagar = Versatile (Widows + Bahuvivah/Polygamy)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with Raja Ram Mohan Roy's works on Sati.
**Why Important:** One of the earliest sociological critiques of domestic social structures in India.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-159
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What was the reason for Mahatma Gandhi to organize a Satyagraha on behalf of the peasants of Kheda?
1. The Administration did not suspend the land revenue collection in spite of a bad harvest.
2. The Administration proposed to introduce Permanent Settlement in Gujarat.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Kheda Satyagraha (1918) was triggered because the authorities refused to grant revenue remission despite a total crop failure (1). Statement 2 is incorrect as the Permanent Settlement was specific to Bengal/Bihar; Gujarat was under the Ryotwari system.
**Keywords:** Kheda Satyagraha, Revenue remission, Bad harvest.
**Related Personalities:** Vallabhbhai Patel, Indulal Yagnik.
**Memory Trick:** "Kheda = Khali (Empty) pockets due to harvest failure."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Permanent Settlement was a pan-India system.
**Why Important:** Gandhi's first real peasant struggle involving a no-tax campaign.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-160
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2008
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What was the purpose with which Sir William Wedderburn and W.S. Caine had set up the Indian Parliamentary Committee in 1893?
**Options:**
(a) To agitate for Indian political reforms in the House of Commons.
(b) To campaign for the entry of Indians into the Imperial Judiciary.
(c) To facilitate a discussion on India's Independence in the British Parliament.
(d) To agitate for the entry of eminent Indians into the British Parliament.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Sir William Wedderburn (an ex-ICS officer and INC President) and W.S. Caine established the committee in London to lobby British MPs and create a pressure group within the House of Commons to support political and administrative reforms for India.
**Keywords:** William Wedderburn, Indian Parliamentary Committee, House of Commons.
**Related Personalities:** Dadabhai Naoroji (who was an MP then).
**Memory Trick:** "Wedderburn wanted the House (Commons) to hear India."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the committee was for "Independence" (which wasn't the goal in 1893).
**Why Important:** Represents the international lobbying phase of the Moderates.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-161
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2008
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was the founder of the 'Servants of India Society'?
**Options:**
(a) Bal Gangadhar Tilak
(b) Dadabhai Naoroji
(c) Gopal Krishna Gokhale
(d) Lala Lajpat Rai
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Gopal Krishna Gokhale founded the Servants of India Society in 1905 in Pune to train Indians to devote their lives to the cause of the country and to promote social and educational welfare.
**Keywords:** Servants of India Society, Gokhale, 1905.
**Related Personalities:** M.G. Ranade (mentor).
**Memory Trick:** "Gokhale was the Guide (founder) for Servants."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Lala Lajpat Rai, who founded the similar-sounding 'Servants of the People Society' in 1921.
**Why Important:** Premier non-political organization for nationalist selfless service.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-162
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the period of Indian freedom struggle, consider the following statements:
1. The Civil Disobedience Movement in Peshawar was led by Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan.
2. In Sholapur, industrial workers led a violent movement against British rule during the Civil Disobedience phase.
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Both are correct. Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan (Frontier Gandhi) led the Red Shirts in Peshawar (1). In Sholapur (Maharashtra), the arrest of Gandhi led to a fierce uprising by textile workers who established a parallel government for a few days (2).
**Keywords:** Peshawar, Sholapur, Civil Disobedience, Red Shirts.
**Related Context:** Salt Satyagraha extensions.
**Memory Trick:** "Peshawar-Pathan (Ghaffar), Sholapur-Steel/Industrial Workers."
**Common Exam Trap:** Believing all CDM activities were purely non-violent (Sholapur saw significant violence).
**Why Important:** Shows the regional intensity and diverse class participation in 1930.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-163
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** The Revolt of 1857
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the Revolt of 1857, which of the following pairs is/are correctly matched?
Leader — Centre of Revolt
1. Delhi — Bakht Khan
2. Kanpur — Nana Sahib
3. Lucknow — Begum Hazrat Mahal
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** All are correctly matched. General Bakht Khan led the troops in Delhi (representing Bahadur Shah II). Nana Sahib (assisted by Tantia Tope) led at Kanpur. Begum Hazrat Mahal led the resistance at Lucknow.
**Keywords:** centres of 1857, Bakht Khan, Begum Hazrat Mahal.
**Related Personalities:** Kunwar Singh (Bihar), Rani Laxmibai (Jhansi).
**Memory Trick:** "B-D (Bakht-Delhi), N-K (Nana-Kanpur), H-L (Hazrat-Lucknow)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Bahadur Shah II was the *military* leader in Delhi (it was Bakht Khan).
**Why Important:** Basic factual geography of the 1857 uprising.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-164
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Swadeshi Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2009
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** During the Indian freedom struggle, the 'Bande Mataram' became the theme song of which movement?
**Options:**
(a) Non-Cooperation Movement
(b) Civil Disobedience Movement
(c) Swadeshi Movement
(d) Quit India Movement
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** During the 1905 anti-partition (Swadeshi) movement in Bengal, 'Bande Mataram' became the primary rallying cry. People marched through streets singing it, making it the unofficial anthem of Indian nationalism.
**Keywords:** Bande Mataram, Swadeshi Movement, 1905.
**Related Personalities:** Bankim Chandra Chattopadhyay (Author).
**Memory Trick:** "Bande Mataram = Boycott (Swadeshi)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Associating it primarily with later movements since it remained popular throughout.
**Why Important:** It was the first time a song was used as a mass political weapon.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-165
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Key Personalities & Ideologies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was **NOT** associated with the Sarvodaya movement?
**Options:**
(a) Jayaprakash Narayan
(b) Vinoba Bhave
(c) Achyut Patwardhan
(d) Dada Dharmadhikari
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Vinoba Bhave was the founder of the Sarvodaya Samaj and Bhoodan movement. Jayaprakash Narayan and Dada Dharmadhikari were key leaders of the Gandhian Sarvodaya philosophy. Achyut Patwardhan was a socialist leader (CSP) famous for his underground activities in 1942 but not primarily identified with the Sarvodaya movement.
**Keywords:** Sarvodaya, Vinoba Bhave, JP Narayan.
**Related Concepts:** Bhoodan, Gramdan.
**Memory Trick:** "Achyut = Action (Quit India), not (purely) Sarvodaya."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking all Gandhians/Socialists were part of the Sarvodaya fold.
**Why Important:** Post-independence application of Gandhian principles.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-166
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2007
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Tattvabodhini Sabha was founded by?
**Options:**
(a) Raja Ram Mohan Roy
(b) Debendranath Tagore
(c) Keshab Chandra Sen
(d) Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Debendranath Tagore founded the Tattvabodhini Sabha in 1839 to propagate Raja Ram Mohan Roy’s ideas and to promote a rational inquiry into India’s past. It later merged with the Brahmo Samaj.
**Keywords:** Tattvabodhini Sabha, 1839, Debendranath Tagore.
**Related Personalities:** Akshay Kumar Dutt (Editor).
**Memory Trick:** "Tagore (Senior) for Truth (Tattva)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Raja Ram Mohan Roy (who founded the Brahmo Sabha, but Tattvabodhini was started by his successor).
**Why Important:** Essential link in the continuity of the 19th-century Renaissance.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-167
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2015
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Government of India Act of 1919 clearly defined:
**Options:**
(a) the separation of power between the judiciary and the legislature
(b) the jurisdiction of the central and provincial governments
(c) the powers of the Secretary of State for India and the Viceroy
(d) None of the above
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The 1919 Act (Mont-Ford Reforms) first introduced a clear demarcation and separation of central and provincial subjects. It further divided provincial subjects into "Transferred" and "Reserved" (Dyarchy).
**Keywords:** GOI Act 1919, Jurisdiction, Central vs Provincial.
**Related Concepts:** Dyarchy, Devolution.
**Memory Trick:** "1919 = Two tiers of subjects (Demarcation)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it defined "Separation of Powers" in the modern sense (legislature vs judiciary).
**Why Important:** Structural origin of Indian federalism.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-168
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following statements correctly explains the impact of Industrial Revolution on India in the first half of the nineteenth century?
**Options:**
(a) Indian handicrafts were ruined.
(b) Machines were introduced in the Indian textile industry in large numbers.
(c) Railway lines were laid in many parts of the country.
(d) Heavy duties were imposed on the imports of British manufactures.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** In the first half of the 19th century (up to 1850), the primary impact was the "De-industrialization" of India. British machine-made cloth flooded the Indian market duty-free, while heavy duties were placed on Indian exports, leading to the ruin of traditional handicrafts (a). Introduction of machines (b) and Railways (c) happened primarily in the *second* half of the 19th century.
**Keywords:** Industrial Revolution, Ruin of handicrafts, De-industrialization.
**Related Concepts:** One-way Free Trade.
**Memory Trick:** "1st Half = Destruction; 2nd Half = (Colonial) Construction."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (c) - Railways started in 1853 (technically 2nd half).
**Why Important:** Central to the economic critique of colonial rule.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-169
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2019
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following groups of plants was domesticated in the 'New World' and introduced into the 'Old World'?
**Options:**
(a) Tobacco, cocoa and rubber
(b) Cotton, wheat and rice
(c) Wheat, coffee and sugarcane
(d) Rubber, coffee and wheat
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** This historical-geographical question refers to the "Columbian Exchange." Tobacco, cocoa (chocolate), and rubber are all native to the Americas (New World) and were introduced to Asia/Europe (Old World) by European colonial powers in the early modern period.
**Keywords:** New World plants, Columbian Exchange, Colonial trade.
**Related Personalities:** Christopher Columbus.
**Memory Trick:** "T-C-R (Tobacco, Cocoa, Rubber) = The American Trio."
**Common Exam Trap:** Including Coffee or Sugarcane (which were Old World crops brought to the New World).
**Why Important:** Reflects the biological impact of the European arrival in India.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-170
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2010
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Simon Commission was appointed to:
**Options:**
(a) review the working of the Government of India Act 1919.
(b) investigate the causes of the 1919 Rowlatt Satyagraha.
(c) suggest a new plan for the Partition of India.
(d) examine the relationship between the Princes and the Crown.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The GOI Act 1919 had a provision that a statutory commission would be appointed after 10 years to review its working and suggest further reforms. The Simon Commission was appointed two years early (1927) for this purpose.
**Keywords:** Simon Commission, Review, GOI Act 1919.
**Related Context:** "Go Back Simon" protests.
**Memory Trick:** "Simon for Statutory Review (of 1919)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Butler Committee (statement d) or Hunter Committee (statement b).
**Why Important:** Triggered the Nehru Report and the Civil Disobedience Movement.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-171
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Revolutionary & Communist Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2006
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the year 1915, the first Provisional Government of India with Mahendra Pratap as President was established in:
**Options:**
(a) Kabul
(b) Tokyo
(c) Berlin
(d) San Francisco
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Raja Mahendra Pratap, along with Barkatullah and Obaidullah Sindhi, established the first Provisional Government of Free India in Kabul (Afghanistan) in 1915, during the First World War. He was supported by Germany and Turkey.
**Keywords:** Provisional Government 1915, Kabul, Mahendra Pratap.
**Related Personalities:** Barkatullah.
**Memory Trick:** "Pratap in the Peaks (Kabul)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Berlin (which was the HQ of the Indian Independence Committee) or Singapore (HQ of Bose's later provisional govt).
**Why Important:** First formal attempt to establish a sovereign Indian administration abroad.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-172
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2014
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following is/are the proposal(s) of the Cripps Mission?
1. Provision for the creation of an Indian Union with Dominion Status.
2. Provision for a Constituent Assembly elected partly by provincial assemblies and partly nominated by princes.
3. Any province not prepared to accept the new constitution would have the right to sign a separate agreement with Britain.
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** All three were core parts of the 1942 Cripps offer: (1) Post-war Dominion status; (2) An assembly with elected and nominated members; (3) The "Local Option" for provinces to secede and sign separate treaties.
**Keywords:** Cripps Mission, Dominion Status, Local Option.
**Related Personalities:** Stafford Cripps.
**Memory Trick:** "Union Status + Princes' Choice + Provincial Exit."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Cripps offered *Full Independence* (he only offered Dominion Status).
**Why Important:** Failure led to the "Quit India" call.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-173
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Chronology
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2014
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian freedom struggle, which of the following is the correct chronological order of the given events?
**Options:**
(a) Simon Commission - First Round Table Conference - Gandhi-Irwin Pact
(b) Gandhi-Irwin Pact - Simon Commission - First Round Table Conference
(c) First Round Table Conference - Gandhi-Irwin Pact - Simon Commission
(d) Simon Commission - Gandhi-Irwin Pact - First Round Table Conference
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Chronology: (1) Simon Commission (appointed 1927, arrived 1928). (2) First Round Table Conference (Nov 1930). (3) Gandhi-Irwin Pact (March 1931).
**Keywords:** Simon Commission, RTC, Gandhi-Irwin.
**Related Dates:** 1928, 1930, 1931.
**Memory Trick:** "S-R-G (Simon-RTC-Gandhi)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Gandhi-Irwin Pact was needed *before* any conference (he only attended the 2nd after the pact).
**Why Important:** Tests the sequential logic of the 1920s-30s transition.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-174
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2013
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Government of India Act of 1909 is famous for:
**Options:**
(a) introducing separate electorates for Muslims.
(b) introducing Dyarchy in the provinces.
(c) the first step toward centralization.
(d) abolition of the East India Company's rule.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Morley-Minto Reforms (1909) officially introduced the system of separate/communal electorates for Muslims, where only Muslims could vote for Muslim candidates.
**Keywords:** Morley-Minto, Separate Electorates, 1909.
**Related Context:** Divide and Rule.
**Memory Trick:** "Morley-Minto = Muslim Electorates (M-M-M)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the 1919 Act (which introduced Dyarchy).
**Why Important:** It institutionalized communalism in Indian politics.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-175
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following is/are the feature(s) of the Cabinet Mission Plan?
1. Rejection of the demand for a full-fledged Pakistan.
2. Grouping of existing provincial assemblies into three sections.
3. A strong central government with powers over defense and foreign affairs.
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct: The Mission (1946) rejected the idea of Pakistan. Statement 2 is correct: It proposed grouping provinces into A, B, and C sections. Statement 3 is incorrect: It proposed a **weak** center with limited powers (Defense, Foreign Affairs, Communications), while provinces/groups had all other powers.
**Keywords:** Cabinet Mission, Grouping, Weak Center.
**Related Personalities:** Pethick-Lawrence, Cripps, Alexander.
**Memory Trick:** "Cabinet = Grouping but Center-less (weak)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Mission proposed a strong center (the weak center was to placate the League).
**Why Important:** Final effort for a united India.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-176
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies (Education)
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following led to the introduction of English Education in India?
1. Charter Act of 1813
2. General Committee of Public Instruction, 1823
3. Orientalist and Anglicist Controversy
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Charter Act of 1813 (1) first sanctioned one lakh rupees for the promotion of knowledge of modern sciences. The General Committee of Public Instruction (1823) was formed to manage this grant (2). The internal debate between Orientalists and Anglicists (3) eventually led to Macaulay’s Minute (1835) and the formal introduction of English as the medium of instruction.
**Keywords:** English Education, Charter Act 1813, Anglicists, Orientalists.
**Related Acts / Dates:** 1813 (Charter Act), 1835 (Macaulay's Minute).
**Memory Trick:** "1813 Money -> 1823 Committee -> Controversy -> English."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the 1813 Act alone was the trigger; it provided the funds, but the *controversy* and *committee* were essential steps to the final decision.
**Why Important:** Foundational policy for the creation of the English-educated Indian middle class.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-177
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2021
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. The Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms of 1919 recommended granting voting rights to all the women above the age of 21.
2. The Government of India Act of 1935 gave women reserved seats in legislature.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect because the 1919 Reforms did not grant universal suffrage; they allowed for a limited franchise and let provincial legislatures decide on women's enfranchisement. Statement 2 is correct as the 1935 Act extended communal representation and provided reserved seats for women, depressed classes, and labourers.
**Keywords:** Montagu-Chelmsford, GOI Act 1935, Women's Franchise, Reserved Seats.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Chelmsford, Edwin Montagu.
**Memory Trick:** "1919 gave limited (rights), 1935 gave reserved (seats)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Assuming voting rights granted in 1919 were "universal."
**Why Important:** Reflects the slow expansion of democratic representation in colonial India.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-178
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2010
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following were the official Congress negotiators for the Cripps Mission?
**Options:**
(a) Mahatma Gandhi and Sardar Patel
(b) Acharya J.B. Kripalani and C. Rajagopalachari
(c) Pandit Nehru and Maulana Azad
(d) Dr. Rajendra Prasad and Rafi Ahmed Kidwai
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** In 1942, Jawaharlal Nehru and Maulana Abul Kalam Azad were appointed as the official negotiators by the Congress to talk with Stafford Cripps regarding the constitutional proposals.
**Keywords:** Cripps Mission, Congress Negotiators, Nehru, Azad.
**Related Dates:** March 1942.
**Memory Trick:** "N-A Negotiators (Nehru-Azad)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Gandhi (who met Cripps but was not the "official" negotiator for these specific terms).
**Why Important:** Shows the high-level diplomatic attempts to resolve the WWII constitutional deadlock.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-179
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2009
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. The discussions in the Third Round Table Conference eventually led to the passing of the Government of India Act of 1935.
2. The Government of India Act of 1935 provided for the establishment of an All India Federation to be based on a Union of the provinces of British India and the Princely States.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Both are correct. The Third RTC (1932) resulted in a White Paper which formed the basis of the 1935 Act. The Act proposed a Federation consisting of British Indian provinces and Princely States (though the federation never materialised as the states didn't join).
**Keywords:** Third RTC, GOI Act 1935, All India Federation.
**Related Acts:** Government of India Act 1935.
**Memory Trick:** "RTC -> White Paper -> 1935 Act -> Federation Idea."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Federation was actually established (it was only *proposed*).
**Why Important:** It was the blueprint for the administrative structure of India.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-180
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2014
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What was/were the object/objects of Queen Victoria's Proclamation (1858)?
1. To disclaim any intention to annex Indian States.
2. To place the Indian administration under the British Crown.
3. To regulate East India Company's trade with India.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Proclamation disclaimed further territorial expansion (1) and transferred governance from the EIC to the Crown (2). Statement 3 is incorrect because the Act abolished the Company's administrative powers entirely rather than just "regulating" its trade (its commercial monopoly had ended earlier).
**Keywords:** Queen's Proclamation 1858, Crown Rule, Annexation.
**Related Acts:** GOI Act 1858.
**Memory Trick:** "End of Lapse, End of Company."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with earlier Charter Acts that "regulated" the Company.
**Why Important:** Marked the beginning of direct British colonial rule over India.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-181
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2013
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian History, the Members of the Constituent Assembly from the Provinces were:
**Options:**
(a) directly elected by the people of those Provinces
(b) nominated by the Indian National Congress and the Muslim League
(c) elected by the Provincial Legislative Assemblies
(d) selected by the Government for their expertise in constitutional matters
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Following the Cabinet Mission Plan (1946), CA members were elected indirectly by the members of the Provincial Legislative Assemblies through proportional representation.
**Keywords:** Constituent Assembly, Provincial Assemblies, Indirect Election.
**Related Acts:** Cabinet Mission Plan 1946.
**Memory Trick:** "Assembly by Assemblies."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting "directly elected" (which was the Congress's original demand but not the reality).
**Why Important:** This body drafted the modern Constitution of India.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-182
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2008
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following suggested the reconstitution of the Viceroy’s Executive Council in which all the portfolios including that of War Members were to be held by the Indian leaders?
**Options:**
(a) Simon Commission
(b) Simla Conference
(c) Cripps Proposal
(d) Cabinet Mission
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Simla Conference (1945), based on the Wavell Plan, proposed an all-Indian executive council except for the Viceroy and Commander-in-Chief.
**Keywords:** Simla Conference, Wavell Plan, Portfolios.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Wavell.
**Memory Trick:** "Wavell = War Member Portfolio to Indians."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Cripps mission which only offered post-war reforms.
**Why Important:** First formal attempt at a fully "Indianised" executive.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-184
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following statements correctly explains the impact of Industrial Revolution on India in the first half of the nineteenth century?
**Options:**
(a) Indian handicrafts were ruined.
(b) Machines were introduced in the Indian textile industry in large numbers.
(c) Railway lines were laid in many parts of the country.
(d) Heavy duties were imposed on the imports of British manufactures.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** In the first half of the 19th century (up to 1850), the "One-Way Free Trade" and flood of British machine-made cloth led to the destruction of India's traditional weaving and handicraft industries. Railways (1853) and machines came later.
**Keywords:** Industrial Revolution, Handicrafts ruined, De-industrialization.
**Related Concepts:** Wealth Drain.
**Memory Trick:** "1st Half = Destruction; 2nd Half = Development (for colonial needs)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (c) - Railways started in the *second* half (1853).
**Why Important:** Highlights the economic impoverishment under early British rule.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-185
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2019
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following groups of plants was domesticated in the 'New World' and introduced into the 'Old World'?
**Options:**
(a) Tobacco, cocoa and rubber
(b) Cotton, wheat and rice
(c) Wheat, coffee and sugarcane
(d) Rubber, coffee and wheat
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** This refers to the "Columbian Exchange." Tobacco, cocoa, and rubber are native to the Americas (New World) and were brought to India/Asia (Old World) by Europeans.
**Keywords:** New World plants, Columbian Exchange, Tobacco.
**Related Personalities:** Christopher Columbus.
**Memory Trick:** "T-C-R from the Americas."
**Common Exam Trap:** Including Coffee or Wheat (which were Old World/Asia natives).
**Why Important:** Shows the biological impact of European colonial arrivals.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-186
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2010
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Simon Commission was appointed to:
**Options:**
(a) review the working of the Government of India Act 1919
(b) investigate the causes of the 1919 Rowlatt Satyagraha
(c) suggest a new plan for the Partition of India
(d) examine the relationship between the Princes and the Crown
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The 1919 Act provided for a commission after 10 years to review its progress. The Simon Commission (1927) was appointed two years early for this purpose.
**Keywords:** Simon Commission, GOI Act 1919 Review.
**Related Context:** "Go Back Simon" protests.
**Memory Trick:** "Simon for Statutory Review."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Hunter Committee (1919 enquiry).
**Why Important:** Led to the Nehru Report and the Civil Disobedience Movement.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-187

**Question Category:** Revolutionary & Communist Movements

**Question:** In the year 1915, the first Provisional Government of India with Mahendra Pratap as President was established in:
**Options:**
(a) Kabul
(b) Tokyo
(c) Berlin
(d) San Francisco
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Raja Mahendra Pratap, Barkatullah, and Obaidullah Sindhi established the first Provisional Government of Free India in Kabul (Afghanistan) during WWI.
**Keywords:** Provisional Government 1915, Kabul, Mahendra Pratap.
**Related Personalities:** Barkatullah.
**Memory Trick:** "Pratap in the Peaks (Kabul)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Berlin (which was the HQ of the Independence Committee but not the Provisional Govt).
**Why Important:** First formal diplomatic attempt for Indian sovereignty abroad.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-188
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following is/are the feature(s) of the Cabinet Mission Plan?
1. Rejection of the demand for a full-fledged Pakistan.
2. Grouping of existing provincial assemblies into three sections.
3. A strong central government with powers over defense and foreign affairs.
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct; the Mission (1946) rejected Partition. Statement 2 is correct; it proposed grouping provinces (A, B, C). Statement 3 is incorrect; it proposed a **weak** center with limited powers (only Defense, Foreign Affairs, Communications) to satisfy the League's autonomy demand.
**Keywords:** Cabinet Mission, Grouping, Weak Center.
**Related Acts:** Cabinet Mission Plan 1946.
**Memory Trick:** "Cabinet = Groups but weak center."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the center was "strong" (it was deliberately weak in the plan).
**Why Important:** Last major attempt to keep India united.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-189
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Swadeshi Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2019
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Swadeshi Movement, consider the following statements:
1. It contributed to the revival of the indigenous artisan crafts and industries.
2. The National Council of Education was established as a part of Swadeshi Movement.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Swadeshi promoted indigenous goods (1). In 1906, the National Council of Education was set up to impart education on national lines and under national control (2).
**Keywords:** Swadeshi, National Council of Education, Indigenous crafts.
**Related Dates:** 1906 (Education Council).
**Memory Trick:** "Swadeshi = Self-Work + Self-Study."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Council was earlier.
**Why Important:** Shows the constructive side of the movement.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-190
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Swadeshi Movement

**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the book "Desher Katha" written by Sakharam Ganesh Deuskar during the freedom struggle, consider the following statements:
1. It warned against the Colonial State’s hypnotic conquest of the mind.
2. It inspired the performance of swadeshi street plays and folk songs.
3. The use of ‘desh’ by Deuskar was in the specific context of the region of Bengal.
Which of the statements given above are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Published in 1904, it exposed British economic exploitation and warned against cultural hypnosis (1, 2). Statement 3 is incorrect because Deuskar used 'Desh' to refer to India (Bharat) as a whole, not just Bengal.
**Keywords:** Desher Katha, Sakharam Deuskar, Swadeshi literature.
**Related Context:** Anti-partition agitation.
**Memory Trick:** "Deuskar's Desh is bigger than Bengal."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking a Bengali book only spoke of Bengal.
**Why Important:** Landmark in vernacular nationalist literature.

**Answer:** (a)

**Why Important:** Transition of the Home Rule movement into the broader Gandhian fold.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-192

**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The object of the Butler Committee of 1927 was to?
**Options:**
(a) Define the jurisdiction of the Central and Provincial Governments.
(b) Define the powers of the Secretary of State for India.
(c) Impose censorship on national press.
(d) Improve the relationship between the Government of India and the Indian States.
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Harcourt Butler Committee (1927) examined the relationship between the Paramount Power (British) and the Princely States and suggested economic improvements.

**Memory Trick:** "Butler for the Princes."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with administrative committees like Muddiman (Dyarchy).
**Why Important:** Pivotal in the "Paramountcy" debate.

**Options:**
(a) Federal Legislature
(b) Governor General
(c) Provincial Legislature
(d) Provincial Governors
**Answer:** (b)

**Related Acts:** GOI Act 1935.
**Memory Trick:** "Residue goes to the Boss (GG)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it went to the Federal Legislature (as it does in the modern Indian Parliament).
**Why Important:** Highlights the centralized control of the Crown.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-194
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2017
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the context of Indian history, the principle of 'Dyarchy (diarchy)' refers to:
**Options:**
(a) Division of the central legislature into two houses.
(b) Introduction of double government i.e., Central and State governments.
(c) Having two sets of rulers; one in London and another in Delhi.
(d) Division of the subjects delegated to the provinces into two categories.
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Dyarchy introduced by the 1919 Act divided provincial subjects into 'Transferred' and 'Reserved' categories.
**Keywords:** Dyarchy, Transferred/Reserved subjects.
**Related Acts:** GOI Act 1919.
**Memory Trick:** "Dyarchy = Dual Rule in Provinces."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with "Bicameralism" (two houses).
**Why Important:** Core structural reform of the 1919 Act.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-195

**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans

**Year:** 2015
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the Cabinet Mission, which of the following statements is/are correct?
1. It recommended a federal government.
2. It enlarged the powers of the Indian courts.
3. It provided for more Indians in the ICS.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3
(c) 1 and 3
(d) None
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Mission proposed a federal union (1). Statements 2 and 3 are incorrect as the Mission focused on the transfer of power and constitutional framework, not judicial powers or ICS recruitment.
**Keywords:** Cabinet Mission 1946, Federal Government.
**Related Personalities:** Pethick-Lawrence.
**Memory Trick:** "Cabinet = Grouping and Federal."
**Common Exam Trap:** Adding general reforms (like ICS) that were not the Mission's scope.
**Why Important:** Final British attempt for a united India.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-196
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2013
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian History, the Members of the Constituent Assembly from the Provinces were
**Options:**
(a) directly elected by the people of those Provinces
(b) nominated by the Indian National Congress and the Muslim League
(c) elected by the Provincial Legislative Assemblies
(d) selected by the Government for their expertise in constitutional matters
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The members were indirectly elected by the members of the Provincial Legislative Assemblies (who themselves were elected on a limited franchise).
**Keywords:** CA Members, Indirect Election.
**Related Acts:** Cabinet Mission Plan 1946.
**Memory Trick:** "Assemblies elected the Assembly."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking they were directly elected by the people.
**Why Important:** Defines the representative nature of India's founding body.
**Sources:**

(b) attainment of Poorna Swaraj was adopted as the goal of the Congress.
(c) Non-Cooperation Movement was launched.

**Related Dates:** 31 Dec 1929.
**Memory Trick:** "Lahore 29 = Total Freedom."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing Swaraj (1906) with Purna Swaraj (1929).
**Why Important:** Final shift in nationalist goals.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-198
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1998
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The August Offer of 1940 was significant because:
**Options:**
(a) It proposed Dominion status after the war.
(b) It gave Congress total authority in the interim.
(c) It rejected the idea of Pakistan.
(d) It allowed Indians to draft their own constitution for the first time.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Lord Linlithgow's offer proposed (1) Dominion status after the war, (2) expansion of the Viceroy's council, and (3) a constituent body after the war. It was the first formal offer of "Dominion Status."
**Keywords:** August Offer, Dominion Status, Linlithgow.
**Related Dates:** Aug 1940.
**Memory Trick:** "Offer of 40 = Dominion Dream."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it gave "Complete Independence."
**Why Important:** Prelude to the Cripps and Quit India phases.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-199
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was the first individual to start the 'Individual Satyagraha' in 1940?
**Options:**
(a) Vinoba Bhave
(b) Jawaharlal Nehru
(c) Brahma Dutt
(d) Sarojini Naidu
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** To protest against WWII participation, Gandhi launched Individual Satyagraha. Vinoba Bhave was the first Satyagrahi, followed by Nehru.
**Keywords:** Individual Satyagraha, Vinoba Bhave, 1940.
**Related Personalities:** Vinoba Bhave, J. Nehru.
**Memory Trick:** "V-N-B: Vinoba, Nehru, Brahma Dutt (The Order)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Nehru as the first (he was the second).
**Why Important:** Showed Gandhi's limited protest strategy to avoid large-scale civil war during the WWII crisis.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-200
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2022
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the proposals of Cripps Mission, consider the following statements:
1. The Constituent Assembly would have members nominated by the Provincial Assemblies as well as the Princely States.
2. Any Province which is not prepared to accept the new Constitution would have the right to sign a separate agreement with Britain regarding its future status.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect; members were to be partly *elected* by provincial assemblies and partly *nominated* by princes. Statement 2 is correct; the mission offered a "Local Option" to stay out of the Indian Union.
**Keywords:** Cripps Mission, Local Option, Nominated Princes.
**Related Dates:** 1942.
**Memory Trick:** "Cripps = Partial Democracy + Partial Partition."
**Common Exam Trap:** Missing the "elected" vs "nominated" distinction for provinces.
**Why Important:** Its failure led to the Quit India Movement.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-201
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2022
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian history, consider the following statements:
1. The Dutch established their factories/warehouses on the east coast on lands granted to them by Gajapati rulers.
2. Alfonso de Albuquerque captured Goa from the Bijapur Sultanate.
3. The English East India Company established a factory at Madras on a plot of land leased from a representative of the Vijayanagara empire.
Which of the statements given above are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect: The Dutch established their factories on the east coast in the early 17th century (Masulipatnam, 1605), while the Gajapati dynasty of Odisha had declined by the mid-16th century. Statement 2 is correct: Alfonso de Albuquerque captured Goa from the Sultan of Bijapur (Ismail Adil Shah) in 1510. Statement 3 is correct: Francis Day obtained the lease of Madras in 1639 from the local Nayak (Damarla Venkatadri Nayaka), who was a representative/vassal of the Aravidu dynasty of the Vijayanagara empire (Venkatapati Raya II).
**Keywords:** Dutch factories, Albuquerque, Goa, Madras factory.
**Related Personalities:** Alfonso de Albuquerque, Francis Day, Venkatapati Raya II.
**Memory Trick:** "Portuguese took Goa, English leased Madras."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Gajapatis were contemporary to the Dutch arrival.
**Why Important:** Tests micro-level chronological and political linkages between European powers and local Indian dynasties.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-202
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the history of India, consider the following pairs:
1. Aurang — In-charge of treasury of the State
2. Banian — Indian agent of the East India Company
3. Mirasidar — Designated revenue payer to the State
Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Pair 1 is incorrectly matched: "Aurang" is a Persian term for a warehouse where goods are collected before being sold. Pair 2 is correctly matched: "Banian" was an Indian agent/middleman for the English East India Company. Pair 3 is correctly matched: "Mirasidar" was a term used in the South (Madras Presidency) to denote a hereditary proprietor of land who was the designated revenue payer to the state.
**Keywords:** Aurang, Banian, Mirasidar, Terminology.
**Related Concepts:** Land Revenue Systems, Trade Agents.
**Memory Trick:** "Banian = Business Agent; Mirasidar = Madras landholder."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing Aurang with an administrative title like 'Amil' or 'Diwan'.
**Why Important:** UPSC frequently tests administrative and economic terminology from the medieval and modern transition.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-203
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2023
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** By which one of the following Acts was the Governor General of Bengal designated as the Governor General of India?
**Options:**
(a) The Regulating Act
(b) The Pitt’s India Act
(c) The Charter Act of 1793
(d) The Charter Act of 1833
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Charter Act of 1833 made the Governor-General of Bengal the Governor-General of India and vested in him all civil and military powers. Lord William Bentinck became the first Governor-General of India under this Act.
**Keywords:** Governor General of India, Charter Act 1833, William Bentinck.
**Related Acts:** Regulating Act 1773 (GG of Bengal), GOI Act 1858 (Viceroy).
**Memory Trick:** "1833: Bengal became India (B-to-I)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting the 1773 Act (which only gave the title 'GG of Bengal').
**Why Important:** Centralisation of the British administration in India.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-204
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2009
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which of the following movements has contributed to a split in the Indian National Congress resulting in 'Moderates' and 'Extremists'?
**Options:**
(a) Swadeshi Movement
(b) Quit India Movement
(c) Non-Cooperation Movement
(d) Civil Disobedience Movement
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Differences over the methods and scope of the Swadeshi and Boycott movement (1905–1907) led to the historic split between the Moderates and Extremists at the 1907 Surat Session. The Extremists wanted to extend the movement outside Bengal and include all forms of association, while Moderates wanted to keep it localized.
**Keywords:** Surat Split, Swadeshi Movement, Moderates, Extremists.
**Related Personalities:** B.G. Tilak, Rash Behari Ghosh.
**Memory Trick:** "Swadeshi split the Surat Session."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the split happened due to the Rowlatt Act or Non-Cooperation.
**Why Important:** Watershed moment that weakened the early national movement.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-205
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Under whose presidency was the first session of the Indian National Congress held?
**Options:**
(a) A.O. Hume
(b) W.C. Bannerjee
(c) Dadabhai Naoroji
(d) Badruddin Tyabji
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The first session of the Indian National Congress was held in December 1885 at Gokuldas Tejpal Sanskrit College, Bombay. It was presided over by Womesh Chandra Bannerjee (W.C. Bannerjee). A.O. Hume was the General Secretary and the primary organizer.
**Keywords:** INC 1885, W.C. Bannerjee, first session.
**Related Personalities:** A.O. Hume, Lord Dufferin.
**Memory Trick:** "W.C. was the winner of the first chair."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting A.O. Hume (who was the founder/secretary, not the President).
**Why Important:** Founding fact of India's premier political organization.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-206
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2004
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the period of colonial rule in India, consider the following statements:
1. Raja Ram Mohan Roy was one of the founders of the Tattvabodhini Sabha.
2. The Brahmo Samaj split into two factions during the leadership of Debendranath Tagore.
3. Keshab Chandra Sen founded the Brahmo Samaj of India.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect: Tattvabodhini Sabha was founded by Debendranath Tagore in 1839 (after Roy's death). Statement 2 is incorrect: The first split in the Brahmo Samaj occurred in 1866, with Keshab Chandra Sen breaking away from Debendranath Tagore's group. Statement 3 is correct: Keshab Chandra Sen founded the "Brahmo Samaj of India" while Tagore's group came to be known as the "Adi Brahmo Samaj".
**Keywords:** Brahmo Samaj, Keshab Chandra Sen, Tattvabodhini Sabha.
**Related Personalities:** Raja Ram Mohan Roy, Debendranath Tagore.
**Memory Trick:** "Keshab's Kin (Samaj of India) broke from the Adi (Tagore)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Attributing Tattvabodhini Sabha to Raja Ram Mohan Roy.
**Why Important:** Detail-oriented check on the evolution of 19th-century reform movements.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-207
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The 'Black Hole Tragedy' is associated with which battle?
**Options:**
(a) Battle of Buxar
(b) Battle of Plassey
(c) Third Battle of Panipat
(d) Battle of Wandiwash
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Black Hole Tragedy (1756) occurred in Calcutta under Nawab Siraj-ud-Daulah. British prisoners were allegedly kept in a small, cramped room, leading to many deaths. This incident was used as a primary justification by Robert Clive for the invasion that led to the Battle of Plassey (1757).
**Keywords:** Black Hole Tragedy, Siraj-ud-Daulah, Plassey.
**Related Dates:** 1756 (Black Hole), 1757 (Plassey).
**Memory Trick:** "Black Hole led to the Blood of Plassey."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it led to the Battle of Buxar (which was later in 1764).
**Why Important:** Iconic propaganda event that altered the course of Bengal's history.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-208
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** Peasant Movement and Tribal Rebellions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** After the Santhal Uprising (1855-56) was pacified, what was/were the measure/measures taken by the British Government?
1. The territories called ‘Santhal Parganas’ were created.
2. It became illegal for a Santhal to transfer land to a non-Santhal.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Both are correct. Following the rebellion, the British created a separate administrative unit called the 'Santhal Parganas' (1) and enacted the Santhal Pargana Tenancy Act, which prohibited the transfer of tribal land to non-tribals (2) to prevent further exploitation by 'Dikus' (outsiders).
**Keywords:** Santhal Uprising, Santhal Parganas, Land transfer.
**Related Personalities:** Sidhu and Kanhu Murmu.
**Memory Trick:** "Uprising led to a protected Pargana."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking no positive measures were taken and only repression followed.
**Why Important:** Represents early colonial recognition of tribal land rights as a means of security.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-209
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Mahatma Gandhi undertook fast unto death in 1932 mainly because:
**Options:**
(a) Round Table Conference failed to satisfy Indian political aspirations
(b) Congress and Muslim League had differences of opinion
(c) Ramsay Macdonald announced the Communal Award
(d) None of the statements (a), (b) and (c) given above is correct in this context
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** In 1932, British Prime Minister Ramsay MacDonald announced the 'Communal Award', which granted separate electorates to the Depressed Classes (Harijans). Gandhi viewed this as an attempt to permanently divide Hindu society and began a fast unto death in Yerwada Jail, which led to the Poona Pact.
**Keywords:** Fast unto death, Communal Award, 1932, Poona Pact.
**Related Personalities:** Ramsay MacDonald, B.R. Ambedkar.
**Memory Trick:** "Award (MacDonald) led to the fast, Pact (Poona) broke the fast."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the fast was about the general failure of the Round Table Conferences.
**Why Important:** Landmark event in the struggle for social reform and political unity.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-210
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the history of India, consider the following pairs:
1. Radhakanta Deb — First President of the British Indian Association
2. Gazulu Lakshminarasu Chetty — Founder of the Madras Mahajana Sabha
3. Surendranath Banerjee — Founder of the Indian Association
Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Pair 1 is correct: Radhakanta Deb was the first president of the British Indian Association (1851). Pair 2 is incorrect: Gazulu Lakshminarasu Chetty founded the Madras Native Association; the Madras Mahajana Sabha was founded in 1884 by leaders like M. Viraraghavachariar and G. Subramania Iyer. Pair 3 is correct: Surendranath Banerjee (along with Anandamohan Bose) founded the Indian Association of Calcutta in 1876.
**Keywords:** British Indian Association, Madras Mahajana Sabha, Indian Association.
**Related Personalities:** Radhakanta Deb, Surendranath Banerjee.
**Memory Trick:** "Banerjee-Indian Assoc, Deb-President (BIA)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing Madras Native Association with Madras Mahajana Sabha.
**Why Important:** Tests knowledge of pre-Congress political mobilization.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-211
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the Indian freedom struggle, which of the following is/are true about Annie Besant?
1. She was responsible for starting the Home Rule Movement.
2. She was the founder of the Theosophical Society.
3. She was once the President of the Indian National Congress.
Select the correct answer:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is correct: Annie Besant started the All-India Home Rule League in 1916. Statement 2 is incorrect: The Theosophical Society was founded in New York in 1875 by Madam Blavatsky and Colonel Olcott (Besant later became its President). Statement 3 is correct: She was the first woman President of the INC at the 1917 Calcutta Session.
**Keywords:** Annie Besant, Home Rule, 1917 INC Session.
**Related Personalities:** Madam Blavatsky, Tilak.
**Memory Trick:** "Annie: Home (Rule) + First Woman President."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking she founded the Theosophical Society (she joined it later).
**Why Important:** Focuses on the role of non-Indian personalities in the freedom struggle.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-212
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** 'Vital-Vidvansak', the first monthly journal to have the untouchable people as its target audience was published by:
**Options:**
(a) Gopal Baba Walangkar
(b) Jyotiba Phule
(c) Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi
(d) B. R. Ambedkar
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** 'Vital-Vidvansak' (Destroyer of Ritualistic Pollutions) was published in 1888 by Gopal Baba Walangkar, an early social reformer from Maharashtra who campaigned against caste discrimination. It is considered one of the first journals dedicated to the Dalit/untouchable cause.
**Keywords:** Vital-Vidvansak, Gopal Baba Walangkar, Dalit Journalism.
**Related Personalities:** Jyotiba Phule.
**Memory Trick:** "Walangkar was the Vital-Vidvansak."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Ambedkar (who started later journals like Mooknayak) or Phule.
**Why Important:** Highlights early, non-mainstream efforts in the anti-caste movement.
**Sources:**.
