**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-213
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Personality Based Questions
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the context of Indian history, the Rakhmabai case of 1884 revolved around:
1. Women's right to gain education
2. Age of consent
3. Restitution of conjugal rights
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Rakhmabai case (1884) was a landmark legal battle where a woman refused to live with her husband (whom she married as a child). The case focused on the 'Restitution of Conjugal Rights' (3). The public debate surrounding it directly influenced the enactment of the Age of Consent Act, 1891 (2). It did not primarily revolve around her right to education, though she later became a doctor.
**Keywords:** Rakhmabai Case, Age of Consent, Conjugal Rights.
**Related Acts:** Age of Consent Act 1891.
**Memory Trick:** "Rakhmabai: Consent and Conjugal Rights."
**Common Exam Trap:** Including education because she was a famous lady doctor.
**Why Important:** One of the most famous legal cases involving women's rights in colonial India.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-214
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** Working Class Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2017
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Trade Disputes Act of 1929 provided for:
**Options:**
(a) the participation of workers in the management of industries.
(b) arbitrary powers to the management to quell industrial disputes.
(c) an intervention by the British Court in the event of a trade dispute.
(d) a system of tribunals and a ban on strikes.
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Trade Disputes Act (1929) introduced a system of courts of inquiry and conciliation boards for industrial disputes. Crucially, it made strikes and lockouts illegal in public utility services without prior notice and placed a general ban on "sympathetic" or political strikes.
**Keywords:** Trade Disputes Act 1929, Ban on strikes, Tribunals.
**Related Personalities:** Bhagat Singh (context of throwing bombs in assembly).
**Memory Trick:** "1929: Disputing the right to strike."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it was a pro-worker act (it was highly restrictive/repressive).
**Why Important:** Directly linked to the radicalisation of the 1920s and the HSRA's protest.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-215
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Swadeshi Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2016
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The 'Swadeshi' and 'Boycott' were adopted as methods of struggle for the first time during the:
**Options:**
(a) agitation against the Partition of Bengal
(b) Home Rule Movement
(c) Non-Cooperation Movement
(d) visit of the Simon Commission to India
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Swadeshi (use of indigenous goods) and Boycott (of British goods) were first formally adopted as political weapons during the Anti-Partition agitation of 1905 in Bengal.
**Keywords:** Swadeshi, Boycott, 1905, Partition of Bengal.
**Related Dates:** August 7, 1905 (Town Hall Meeting).
**Memory Trick:** "Swadeshi started when Bengal was split."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Non-Cooperation Movement where these methods were used at a much larger scale.
**Why Important:** Marks the birth of modern mass political agitation in India.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-216
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2013
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The 'Quit India Movement' was launched in response to:
**Options:**
(a) Cabinet Mission Plan
(b) Cripps Proposals
(c) Simon Commission Report
(d) Wavell Plan
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The failure of the Cripps Mission (March 1942) to offer immediate self-government or an acceptable constitutional roadmap led Gandhi to call for the Quit India Movement in August 1942.
**Keywords:** Quit India, 1942, Cripps Mission failure.
**Related Personalities:** Stafford Cripps.
**Memory Trick:** "Cripps went back, Quit India came forward."
**Common Exam Trap:** Swapping it with Cabinet Mission (which happened *after* the movement).
**Why Important:** The immediate political catalyst for the 'Do or Die' struggle.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-217
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was/were associated with the introduction of Ryotwari Settlement in India during the British rule?
1. Lord Cornwallis
2. Alexander Read
3. Thomas Munro
Select the correct answer:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect: Lord Cornwallis is associated with the Permanent Settlement (Zamindari). Statements 2 and 3 are correct: Alexander Read first introduced it on a small scale in the Baramahal district (1792), and Thomas Munro later expanded it across the Madras Presidency (1820).
**Keywords:** Ryotwari, Thomas Munro, Alexander Read.
**Related Context:** Land Revenue Systems.
**Memory Trick:** "Read and Munro made the Ryot (peasant) pay."
**Common Exam Trap:** Including Cornwallis due to his general fame in land reforms.
**Why Important:** Key land system used in South and West India.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-218
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. The First Session of the Indian National Congress was held in Calcutta.
2. The Second Session of the Indian National Congress was held under the presidentship of Dadabhai Naoroji.
3. Both Indian National Congress and Muslim League held their sessions at Lucknow in 1916 and concluded the Lucknow Pact.
Which of the statements given above are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is incorrect: The first session was held in Bombay (1885). Statement 2 is correct: The second session was held in Calcutta (1886) with Dadabhai Naoroji as President. Statement 3 is correct: In 1916, both organizations met in Lucknow and signed the Pact for joint political demands.
**Keywords:** INC Sessions, Lucknow Pact, Dadabhai Naoroji.
**Related Dates:** 1885, 1886, 1916.
**Memory Trick:** "1-Bombay, 2-Calcutta; 1916-Lucknow Unity."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the first session was in Calcutta because it was the capital.
**Why Important:** Covers fundamental organizational milestones of the INC.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-219
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Revolutionary & Communist Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2014
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Ghaddar was a:
**Options:**
(a) Revolutionary association of Indians with headquarters at San Francisco.
(b) Nationalist organization operating from Singapore.
(c) Militant organization with headquarters at Berlin.
(d) Communist movement for India's freedom with headquarters at Tashkent.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Ghadar Party (initially Pacific Coast Hindustan Association) was a revolutionary organization founded in 1913 by Indians (primarily Punjabis) in the US and Canada. Its headquarters, the 'Yugantar Ashram', was in San Francisco.
**Keywords:** Ghadar Party, San Francisco, 1913.
**Related Personalities:** Lala Hardayal, Sohan Singh Bhakna.
**Memory Trick:** "Ghadar in the Golden State (San Francisco)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Berlin Committee or the Tashkent CPI.
**Why Important:** Global face of the Indian revolution.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-220
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2004
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The name of the famous person of India who returned the Knighthood conferred on him by the British Government as a token of protest against the atrocities in Punjab in 1919 was:
**Options:**
(a) Rabindranath Tagore
(b) Tej Bahadur Sapru
(c) Ashutosh Mukherjee
(d) S. Subramania Iyer
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** In response to the Jallianwala Bagh Massacre (April 1919), Rabindranath Tagore renounced his knighthood in a famous letter to the Viceroy, stating that "The time has come when badges of honour make our shame glaring in the incongruous context of humiliation."
**Keywords:** Knighthood, Tagore, Jallianwala Bagh.
**Related Personalities:** Mahatma Gandhi (returned Kaiser-i-Hind).
**Memory Trick:** "Tagore renounced Title for Tragedies."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing S. Subramania Iyer (who returned his title earlier during the Home Rule League arrests) with Tagore.
**Why Important:** High point of intellectual protest against colonial violence.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-221
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2003
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following places was the first to have a municipality in India?
**Options:**
(a) Bombay
(b) Calcutta
(c) Lucknow
(d) Madras
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The first Municipal Corporation in India was set up at Madras in 1687 (Royal Charter 1688). Corporations at Bombay and Calcutta were established much later in 1726.
**Keywords:** Municipality, Madras 1687.
**Related Acts:** Charter of 1726.
**Memory Trick:** "Madras was the Mother of Municipalities."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Calcutta (the later capital) or Bombay.
**Why Important:** Traces the origins of local self-government in India.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-222
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the history of India, the terms 'Kulyavapa' and 'Dronavapa' denote:
**Options:**
(a) Measurement of land
(b) Coins of different denominations
(c) Classification of urban land
(d) Religious rituals
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** These terms appear in inscriptions of the Gupta and post-Gupta periods (and continued into the transition to modern land administration study). 'Vapa' means sowing; 'Kulyavapa' and 'Dronavapa' represent the area of land required to sow one kulya and one drona of grain respectively. They were units of land measurement.
**Keywords:** Kulyavapa, Dronavapa, Land Measurement.
**Related Context:** Revenue administration.
**Memory Trick:** "Vapa = (Sowing) Volumes of land."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking they are names of coins or taxes.
**Why Important:** Tests precision in ancient-to-medieval administrative terminology often relevant for history optional.
**Sources:**.

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-223
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In which of the following sessions of the Indian National Congress was the 'resolution on Fundamental Rights and Economic Policy' passed?
**Options:**
(a) Belgaum Session (1924)
(b) Karachi Session (1931)
(c) Lahore Session (1929)
(d) Faizpur Session (1936)
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Karachi Session (1931), presided over by Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel, is famous for passing the resolution on Fundamental Rights and the National Economic Programme. This was a response to the growing radical socialist influence within the Congress.
**Keywords:** Karachi Session 1931, Fundamental Rights, Economic Policy.
**Related Personalities:** Sardar Patel, M.N. Roy (drafting).
**Memory Trick:** "Karachi = Rights and Rupee (Economy)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Lahore (1929) which was for Purna Swaraj.
**Why Important:** Defined the social and economic vision of independent India.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-224
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who of the following suggested that the Indian National Congress should be disbanded after independence?
**Options:**
(a) C. Rajagopalachari
(b) J.B. Kripalani
(c) Mahatma Gandhi
(d) Jai Prakash Narayan
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Mahatma Gandhi, in his 'Last Will and Testament' (drafted just before his assassination), suggested that the INC as a propaganda vehicle and parliamentary machine had outlived its use and should be disbanded and transformed into a 'Lok Sevak Sangh' to serve the people in villages.
**Keywords:** Disbanding INC, Gandhi, Lok Sevak Sangh.
**Related Dates:** January 1948.
**Memory Trick:** "Gandhi wanted the Party to become a Service (Sangh)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking a political rival like JP Narayan made this suggestion.
**Why Important:** Reflects Gandhi's vision for post-independence social reconstruction vs. political power.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-225
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Revolutionary & Communist Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1997
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The slogan 'Inquilab Zindabad' was first raised by:
**Options:**
(a) Bhagat Singh
(b) Iqbal
(c) Hasrat Mohani
(d) S.C. Bose
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The slogan 'Inquilab Zindabad' (Long Live Revolution) was coined by the Urdu poet and revolutionary leader Hasrat Mohani in 1921. However, it was popularized and "first raised" in a major political context by Bhagat Singh and Batukeshwar Dutt after throwing bombs in the Central Legislative Assembly in 1929. (Note: Most keys and standard UPSC interpretation credit Bhagat Singh with raising it).
**Keywords:** Inquilab Zindabad, Bhagat Singh, Hasrat Mohani.
**Related Context:** HSRA, 1929 Assembly Bombing.
**Memory Trick:** "Mohani Made it, Bhagat Boomed it."
**Common Exam Trap:** Swapping the coiner (Mohani) with the popularizer (Singh).
**Why Important:** The most enduring slogan of the Indian revolutionary movement.
**Sources:**.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-226
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which among the following events happened earliest?
**Options:**
(a) Swami Dayanand established Arya Samaj.
(b) Dinabandhu Mitra wrote *Neel Darpan*.
(c) Bankim Chandra Chattopadhyay wrote *Anandmath*.
(d) Satyendranath Tagore became the first Indian to succeed in the Indian Civil Services Examination.
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Chronology of events: 
1. *Neel Darpan* was written by Dinabandhu Mitra in **1858-1859** following the Indigo Revolt.
2. Satyendranath Tagore became the first Indian to join the ICS in **1863**.
3. Swami Dayanand Saraswati established the Arya Samaj in **1875**.
4. Bankim Chandra Chattopadhyay wrote *Anandmath* in **1882**.
Therefore, the earliest event is the publication of *Neel Darpan*.
**Keywords:** Neel Darpan, Arya Samaj, Anandmath, Satyendranath Tagore.
**Related Personalities:** Dinabandhu Mitra, Dayanand Saraswati, Bankim Chandra.
**Memory Trick:** "Blue (Neel) mirror came before the Saffron (Arya) society."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the ICS success (1863) with the establishment of Arya Samaj (1875).
**Why Important:** Tests precise chronological awareness of 19th-century cultural and administrative milestones.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-227
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements: Some of the main features of the Government of India Act, 1935 were the:
1. Abolition of diarchy in the Governor’s provinces.
2. Power of the Governors to veto legislative action and to legislate on their own.
3. Abolition of the principle of communal representation.
Which of these statements are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The GOI Act 1935 abolished dyarchy in the provinces and introduced provincial autonomy (Statement 1). It gave Governors significant discretionary powers, including vetoing bills and issuing ordinances (Statement 2). However, it did **not** abolish communal representation; in fact, it *extended* it to depressed classes, women, and labour (Statement 3 is incorrect).
**Keywords:** GOI Act 1935, Provincial Autonomy, Dyarchy, Veto.
**Related Acts:** GOI Act 1919 (introduced dyarchy).
**Memory Trick:** "1935 = Autonomy in Provinces, but Electorates expanded, not ended."
**Common Exam Trap:** Believing that the move toward autonomy meant an end to communal voting.
**Why Important:** This Act formed the skeletal basis for the modern Indian Constitution.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-228
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2002
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The real intention of the British to include the princely states in the Federal Union proposed by the India Act of 1935 was to:
**Options:**
(a) exercise more and direct political and administrative control over the princely states
(b) involve the princes actively in the administration of the Central Government
(c) use the princes to counter-balance the anti-imperialist doctrines of the nationalist leaders
(d) finally admit the princely states under the full legal and political authority of the British Crown
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The British proposed an All-India Federation in 1935 to include the Princely States because the Princes were seen as loyal "conservative" elements. Their presence in the federal legislature was intended to check and neutralise the influence of the radical, anti-imperialist Congress nationalists.
**Keywords:** 1935 Act, Federation, Princely States, Counter-balance.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Linlithgow.
**Memory Trick:** "Princes were the Brake for the Nationalist Engine."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the goal was administrative efficiency (it was political survival).
**Why Important:** Explains the British strategy of 'Divide and Rule' applied to constitutional structures.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-229
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2021
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to Indian history, which of the following statements is/are correct?
1. The Nizamat of Arcot emerged out of Hyderabad State.
2. The Mysore Kingdom emerged out of Vijayanagara Empire.
3. Rohilkhand Kingdom was formed out of the territories occupied by Ahmad Shah Durrani.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** 
- Statement 1 is correct: The Carnatic (Arcot) was a province of the Hyderabad subah and later became independent.
- Statement 2 is correct: The Wodeyars established the Mysore kingdom on the ruins of the Vijayanagara Empire.
- Statement 3 is incorrect: Rohilkhand was established by Ali Muhammad Khan and Afghan settlers in the early 18th century as the Mughal central authority collapsed, prior to the major Durrani invasions.
**Keywords:** Arcot, Mysore, Rohilkhand, Successor States.
**Related Personalities:** Nizam-ul-Mulk, Hyder Ali.
**Memory Trick:** "Arcot from Hyderabad, Mysore from Vijayanagara (A-H, M-V)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking all Afghan states in India were Durrani-founded.
**Why Important:** Tests knowledge of regional power shifts during the Mughal decline.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-230
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** The Revolt of 1857
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2005
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Kunwar Singh was a prominent leader of the Revolt of 1857 in:
**Options:**
(a) Bihar
(b) Madhya Pradesh
(c) Rajasthan
(d) Uttar Pradesh
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Kunwar Singh, an 80-year-old zamindar of Jagdishpur, led the revolt in the Arrah/Jagdishpur region of Bihar. He was one of the most successful military leaders of the uprising.
**Keywords:** Kunwar Singh, 1857 Revolt, Jagdishpur, Bihar.
**Related Personalities:** Nana Sahib, Begum Hazrat Mahal.
**Memory Trick:** "Kunwar (Prince) of Bihar."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing him with leaders of Central India like Tatya Tope.
**Why Important:** Key figure of regional resistance in the first war of independence.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-231
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Expansion in India
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2004
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following princely States of the British rule in India:
1. Jhansi
2. Sambalpur
3. Satara
The correct chronological order in which they were annexed by the British is:
**Options:**
(a) 1, 2, 3
(b) 1, 3, 2
(c) 3, 2, 1
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Under Lord Dalhousie's "Doctrine of Lapse", states were annexed in this order: Satara (**1848**), Jaitpur and Sambalpur (**1849**), Baghat (1850), Udaipur (1852), Jhansi (**1853**), and Nagpur (1854).
**Keywords:** Doctrine of Lapse, Annexation, Satara, Sambalpur, Jhansi.
**Related Personality:** Lord Dalhousie.
**Memory Trick:** "Sa-Sam-Jhan (Satara, Sambalpur, Jhansi)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Placing Jhansi first because of its fame in the 1857 revolt.
**Why Important:** One of the most controversial British expansionist policies.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-232
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Expansion in India
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2003
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following statements is NOT correct?
**Options:**
(a) Ali Mardan Khan introduced the system of revenue farming in Bengal.
(b) Maharaja Ranjit Singh set up modern foundries to manufacture cannons at Lahore.
(c) Sawai Jai Singh of Amber built five astronomical observatories.
(d) Tipu Sultan introduced a new calendar and a new coinage system.
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** (a) is incorrect because revenue farming (Ijara) was introduced in Bengal by **Murshid Quli Khan**, not Ali Mardan Khan (who was a Mughal engineer). (b) is correct: Ranjit Singh modernized his army and set up foundries at Lahore and Amritsar. (c) is correct: Sawai Jai Singh built Jantar Mantars. (d) is correct: Tipu Sultan was known for his administrative innovations.
**Keywords:** Ranjit Singh, Tipu Sultan, Revenue Farming, Jantar Mantar.
**Related Personalities:** Murshid Quli Khan, Sawai Jai Singh.
**Memory Trick:** "Murshid made the Money (revenue) system in Bengal."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Tipu Sultan only focused on military (he was a heavy administrative reformer).
**Why Important:** Tests micro-details about the "Great Men" of the 18th century transition.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-233
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Administration
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1997
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was associated with the suppression of Thugs?
**Options:**
(a) General Henry Prendergast
(b) Captain Sleeman
(c) Alexander Burnes
(d) Captain Robert Pemberton
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** During the governorship of Lord William Bentinck (1828–1835), Captain (later Major-General) William Sleeman was appointed to lead the campaign that successfully eliminated the organized bands of robbers known as Thugs.
**Keywords:** Thugs, Captain Sleeman, Lord William Bentinck.
**Related Personality:** William Bentinck.
**Memory Trick:** "Sleeman Slept (put to rest) the Thugs."
**Common Exam Trap:** Attributing the success to the Governor-General himself without naming the specific officer in charge.
**Why Important:** One of the key "humanitarian" social interventions cited by the British.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-234
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1998
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following events was characterised by Montague as 'Preventive Murder'?
**Options:**
(a) Killing of INA activists
(b) Massacre of Jallianwala Bagh
(c) Shooting of the Mahatma
(d) Shooting of Curzon-Wyllie
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Edwin Montagu (Secretary of State) used the term 'Preventive Murder' to describe the Jallianwala Bagh massacre (April 13, 1919), expressing his horror at General Dyer’s actions while the official British stance remained defensive.
**Keywords:** Jallianwala Bagh, Montague, Preventive Murder.
**Related Personality:** General Dyer.
**Memory Trick:** "Montagu called the Massacre a Murder."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing Montagu's liberal criticism with the actual Rowlatt legislative policy.
**Why Important:** Highlights the internal British controversy over colonial violence.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-235
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Anarchical and Revolutionary Crime Act (1919) was popularly known as the:
**Options:**
(a) Rowlatt Act
(b) Pitt's India Act
(c) Indian Arms Act
(d) Ilbert Bill
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Rowlatt Act (1919) was officially named the "Anarchical and Revolutionary Crimes Act". It allowed the government to imprison any person suspected of "terrorist" activities for up to two years without trial.
**Keywords:** Rowlatt Act, 1919, Mass Satyagraha.
**Related Personalities:** Justice Rowlatt.
**Memory Trick:** "No Dalil, No Vakil, No Appeal = Rowlatt."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the name was just "The Rowlatt Act" (which was the shorthand).
**Why Important:** Immediate cause of the Jallianwala Bagh protest and the launch of the Rowlatt Satyagraha.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-238
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Balkan Plan for fragmentation of India was the brain-child of:
**Options:**
(a) W. Churchill
(b) M. A. Jinnah
(c) Lord Mountbatten
(d) V. P. Menon
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** In May 1947, Lord Mountbatten proposed the 'Plan Balkan', which suggested that provinces should be allowed to declare themselves independent before being asked to join a union. Nehru vehemently opposed this, fearing it would lead to total disintegration.
**Keywords:** Balkan Plan, Lord Mountbatten, Fragmentation.
**Related Dates:** May 1947.
**Memory Trick:** "Balkanization Plan by Mountbatten."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Jinnah proposed it (he wanted Pakistan, but Mountbatten proposed the mechanism of provincial choice).
**Why Important:** Led to the revised "June 3rd Plan" which fixed Partition as the only path.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-239
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** As an alternative to the partition of India, Gandhiji suggested to Mountbatten that he:
**Options:**
(a) postpone granting of independence
(b) invite Jinnah to form the government
(c) invite Nehru and Jinnah to form the government together
(d) invite the army to take over for some time
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** In a final effort to keep India united, Gandhi suggested that Mountbatten should invite Muhammad Ali Jinnah to form the central government and appoint his own ministers, provided he worked for the benefit of a united India.
**Keywords:** Gandhi, Partition alternative, Jinnah.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Mountbatten.
**Memory Trick:** "Give Jinnah the Job (Govt) to save the Junction (Unity)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (c), but the specific radical suggestion was to give Jinnah total control to prevent partition.
**Why Important:** Shows Gandhi's desperate pragmatic attempts to avoid division.
**Sources:**

4. Badruddin Tyabji : Muslim League

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-245
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the stapled commodities of the English East India Company from Bengal in the middle of the 18th century, which of the following were exported?
**Options:**
(a) Raw cotton, oil-seeds and opium
(b) Sugar, salt, zinc and lead
(c) Copper, silver, gold, spices and tea
(d) Cotton, silk, saltpetre and opium
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Bengal was the main source of the EIC's lucrative exports, which primarily included textiles (cotton and silk), saltpetre (for gunpowder), and opium (mostly for the China trade).
**Keywords:** EIC Exports, Bengal, Cotton, Saltpetre.
**Related Context:** Mercantilism 1757-1813.
**Memory Trick:** "S-O-S-C (Silk, Opium, Saltpetre, Cotton)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Including spices (which came mostly from Malabar/Java) or tea (which became a staple later in the 19th century).
**Why Important:** Economic basis of British interest in Bengal control.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-246
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2000
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I (Land System) with List II (Feature):
A. Jagirdari System - 1. Land allotted to big feudal landlords
B. Zamindari System - 2. Land allotted to revenue farmers
C. Ryotwari System - 3. Land allotted to each peasant with right to sell
D. Mahalwari System - 4. Revenue settlement made at village level
**Options:**
(a) A-1, B-2, C-3, D-4
(b) A-1, B-4, C-3, D-2
(c) A-3, B-2, C-1, D-4
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** 
- Jagirdari (A-1): Grant of land/revenue rights to officials for service.
- Zamindari (B-2): System of revenue farming (Permanent Settlement) where intermediaries paid state.
- Ryotwari (C-3): Direct settlement with the individual 'ryot' (peasant).
- Mahalwari (D-4): Settlement with the 'Mahal' or village community.
**Keywords:** Jagirdari, Zamindari, Ryotwari, Mahalwari.
**Related Personalities:** Cornwallis (Zamindari), Munro (Ryotwari), Holt Mackenzie (Mahalwari).
**Memory Trick:** "Ryot = Peasant (Direct); Mahal = Village (Community)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Zamindars were always the owners (they were initially revenue farmers turned proprietors by Cornwallis).
**Why Important:** Core agrarian history theme.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-247

(d) Lord Minto
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Lord Curzon (1899–1905) was extremely hostile to the Indian National Congress and expressed this desire to see it perish during his viceroyalty.
**Keywords:** Lord Curzon, INC demise, peaceful demise.
**Related Acts:** Partition of Bengal 1905.
**Memory Trick:** "Curzon wanted to Cancel (the) Congress."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Lord Dufferin, who called it a "microscopic minority" but didn't explicitly speak of assisting its "demise" in this famous quote.
**Why Important:** Shows the extreme reactionary phase of British administration before 1905.

**Question:** Who among the following were the founders of the “Hind Mazdoor Sabha” established in 1948?
**Options:**
(a) B. Krishna Pillai, E.M.S. Namboodiripad and K.C. George
(b) Jayaprakash Narayan, Deen Dayal Upadhyay and M.N. Roy
(c) C.P. Ramaswamy Iyer, K. Kamaraj and Veeresalingam Pantulu

**Question Category:** British Expansion in India

**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** In the Battle of Buxar (1764), the East India Company fought against the combined forces of:
**Options:**
(a) Mir Kasim, Shuja-ud-Daula and Shah Alam II
(b) Mir Jafar, Shuja-ud-Daula and Shah Alam II
(c) Mir Kasim, Tipu Sultan and Shah Alam II
(d) Mir Jafar, Tipu Sultan and Shuja-ud-Daula
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Battle of Buxar saw the British (Hector Munro) defeat the alliance of Mir Kasim (Bengal Nawab), Shuja-ud-Daula (Awadh Nawab), and Shah Alam II (Mughal Emperor).
**Keywords:** Battle of Buxar, 1764, Mir Kasim, Shah Alam II.
**Related Acts:** Treaty of Allahabad 1765.
**Memory Trick:** "K-S-S (Kasim, Shuja, Shah) at Buxar."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing the Nawab of Bengal (Mir Kasim) with his predecessor (Mir Jafar).
**Why Important:** This victory granted the EIC the Diwani rights (tax collection) over Bengal, Bihar, and Odisha.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-250
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I (Titles) with List II (Acts):
I. GG of Presidency of Fort William in Bengal (Regulating Act, 1773)
II. Governor General of India (Charter Act, 1833)
III. Governor General and Viceroy of India (Indian Councils Act, 1858)
IV. Governor General and Crown Representative (GOI Act, 1935)
List II (Personalities):
A. Lord Cornwallis
B. Lord Dalhousie
C. Lord Minto
D. Lord Wavell
**Options:**
(a) I-A, II-B, III-C, IV-D
(b) I-A, II-C, III-D, IV-B
(c) I-B, II-C, III-D, IV-A
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** 
- I matches Cornwallis (who held the title under the 1773 act era/later reforms). 
- II matches Dalhousie (GG of India era). 
- III matches Minto (Viceroy). 
- IV matches Wavell (1935 Act era GG/Crown Rep).
**Keywords:** Governor General, Viceroy, Crown Representative.
**Related Personalities:** Lord William Bentinck (1st GG India).
**Memory Trick:** "Bengal (1773) -> India (1833) -> Viceroy (1858) -> Representative (1935)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Not knowing that 'Crown Representative' was a specific title added in 1935 for relations with Princes.
**Why Important:** Tests constitutional terminology for the head of state.

**Question:** The meeting of Indian and British political leaders during 1930-32 in London has often been referred to as the First, Second and Third Round Table Conferences. It would be incorrect to refer to them as such because:

(a) the Indian National Congress did not take part in two of them
(b) Indian parties other than the Indian National Congress participating in the Conference represented sectional interests and not the whole of India
(c) British Labour Party had withdrawn from the Conference
(d) It was an instance of a conference held in three sessions and not that of three separate conferences

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-256
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The primary difference between the 'Moderates' and 'Extremists' in the early years of the INC was:
**Options:**
(a) goal of Swaraj
(b) methods of struggle
(c) loyalty to the British Crown
(d) social reform vs political reform
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** While both wanted self-government eventually, the Moderates used constitutional methods (Prayer, Petition, Protest), whereas Extremists advocated mass mobilization (Boycott, Swadeshi).
**Keywords:** Moderates, Extremists, Methods.
**Related Personalities:** Gokhale, Tilak.
**Memory Trick:** "Goal same, Path different."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking they had different goals early on (both initially accepted some form of self-rule within the empire).
**Why Important:** Core ideological rift of the 1905-1907 period.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-257
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The concept of 'Drain of Wealth' from India to England was first propounded by:
**Options:**
(a) Dadabhai Naoroji
(b) R. C. Dutt
(c) G. V. Joshi
(d) Gopal Krishna Gokhale
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Dadabhai Naoroji first proposed the theory in his paper "England's Debt to India" (1867) and later in his book "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India".
**Keywords:** Drain of Wealth, Naoroji.
**Related Books:** Poverty and Un-British Rule in India.
**Memory Trick:** "Grand Old Man Naoroji noticed the No-Return (Drain)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting R.C. Dutt (who supported the theory but didn't *first* propound it).
**Why Important:** Intellectual bedrock of Indian nationalism.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-258
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Swadeshi Movement
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The main reasoning given by the British for the Partition of Bengal (1905) was:
**Options:**
(a) to curb the growth of nationalism in Bengal
(b) to improve administrative efficiency
(c) to create a Muslim majority province
(d) to favor the people of East Bengal
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The *official* reason given by the British (Lord Curzon) was that Bengal was too large for a single governor to manage efficiently.
**Keywords:** Partition of Bengal, 1905, Administrative Efficiency.
**Related Personality:** Lord Curzon.
**Memory Trick:** "British said Efficiency, Indians felt Enmity."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (a), which was the *real* reason, but the question asks for the *official* reasoning given by the British.
**Why Important:** Tests awareness of colonial political rhetoric.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-259
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Lucknow Pact of 1916 was significant because it brought about a rapprochement between:
**Options:**
(a) the Congress and the Muslim League
(b) the Moderates and the Extremists
(c) both (a) and (b)
(d) the INC and the Home Rule League
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The 1916 Lucknow session achieved two unities: (1) The Moderates and Extremists reunited after the 1907 split, and (2) the Congress and Muslim League signed a pact for joint constitutional demands.
**Keywords:** Lucknow Pact, 1916, INC-League Unity.
**Related Personalities:** Tilak, Annie Besant, Jinnah.
**Memory Trick:** "Lucknow = Lucky Unity (Moderates/Extremists + Hindus/Muslims)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting only (a) and forgetting the internal Congress reunion.
**Why Important:** United Front for the post-WWI era.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-260

**Question Category:** Early Nationalism & INC
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Home Rule Movement in India was started by:
**Options:**
(a) B. G. Tilak and Annie Besant
(b) G. K. Gokhale and Tilak
(c) Annie Besant and Gokhale
(d) Lala Lajpat Rai and Tilak
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** B.G. Tilak started his league in April 1916 (Pune), and Annie Besant started hers in September 1916 (Madras).
**Keywords:** Home Rule League, 1916, Tilak, Besant.
**Related Dates:** 1916.
**Memory Trick:** "Home Rule = Tilak (April) + Besant (Sept)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Believing they merged (they remained separate for organizational reasons).
**Why Important:** Prelude to the mass Gandhian phase.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-262
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Mahatma Gandhi withdrew the Non-Cooperation Movement in 1922 because of:
**Options:**
(a) government repression
(b) lack of public response
(c) the Chauri-Chaura incident
(d) communal riots
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** In February 1922, a mob set fire to a police station in Chauri Chaura (UP), killing 22 policemen. Gandhi, adhering to strict non-violence, immediately suspended the movement.
**Keywords:** Non-Cooperation Movement, Chauri-Chaura, Withdrawal.
**Related Dates:** February 5, 1922.
**Memory Trick:** "Violence in Chauri = Vote of No (NCM)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the movement was failing (it was actually at its peak mass participation).
**Why Important:** Marked the end of the first great mass struggle.
**Sources:**

---

**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase

**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Swaraj Party was formed by:
**Options:**
(a) C. R. Das and Motilal Nehru
(b) Jawaharlal Nehru and C. R. Das
(c) Motilal Nehru and Rajendra Prasad
(d) Subhas Bose and C. R. Das
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Disillusioned with the withdrawal of NCM, C.R. Das (President) and Motilal Nehru (Secretary) formed the Congress-Khilafat Swarajya Party in 1923 to contest elections.
**Keywords:** Swaraj Party, 1923, Motilal Nehru, C.R. Das.
**Related Context:** Council Entry.
**Memory Trick:** "Das and Nehru wanted to Do (councils)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Jawaharlal Nehru (he was a 'no-changer' supporter initially).
**Why Important:** Represented the parliamentary strategy within the movement.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-264
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1995
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Simon Commission was boycotted by Indians mainly because:
**Options:**
(a) it was appointed before the scheduled date
(b) it recommended partition
(c) there was no Indian member in it
(d) it was presided over by a British official
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The commission was composed of seven British MPs and no Indians, which was seen as a grave insult to the principle of self-determination.
**Keywords:** Simon Commission, Boycott, All-White.
**Related Personalities:** John Simon.
**Memory Trick:** "Simon: See (no) Indians."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the boycott was because of its *proposals* (it happened when they landed, before reports were out).
**Why Important:** United almost all Indian factions in a common protest.
**Sources:**

**Options:**
(a) Subhas Chandra Bose
(b) Mohan Singh
(c) Rash Behari Bose
(d) Shah Nawaz Khan

**Memory Trick:** "Mohan Made it, Subhas led it."

**Why Important:** Distinguishes between founding and command.

**Options:**
(a) Two Sections
(b) Three Sections
(c) Four Sections
(d) Five Sections
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Provinces were grouped into Sections A (Hindu majority), B (North-West Muslim majority), and C (East Muslim majority).

**Related Acts:** Cabinet Mission Plan.

**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it was just two groups (Hindu and Muslim).
**Why Important:** The failure of this grouping logic made Partition inevitable.

**Options:**
(a) Mahatma Gandhi

(c) Lord Wavell
(d) Vallabhbhai Patel
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** While the League initially boycotted the govt, Lord Wavell persuaded Jinnah to join in October 1946 to ensure a balanced administration and prevent total Congress dominance.

**Memory Trick:** "Wavell Welcomed the League."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Nehru (who was the political rival and didn't initially invite them personally).

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-274
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2003
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Assertion (A): In 1916, Maulana Mohammad Ali and Abul Kalam Azad resigned from the Legislative Council. 
Reason (R): The Rowlatt Act was passed in spite of unanimous opposition from the Indian members.
**Options:**
(a) Both A and R are individually true and R is the correct explanation of A
(b) Both A and R are individually true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A
(c) A is true but R is false
(d) A is false but R is true
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** Assertion (A) is false; while many resigned over Rowlatt in 1919 (e.g., Jinnah, Malaviya, Mazharul Haque), the date 1916 is incorrect. Reason (R) is true; the Rowlatt Act (1919) was indeed forced through despite unanimous Indian member opposition.
**Keywords:** Rowlatt Act, Resignation, Indian Members.
**Related Personalities:** Muhammad Ali Jinnah (resigned).
**Memory Trick:** "Rowlatt was 19, not 16."
**Common Exam Trap:** Assuming all leaders resigned simultaneously at the earliest date.
**Why Important:** Demonstrates the lack of legislative power Indians had under the "reform" acts.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-275
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2002
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The "Filtration Theory" in the history of Indian education aimed to:
**Options:**
(a) educate the masses directly through vernacular schools
(b) educate a small section of the upper class who would then educate the masses
(c) provide technical education to the middle class for industrialization
(d) filter out non-British elements from the educational curriculum
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Lord Macaulay's policy (1835) believed that due to limited resources, education should "filter down" from the top. By educating the elite in English, they would become "British in taste and intellect" and eventually pass knowledge to the masses.
**Keywords:** Downward Filtration Theory, Macaulay, English Education.
**Related Personality:** Lord Macaulay.
**Memory Trick:** "Filter from Elite to Everyone."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it was about religious filtering.
**Why Important:** Defined the class-based nature of colonial education for decades.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-276
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Regarding Wood’s Dispatch, which of the following statements are true?
1. Grants-in-aid system was introduced.
2. Establishment of universities was recommended.
3. English as a medium of instruction at all levels of education was recommended.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** Wood's Despatch (1854) introduced the grants-in-aid system to encourage private enterprise in education. It recommended the establishment of universities in Calcutta, Bombay, and Madras on the model of London University. However, it recommended English as the medium of instruction only for higher studies, while suggesting vernacular languages for school-level education, making statement 3 incorrect.
**Keywords:** Wood's Dispatch, Grants-in-aid, Universities.
**Related Personalities:** Charles Wood, Lord Dalhousie.
**Memory Trick:** "Wood's model: Money (grants) + London (universities)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking English was recommended for *all* levels (it was only for higher education).
**Why Important:** Known as the "Magna Carta of English Education in India".
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-277
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Economically, one of the results of the British rule in India in the 19th century was the:
**Options:**
(a) increase in the export of Indian handicrafts
(b) growth in the number of Indian owned factories
(c) commercialization of Indian agriculture
(d) rapid increase in the urban population
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** British rule led to the commercialization of Indian agriculture, where crops were grown for sale in the market rather than for self-consumption. This was driven by the need for raw materials like cotton, jute, and indigo for British industries. Handicrafts were ruined (a), and industrial growth was suppressed (b).
**Keywords:** Commercialization, 19th Century, British Economy.
**Related Concepts:** De-industrialization, Plantation crops.
**Memory Trick:** "Cash crops for Colonial coffers."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (d); actually, ruralization occurred due to the ruin of traditional urban craft centers.
**Why Important:** Highlights the structural shift in the Indian agrarian economy.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-278
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the period of colonial rule in India, "Home Charges" formed an important part of drain of wealth from India. Which of the following funds constituted Home Charges?
1. Funds used to support the India Office in London.
2. Funds used to pay salaries and pensions of British personnel engaged in India.
3. Funds used for waging wars outside India by the British.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Home Charges were expenditures incurred in England by the Secretary of State on behalf of India. These included the maintenance of the India Office (1) and salaries/pensions of British officers (2). Statement 3 is often excluded from the technical definition of "Home Charges" in official UPSC keys, as war costs were generally categorized as military debt/direct drain rather than administrative overhead.
**Keywords:** Home Charges, Drain of Wealth, India Office.
**Related Personalities:** Dadabhai Naoroji.
**Memory Trick:** "Home Charges = Paying for the Boss's London Home."
**Common Exam Trap:** Including all colonial expenses as "Home Charges".
**Why Important:** Core pillar of the economic critique of the Raj.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-279
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The tendency for increased litigation in India after the introduction of the land settlement system by Lord Cornwallis is usually ascribed to which of the following provisions?
**Options:**
(a) Making Zamindar's position stronger vis-a-vis the ryot
(b) Making East India Company an overlord of Zamindars
(c) Making judicial system more efficient
(d) None of the (a), (b) and (c) above
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** The surge in litigation after the Permanent Settlement (1793) was primarily due to the abolition of the Court Fee and the separation of executive and judicial functions, which made the legal system more accessible but also overwhelmed. However, the most critical factor was the removal of the Collector's judicial powers and the rigid "Sunset Law," which led to frequent land transfers and disputes that weren't adequately addressed by the options provided.
**Keywords:** Litigation, Cornwallis, Land Settlement.
**Related Acts:** Cornwallis Code 1793.
**Memory Trick:** "Cornwallis made the law clear but the land contested."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (c) assuming efficiency was the goal, whereas it was accessibility and procedural change that led to the backlog.
**Why Important:** Shows the social unintended consequences of administrative reforms.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-280
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Constitutional Developments & British Plans
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the period of Indian freedom struggle, which of the following was/were recommended by the ‘Nehru Report’ (1928)?
1. Complete Independence for India.
2. Joint electorates for reservation of seats for minorities.
3. Provision of Fundamental Rights for the people of India in the Constitution.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Nehru Report (1928) demanded Dominion Status, not Complete Independence (making statement 1 incorrect). It recommended joint electorates with reserved seats for Muslims where they were in a minority (2) and a list of 19 fundamental rights (3).
**Keywords:** Nehru Report, Dominion Status, Fundamental Rights.
**Related Personalities:** Motilal Nehru.
**Memory Trick:** "Nehru Report = Rights but No (Complete) Independence."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking it asked for Purna Swaraj (that was the 1929 Lahore session).
**Why Important:** First comprehensive Indian-led constitutional draft.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-281
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2015
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who among the following was/were economic critic/critics of colonialism in India?
1. Dadabhai Naoroji
2. G. Subramania Iyer
3. R.C. Dutt
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** All three were major critics. Naoroji propounded the 'Drain Theory'. G. Subramania Iyer (founder of *The Hindu*) criticized economic policies. R.C. Dutt wrote the seminal 'Economic History of India'.
**Keywords:** Economic Critics, Drain of Wealth.
**Related Personalities:** M.G. Ranade.
**Memory Trick:** "N-I-D (Naoroji, Iyer, Dutt) noticed the Drain."
**Common Exam Trap:** Limiting economic criticism to only Naoroji.
**Why Important:** This intellectual work fueled the nationalist movement.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-282
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Ilbert Bill controversy was a landmark in the history of the Indian National Movement because it related to the:
**Options:**
(a) imposition of certain restrictions on the Indians carrying arms.
(b) imposition of restrictions on Indian language newspapers and magazines.
(c) removal of racial disqualifications with the regard to the judicial education.
(d) None of the above.
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Ilbert Bill (1883) sought to allow Indian judges to try Europeans in criminal cases, thereby removing racial discrimination in the judiciary. The fierce opposition by the British ("White Mutiny") made Indians realize the depth of racial bias and the need for organized political struggle.
**Keywords:** Ilbert Bill, Lord Ripon, Racial discrimination.
**Related Context:** Pre-INC associations.
**Memory Trick:** "Ilbert = Impartial (Judiciary)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with the Vernacular Press Act (statement b).
**Why Important:** Catalyst for the formation of the INC in 1885.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-283
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** The Revolt of 1857
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the Revolt of 1857, which of the following pairs is/are correctly matched?
Leader — Centre of Revolt
1. Delhi — Bakht Khan
2. Kanpur — Nana Sahib
3. Lucknow — Begum Hazrat Mahal
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (d)
**Detailed Explanation:** All are correctly matched. General Bakht Khan led the troops in Delhi. Nana Sahib led the uprising in Kanpur with Tantia Tope. Begum Hazrat Mahal led the resistance in Lucknow against the British.
**Keywords:** 1857 Leaders, Bakht Khan, Nana Sahib.
**Related Personalities:** Rani Laxmibai, Kunwar Singh.
**Memory Trick:** "B-D (Bakht-Delhi), N-K (Nana-Kanpur), H-L (Hazrat-Lucknow)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Bahadur Shah II was the military leader (it was Bakht Khan).
**Why Important:** Fundamental factual matching for 1857.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-284
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** What was the reason for Mahatma Gandhi to organize a Satyagraha on behalf of the peasants of Kheda?
1. The Administration did not suspend the land revenue collection in spite of a bad harvest.
2. The Administration proposed to introduce Permanent Settlement in Gujarat.
Select the correct answer using the code given below:
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Kheda Satyagraha (1918) was triggered by the government's refusal to grant revenue remission despite a crop failure. Statement 2 is false; the Permanent Settlement was for Bengal/Bihar, while Gujarat was under a different system.
**Keywords:** Kheda Satyagraha, Revenue remission.
**Related Personalities:** Vallabhbhai Patel.
**Memory Trick:** "Kheda = Khali (Empty) harvest."
**Common Exam Trap:** Assuming Permanent Settlement applied everywhere in India.
**Why Important:** Established Gandhi as a leader for agrarian causes.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-285
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase

**Year:** 2012
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** With reference to the period of Indian freedom struggle, consider the following statements:
1. The Civil Disobedience Movement in Peshawar was led by Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan.
2. In Sholapur, industrial workers led a violent movement against British rule during the Civil Disobedience phase.
**Options:**
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) Both 1 and 2
(d) Neither 1 nor 2
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Both are correct. Ghaffar Khan (Frontier Gandhi) led the 'Red Shirts' in Peshawar. In Sholapur, the news of Gandhi's arrest led to a fierce uprising by textile workers who established a parallel government for a few days.
**Keywords:** Peshawar, Sholapur, Civil Disobedience.
**Related Personalities:** Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan.
**Memory Trick:** "Ghaffar in the West (Peshawar), Workers in Sholapur."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking CDM was entirely non-violent (Sholapur saw significant violence).
**Why Important:** Highlights the regional diversity of CDM.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-287
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** Gandhian Phase
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2011
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Mahatma Gandhi said that some of his deepest convictions were reflected in a book titled, ‘Unto this Last’, and the book transformed his life. What was the message from the book that transformed Mahatma Gandhi?
**Options:**
(a) Uplifting the oppressed and poor is the moral duty of an educated man.
(b) The good of the individual is contained in the good of all.
(c) The life of celibacy and spiritual pursuit are essential for a noble life.
(d) All the statements (a), (b) and (c) are correct in this context.
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** John Ruskin's *Unto this Last* taught Gandhi that the good of the individual is contained in the good of all (Sarvodaya). He later adapted this into his philosophy of social welfare.
**Keywords:** Unto this Last, Sarvodaya, John Ruskin.
**Related Concepts:** Phoenix Settlement.
**Memory Trick:** "Ruskin's Result = Sarvodaya (All)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting (d) because they all sound 'Gandhian', but statement (b) is the *specific* message he emphasized from Ruskin.
**Why Important:** Foundational text for Gandhian social philosophy.
**Sources:**

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-288
**Difficulty:** Moderate
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which one of the following statements does **not** apply to the system of Subsidiary Alliance introduced by Lord Wellesley?
**Options:**
(a) To maintain a large standing army at other's expense
(b) To keep India safe from Napoleonic danger
(c) To secure a fixed income for the Company
(d) To establish British paramountcy over the Indian States
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The Subsidiary Alliance aimed to protect the Company from French threats (b), maintain a standing army funded by Indian states (a), and establish British supremacy (d). It did not aim to secure a "fixed income"; rather, it was a political-military arrangement for control.
**Keywords:** Subsidiary Alliance, Lord Wellesley.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Wellesley.
**Memory Trick:** "Wellesley wanted Soldiers, not Salaries (fixed income)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking the Company wanted direct profit from the alliance (it was for strategic dominance).
**Why Important:** Most important tool for British expansion without annexation.
**Sources:**

---

**Keywords:** Chapchar Kut, Khongjom Parva, Thang-ta.
**Related Context:** Northeast India culture.
**Memory Trick:** "Thang-ta is Manipuri (M-M)."

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-291

**Year:** 2018
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Consider the following statements:
1. In the first Lok Sabha, the single largest party in the opposition was the Swatantra Party.
2. In the Lok Sabha, a “Leader of the Opposition” was recognised for the first time in 1969.
3. In the Lok Sabha, if a party does not have a minimum of 75 members, its leader cannot be recognised as the Leader of the Opposition.
Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
**Options:**
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Statement 1 is false; CPI was the largest opposition in the first Lok Sabha (Swatantra Party formed in 1959). Statement 2 is true; the first official LoP was recognized in 1969. Statement 3 is false; the requirement is 10% of total strength (approx 55 members).
**Keywords:** First Lok Sabha, Leader of Opposition.
**Related Personalities:** Ram Subhag Singh.
**Memory Trick:** "LoP = 1/10th of the House."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing first opposition party with later prominent ones.

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-293

**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 2020
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Indigo cultivation in India declined by the beginning of the 20th century because of:
**Options:**
(a) peasant resistance to the oppressive conduct of planters
(b) its unprofitability in the world market because of new inventions
(c) national leaders' opposition to the cultivation of indigo
(d) Government control over the planters
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** The invention of synthetic dyes in Germany at the end of the 19th century made natural indigo uncompetitive and unprofitable. This led to the decline of the industry in India.
**Keywords:** Indigo, Synthetic dyes, Germany.
**Related Context:** Champaran Satyagraha.
**Memory Trick:** "Synthetic killed Natural Blue."
**Common Exam Trap:** Attributing decline solely to peasant revolts (which happened, but the economic *decline* was driven by global market changes).
**Why Important:** Background to the agrarian crisis in Champaran.

(a) Both A and R are individually true and R is the correct explanation of A
(b) Both A and R are individually true but R is not a correct explanation of A

(d) A is false but R is true

(a) Indian Council Act, 1861
(b) Government of India Act, 1858
(c) Indian Councils Act, 1892
(d) Indian Councils Act, 1909

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-PYQ-308
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Question Category:** Transfer of Power & Partition
**Exam Name:** UPSC CSE Prelims
**Year:** 1996
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Match List I (Titles) with List II (Personalities):
I. GG of Presidency of Fort William (1773 Act)
II. Governor General of India (1833 Act)
III. Governor General and Viceroy (1858 Act)
IV. Governor General and Crown Representative (1935 Act)
List II: A. Wavell, B. Dalhousie, C. Cornwallis, D. Minto
**Options:**
(a) I-C, II-B, III-D, IV-A
(b) I-C, II-D, III-A, IV-E
(c) I-B, II-C, III-D, IV-E
(d) I-D, II-B, III-C, IV-A
**Answer:** (a)
**Detailed Explanation:** I-C: Cornwallis (early phase). II-B: Dalhousie (GG India phase). III-D: Minto (Viceroy phase). IV-A: Wavell (1935 Act era/Crown Rep).
**Keywords:** Governor General, Viceroy, Crown Representative.
**Related Acts:** 1773, 1833, 1858, 1935.
**Memory Trick:** "Bengal (1773) -> India (1833) -> Viceroy (1858) -> Representative (1935)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Not knowing 'Crown Representative' was a specific 1935 title.
**Why Important:** Core evolution of the Head of State titles.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-AI-309
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** AI Predicted Question
**Year:** 2026
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who was the French minister instrumental in founding the French East India Company (Compagnie des Indes Orientales) in 1664?
**Options:**
(a) Mazarin
(b) Richelieu
(c) Colbert
(d) Dupleix
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Jean-Baptiste Colbert, the minister of Finance under King Louis XIV, founded the French East India Company in 1664 to compete with the Dutch and English.
**Keywords:** Colbert, 1664, French East India Company.
**Related Personalities:** Louis XIV.
**Memory Trick:** "Colbert Created the Company."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Dupleix (who was a later governor, not the founder).
**Why Important:** Last major European power to enter India.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-AI-310
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Advent of Europeans & British Expansion
**Exam Name:** AI Predicted Question
**Year:** 2026
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Battle of Bedara (1759) resulted in the final defeat and expulsion of which European power from major Indian influence?
**Options:**
(a) The Portuguese
(b) The Danes
(c) The Dutch
(d) The French
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The British defeated the Dutch in the Battle of Bedara (1759), effectively ending Dutch ambitions in India and forcing them to concentrate on the Indonesian archipelago.
**Keywords:** Bedara, 1759, Dutch.
**Related Battles:** Plassey, Wandiwash.
**Memory Trick:** "Bedara broke the Dutch."
**Common Exam Trap:** Confusing it with Wandiwash (French).
**Why Important:** Cleared a major rival for the British.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-AI-311
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** AI Predicted Question
**Year:** 2026
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Which treaty granted the English East India Company the 'Diwani' rights over Bengal, Bihar, and Odisha?
**Options:**
(a) Treaty of Alinagar
(b) Treaty of Allahabad
(c) Treaty of Paris
(d) Treaty of Salbai
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Following the victory in the Battle of Buxar (1764), the Treaty of Allahabad (1765) was signed between Robert Clive and Mughal Emperor Shah Alam II, granting the EIC the right to collect revenue (Diwani).
**Keywords:** Treaty of Allahabad, 1765, Diwani rights.
**Related Personalities:** Robert Clive, Shah Alam II.
**Memory Trick:** "Allahabad = All the cash (Diwani)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Diwani was granted after Plassey (it was after Buxar).
**Why Important:** Formalized the EIC's status as a territorial ruler.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-AI-312
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** AI Predicted Question
**Year:** 2026
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who was the Governor-General of India during the introduction of the Permanent Settlement in Bengal in 1793?
**Options:**
(a) Warren Hastings
(b) Lord Wellesley
(c) Lord Cornwallis
(d) Lord Dalhousie
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Lord Cornwallis introduced the Permanent Settlement (Zamindari System) in Bengal and Bihar in 1793 to fix land revenue permanently.
**Keywords:** Permanent Settlement, Cornwallis, 1793.
**Related Personalities:** John Shore.
**Memory Trick:** "Cornwallis fixed the Corn (Revenue)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting Warren Hastings (who introduced the 'Izaredari' or auction system).
**Why Important:** Landmark agrarian policy that defined Bengal's socio-economic structure.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-AI-313
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Acts and Policies
**Exam Name:** AI Predicted Question
**Year:** 2026
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** The Vernacular Press Act of 1878, aimed at suppressing non-English newspapers, was enacted under which Viceroy?
**Options:**
(a) Lord Mayo
(b) Lord Northbrook
(c) Lord Lytton
(d) Lord Ripon
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** Lord Lytton passed the "Gagging Act" (Vernacular Press Act) in 1878 to suppress criticism of government policies in regional languages. It was later repealed by Lord Ripon in 1882.
**Keywords:** Vernacular Press Act, Lord Lytton.
**Related Dates:** 1878.
**Memory Trick:** "Lytton = Lock (the press); Ripon = Release (the press)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Thinking Ripon *passed* it (he *repealed* it).
**Why Important:** Major point of contention that fueled early nationalism.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-AI-314
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** Socio-Religious Movements
**Exam Name:** AI Predicted Question
**Year:** 2026
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Who founded the 'Atmiya Sabha' in Calcutta in 1815?
**Options:**
(a) Debendranath Tagore
(b) Raja Ram Mohan Roy
(c) Keshab Chandra Sen
(d) Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar
**Answer:** (b)
**Detailed Explanation:** Raja Ram Mohan Roy founded the Atmiya Sabha (Society of Friends) in 1815 to conduct religious discussions and promote monotheism.
**Keywords:** Atmiya Sabha, Ram Mohan Roy, 1815.
**Related Context:** Brahmo Samaj (1828).
**Memory Trick:** "Atmiya (Friends) of Ram."
**Common Exam Trap:** Swapping Atmiya Sabha with Brahmo Samaj.
**Why Important:** Precursor to the broader socio-religious reform movement.
**Sources:**

---

**Master ID:** UPSC-MH-AI-315
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Question Category:** British Administration & Economic Policies
**Exam Name:** AI Predicted Question
**Year:** 2026
**Stage:** Preliminary
**Question:** Under which Viceroy was the first (non-synchronous) census of India conducted in 1872?
**Options:**
(a) Lord Canning
(b) Lord Lawrence
(c) Lord Mayo
(d) Lord Lytton
**Answer:** (c)
**Detailed Explanation:** The first attempt at a census in India was made in 1872 during the viceroyalty of Lord Mayo. The first complete synchronous census occurred in 1881 under Lord Ripon.
**Keywords:** Census, 1872, Lord Mayo.
**Related Personalities:** Lord Ripon.
**Memory Trick:** "Mayo's Measurement (Census)."
**Common Exam Trap:** Selecting 1881 as the *first* census (1881 was the first *complete synchronous* one).
**Why Important:** Beginning of systematic demographic data collection.
**Sources:**
